O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	O ye, dear sons, I have completed this book which is behind the knowledge of medicine assembled in its completion, and have made the end for his explanations and by his declarations.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it came to me in a vision that I will complete this book for you, which is part of the work of hands, namely "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the work of hands is forced in our region and is strange everywhere throughout all things, so has perished the knowledge and was forgotten, and remains only from the fires that were burned only the small descriptions in books of the ancients who had used their hands.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And from this is come the errors and the foolishness, and are closed the intentions and are delayed the knowledge.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	It seems to me that I can revive this text according to the order of this treatment following the way of exposition and declaration and abbreviation; and came together with the forms of cautery instruments and other tools of the work with the adjustment of declaration and preparation of it, such as it is necessary.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And because no good masters of hands are found in our times, the art of medicine is stretched out.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And it is fitting for him who enters this that he will have to delve into the science of anatomy, as Galen says, until he knows the joint of the members, and their forms and conjunctions and separations, and has knowledge of bones and nerves and joints and the number of bones, and the movement and rest of the veins, and of their origin.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc; et meismement en l’art de main.	And therefore Hippocrates says that the nose is very sensitive, and the ear is less so; and it is the same in the art of skill.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes; ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	And therefore, in the introduction of this book, I want to say that he who is not well acquainted with these things should beware lest he fall into error and hurt people; thus I have often seen more of those who intervene in this science and abandon their knowledge and experience.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa I apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col; por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	For I have seen a mad doctor who cut the abscess of a woman with scrofula or a lump on her neck, and cut at the arteries in the neck; because so much blood came out that the woman died between his hands.
Et vis I autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans; si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens III jors.	And I have also seen another doctor who treated a large stone from an old man, and the stone was so big that he removed a piece of his bladder with it; and died three days later in his own home.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I have heard that it is called cauterization, and I saw the condition of the patient and the size of the wound, and I know well that if you cut like this, he will die.
Et vis I autre mire qui prist en cure I duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie; et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi I termine; et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie; et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	And I saw another physician who treated a duke of our land, who had a broken leg and an open wound; and the foolish physician stretched the break on the wound with force, binding it tightly, without letting it heal, and thus he finished his cure, and the patient commanded that he should not release him again; and so he stayed like this until the leg was completely frozen, and the feet and came to perdition.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe; et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	I was called to come to him, and I hastened to come to release the leg; and when I heard it was dislocated, it was in peace and he did not feel any pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner; et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	But all corruption was already confirmed in the member, and it cannot be cured; and the corruption does not cease to spread through the member until the member is completely lost.
Et vis I autre mire qui effondra I apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And there is another evil that crushes and inflames the abscess, then sets it on fire by the malice of its power.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	Because a chancre, when it is pure of melancholic humors, does not require that one touches it with iron unless there is a need to remove the corrupted part.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en II divisions: c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions; et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	And dear son, it is necessary for you to know that surgical work is divided into two divisions: first, knowing whether there is a risk in many situations; and I will show you in each book of this work where there is fear and risk.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez; et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit; et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez,
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	Don't try to treat evil sickness, lest you are called a fool's physician.
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	I have devised this treatment according to the three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez; et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	The first chapters are about fire cauteries and cold medicine treatments, and they order the head up to the feet; and the shapes of the ointments, and the tools for cautery, and all that is necessary in the work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses; et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	The second chapters are about cutting and piercing, and ventouses, wounds, and the extraction of arrows, and similar things; and the chapters order these and the shapes of the ointments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses; et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	The third chapters are about restoring dislocations and twists, and similar things; and it orders the head up to the feet, and the shapes of the ointments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	So that we remember the work, it is necessary to tell the quality of aid and the danger of each kind.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus; et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu; et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	I say that the quality of aid and the danger is the longest word and subtle science and the secret responses; and those who are wise men speak about this, and agree with it; and they give little attention to my words, because I am too long-winded.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que II complexions: c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	I say that cautery provides relief universally for all kinds of flesh or matter, whether it is one type of flesh: I mean the hot flesh with matter, and the dry flesh with matter.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	In hot and dry flesh together with matter, some considered that cautery was great aid, and the others said the opposite: that cautery is of no use for sicknesses that come from heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour; et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	For the nature of fire is hot, and should not be treated with hot disease by heat, or drying; but tell those who say the cautery does great harm to hot and dry diseases that it brings great relief to diseases of the body in men.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you buy the body of an ox and its moisture is in harmony with the nature of fire, you find that the body is frozen.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this word.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have found it to be true by experience.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens; des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	And no way should be entered into fire except for one who has proved it by experience, and who knows from long use the cautery of cutting, and the variety of human complexities, and the dispositions and causes of their diseases, and remedies, and space of time; while for other complexions we have no great fear, nor ourselves in cold and moist diseases.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all the physicians will assemble and agree on the cautery.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know, sons, that cautery is gathering fire from the secrets of remedies, and is more beneficial than cautery with burning medicine.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	Because fire is simple, and comes only from the member that is burned, and does not harm other members if not called upon.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation; et par aventure ocit lou malaide Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	The burning medicines come from one member to another through displacement, and bring disease of grief or of recovery; and by chance the fire kills the sick person because of their high heat and because of the kindness of its nature does not do that, if it has excess.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses; et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant; or le recevez en vos pensees.	And this is what I have found by experiment and through long service and study, which I have put into the art, and has been known from a long time ago; and therefore I excuse myself for the length of my words, because it does not please me to show you the secret that is answered with fire, and the quality of the work, how it cures diseases of the body, as the philosopher said, demonstrating it; so receive it in your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, my son, that they will agree on when these cauteries are to be made, and have chosen the prayers.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere; et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	And I say that cautery is suitable in all times, because the evils that remain underneath are removed by the aid of cautery; and even though the cauteries cause painful necessities that cannot be put off until greater evil comes to the member.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire; car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue; et il le dient ensi; mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	And never think that it is the same thing, my dear son, as how they speak; for the disease which is healed by cautery has no return; and he says thus; but it's not so, because cautery is not just a medicine that cures, but one that changes the complexion, and dries out the humors that are causing pain, and it heals more than other medicines due to its haste of action, and for the virtue of its work and its authority.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.	In case some disease occurs without ever matching the patient's complexion and the nature of the disease, and all excesses are assembled in them through the acquisition of meat and similar things, so if they do not administer cautery to him when he has little excess and moisture, just as cauterization for pain and similar things works, but this happens rarely; yet it often occurs.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir; mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	And many people do not understand why cauterization is called the art of medicine, and it's seeing; but they don't believe that cauterization has value after medicine, their opinions are false, and cauterization is considered the art of medicine because when we administer various types of cures in any disease and they don't work, then we administer cauterization and it works.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Then open well what cauterizes is from the medicine, not according to the foolish views of the mad.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	The ancients said that cauterizing with an instrument of gold is more precious than iron, and they did not say that fire was used only for the quality of the gold and its highness; and they said that the cauterizing instruments do not rot, but this is not true because I have tried it, and I have found that it is true in some people; and cauterizing with gold is more precious than iron, as they said.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez; et s’on le chaufe trop; si font au feu; et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	And if you cauterize an instrument of gold, you do not know well when it is caused by the color of the gold, and when it cools down quickly; and if one heats it too much, they make it in the fire; and thus there is enough hindrance.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And for this reason we use fire cautery, which we have tried before in our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	Or we have ordered this chapter to be written on the head since it is easier to find.
dou cautere olivaire	How to perform olive oil cautery.
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	This cautery is worth the moisture and coldness on the head, and for one disease called "soda", which occurs because of an imbalance of humors that discharge from the brain to the eyes, ears, and head, as well as numerous dreams, pain in the teeth, pain in the throat, and similar diseases, just like paralysis, soda, apoplexy, and other similar diseases.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief III nuis ou IIII, selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	The form of this cautery is that the patient should be purged by medicine to dissolve and clean out the brain, if it is obstructed with pus or four humors, according to what the virtues, juice, and custom of the patient can tolerate; and then apply the cauterized head to the patient.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses II eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	And then the finger shall be placed between your hands, and held by one hand on his palm; after putting the root of your palm upon the root of his nail between his two fingers; and when it comes to your middle, if it bleeds at that place, take the cautery called "olivare" for this purpose.
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant; puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os I sol petit; et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit; aprés pren I poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse III jors; aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre; et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then put a small signet ring of ink on the skin, and make downward cuts and extractions with your hand little by little in turning; then lift your hand gently, and treat the wound so that you see a bone exposed small; if you do not see it, repeatedly apply the cautery until you see the bone as I have told you; after take some wool, and put it on with oil and soft cotton inside, and place it on the skin, and let it stay for three days; after cover it with a moist linen cloth in butter; and leave it so that the bleeding is stopped; after cure the wound of the ligament called "tetrafarmaçon", until it is healed.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge; et por ce si aide mues.	And if the ancient ones said, when a wound stays open for longer, it is more purged. And therefore one should aid muscles.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And none of these said that one must so cool the cautery that part of the bone is burned, and then reset what has been burned with the bone, and cure it.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme I vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors; et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte; aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	And they said the other, one must cool the cautery so much that you put it as far down as a bone as big as a green thorn, which women use to make their breasts tight, for this reason the humors come out in motion; and then one cools the wound long. After, one must cure and sew it.
Et ces II manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor; et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier; car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres; et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	And these two ways of cauterization do not seem to me to be good in all respects, fires that give some men a sight of fear; and it seems to me I should leave them, for the joints are weakened by the continuous solutions of nature, as we have shown in other members; and myself when the joints of the patient are weak by nature, and the first appearance of cauterization is more healing and moistening for me, that's why I use over it in some cases, therefore this seems a cure.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	of the ancient head pain
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres; et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	When in the head there is chronic pain that lasts for a long time, and to alleviate it, the patient must use the powder and pills called "coccie", and purgatives of the head, oils, and plasters; and if you apply the cautery we have mentioned before, and it has no effect.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit; adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	Take care that if the patient's joints are of strong nature, and not too cold; then apply the cautery under that same cautery as we have mentioned above.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai I cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»; et est I leus en coi on met ventouses; et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os: li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors; et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	After applying the cautery to both corners of the head where the bone is, just as we have said, and doing the cautery that is called "vasselz", which is used with forceps; and take care not to see with your hand where the bone is: the patient feels a greater pain in this cautery than in others, and I will speak of it later; and it is necessary that the corns be applied more subtly than those for cauterizing the middle part of the head, and this is the form:
dou cautere dou chief	the fire cautery of the head
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie: adonques li fai cauteres selonc II manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	When there is sudden pain in one part of the head, and the disease has spread up to the bone, and the joints are purged with medicines, and other treatments have been tried, as I mentioned in the division of diseases, but they do not help: then he should perform cautery according to two methods, namely with cold medicine and fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope I poc as II chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir; et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi XII houres; et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi II jors ou III; puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	The cautery with cold medicine is that you take an ounce of alum, and remove the scab and the covering skin over the two joints, and then make a poultice on the temple in such a way that you can put the alum under the skin; and when it has been placed so that the lie (a type of plaster) holds well, he tightens and restrains it well and leaves it like this for 12 hours; and then removes it and treats with hot alum again, leaving the wound like two or three days; then puts on a cotton poultice in lard until it is cured.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	After the treatment of ointment until it is healthy; and if you see, then do what I wrote about certain burning medicines that I have written or dosed to treat burning medicines.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	The iron cauterization is done in this manner.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Heat the cauterization so that it has this form:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait I poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance; et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse; et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	And it is called "clos" because the chief is shaped like a close or has a little bit of wood, and in the middle it has a small appearance; and place it on the painful area, hold your hand tight and turn the iron gently, until the moist part of the spice is burned; and lift your hand so that the artery does not burn, which is before, and discharge abundance of blood.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par III jors; puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	After metting cotton on the wound of the vein, and puts sor on the leg for III days; then he puts cotton soaked in butter, and then heals the leg with ointment until it is sound; and if you want to cauterize this emigraine with the cautery which is called "cultellare", at all the point, and keep off the artery in this emigraine which is not ancient.
de emigraine	of the headache
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans; et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez; et laisse l’uevre em mi voie; mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	When you cure headache as we have said before in the division of diseases, and it does not profit, and you see that those who use cautery before say of medicine and iron do not suffer, then it is necessary to heat the cautery which is called "cultellare" until it is white; and so apply a hot bandage on the leg with half a double strand of linen, and hold your hand once, and strain so that you do not cover the artery and that it does not come near the bone; and beware of the jaw that swells when one eats, and the nerves will have no sight but the numbness and the spasm will come to the sick, and beware of the corruption of blood from the artery when it is cut, or cutting has great fear and itself to that which does not fit, and who is not examined and tried; and leave the open wound in my way; but I will tell you how one preserves health when the artery is cut, and I will show you to him in this book.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait II coutelz; et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	If the fire cautery does not ease the illness and the patient suffers, cauterize the wound in the same way as we have said, and treat the wound until it is healed; and if you see, administer the cauterization that we have said or chapter on the extraction of an artery, with the cauterization which has two stitches; and this cautery is better than that one and more helpful.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	from the pain of the ears due to coldness.
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When the pain in the ear comes from coldness and we have applied medicinal solutes and other treatments that we have said on division, and the pains do not cease, then apply this cauterization which is called "pins", for it has the form:
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les II se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche; et ait X poins entor chescune oreille; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After poking all around the diseased ear, or on both ears where pain holds firm, and then pushing a little towards the root of the ear after marking the level with an awl; and applying X points around each ear; after treatment, make it healthy.
de la torture de la bouche	of the torment of the mouth
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie; et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	Torment that must be cured by cautery is only of those that are caused by pus, just as we have said in our divisions of the disease; and do not perform any cautery on superficial symptoms which come from ulcers and phlegm.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de III cauteres: l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des II levres; et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce; et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	When you treat this superficial torment that is caused by pus and dries and purging of the head and gargrene, and it is not worth anything, then it is necessary to cauterize the patient with three cauteries: one in the root of the ear, and another near the temple, and the third between the two lips; and insert the cauterium into the healthy part that opens up, and do the cauterization directly on top of the ear above a little below the nail of the head, and another one as long as the space of a finger in the temple; and leave the cauterium there until the blood cools. And this is the form of the cautery:
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros; aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And this is the resemblance of the sawing cut that we have shown before, but it is a bit more subtle and should be the cuts a bit larger; after care, let him heal as I have said, until he is healthy.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai IIII cauteres: II sus les II cornes dou chief, et I emmi le chief, et I ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac; et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	When apoplexy is old and you treat it in this way, but he does not get better, and the patient has no fever, then do four cauterizations: two on each of the two horns of the head, and one on the forehead, and one on the limb called "vasselz" as we have said before, and a cautery on the belly below the stomach; treat it in this way as we have said.
de litargie	of lethargy
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil; aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres; et c’est li maniere dou cautere: si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	For this disease, it is fitting to give the patient large and pill-like substances for the brain; after that, let him take the head of the patient with all his ailments, and place the emplastre of sinapis on the occipital bone, which is written in the treatment of emplastres; and this is the way of cautery: if he does so as I have said.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est; et s’il ne l’est, se li fai III cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere I doi de gros; et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai I cautere en mileu; et se mestiers est, II autres sus les II cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	If it is thus healthy, good is the state of the body and of the soul; and if not, three cauteries should be done to the extremities in the lower part near the neck, with a distance of one space between each cautery two of great size; and the cure as for others, and if you see it worsen, then let him have one cautery in the middle; and if it is skilled, then two other ones above the two horns, and the cure so long as he becomes healthy; and let those cauteries be called "olivare", just as I said before.
de la froidor dou chief	of coldness from the head
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit; aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et I derrier et III sus l’espinee dou col; et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai IIII cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos; et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	It is necessary that the head be cleansed of years and of what we have said before; after taking away the pus from the patient, then do cautery to the extremities of the head and on each horn, and two lower and three above the neck spine; and if you think it needs more, and the body is moist and the patient suffers greatly, and the disease is severe, then do four cauteries above the neck spine; and let him remain until his pain subsides, and lift your hand; after the cure as long as he becomes healthy, and let be those cauteries called "olivare" which we have said before.
de l’epilempsie	Of epilepsy
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	The epilepsy physicians should use fire cautery only on those who are spongy, and it is advisable first to moisten the brain with years and other remedies that we have said in the division when the patient is great and suffers from a great amount of painful medicine.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes; aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai I cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et I cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne; et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if it is an infant who cannot suffer, then let him do gargling and mastication moistening the brain often with bones meat; after letting him eat broth, and then he does fire cautery according to what we have said before, and he does fire cautery on the neck, and on each horn; and if the patient is violent and suffers greatly, then he does cauteries so as I have said to that who has paralysis and softening of the body, on the spine at the back and in the neck, and let him do oil cautery according to the manner I have said.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai I cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	If the patient is sick, then if he does fire cautery according to this manner:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When because of melancholy there are fluxes or moist spots corrupted and thick pus, then the fire cautery on affected parts as we have said to those who have paralysis.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	And if because of melancholy the fluxes decline to melancholy, and the body of the patient is moist, then give drink for what reason the brains may be purified, according to what has been said before in the division.
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide; aprés fai I torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com I cercle, si le met emmi le chief; et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars; aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien; et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir; aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier; et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the head of the patient is treated; after making the linen strip well made, like a circle, if you tie it to the head; and let the patient lie crosswise, and let them be held tight all over; afterwards present the linen, and apply ointment made from boiled butter of old sheep; and place the hot cloth on temperately so that it may not cause pain; after emptying the circle by tying it around the head, and letting it cool; and make this for each patient once a week with another good regimen, until they are cured.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere.	If you see someone being cautered while performing multiple pricks on the entire surface.
Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument; et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	This method of cautery makes the brain more swollen; and then applies wet cotton in butter and pig fat.
de l’awe des eulz	of the eyes.
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	When the eye comes first due to the signs I have said in the division, then start and do immediately give the patient a bitter medicine, cleansing the head from all moisture, and making it sweat or take a bath several times a day.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai II cauteres sus les II temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as II eulz ensamble, ou en I se li dessendemens est en I; et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple; et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	After he commands him to look up his head, and makes cautery on the inside of the head, and makes two more cauteries on both temples, if there is any weakness in both eyes together, or if one is weak in one; and strike all the veins and arteries under the wound, and make the cautery long according to the width of the temple; and beware of blood discharge, and if you see too much blood coming out, then bind with a strong poultice as you have.
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras; et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les II os derrier.	And I will teach you in the extraction of arteries and incising caution how to do it, and never at any time perform cautery or heat treatment below the two bones behind.
dou cors des larmes	of the eye.
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors; et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz: I cautere emmi le chief, et II cauteres sus les II temples, et II cauteres ou haiterel desoz les II os; et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout I petit cautere.	When the eyes are old and accustomed and have veins on them, or arteries that appear to be in front of the forehead; and if one sees that it's an accumulation of cold, moist, inflammatory matter, then do the cautery as I said at the beginning: cut off the top of the head, and cauterize each temple, and cauterize below each bone; and if necessary, more, cauterize with a sharp point under the eyebrow.
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	In the body of tears within the eyes
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide III nuis cochies; aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire; et fai II cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les II sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous; et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	When you administer the medicine as we have discussed in division, and it does not benefit the patient, then give to him three bitter medicines; after the king, and cut out the liver with fire, and do two cauteries of the cautery called "clavilis" above the two sores, one below the cheek; and beware of the artery that you do not cover.
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	And this is the form of the cautery called "clavilis":
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare».	When the paper of oil is softened by disease and moisture, then apply the cautery called "olivare".
de coi ci est li forme:	Because this is the form:
Et se tu vues si fai II cauteres sus les II sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont; et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	If you see such a burn, do II cauteries on the II wounds as well, long as the wound is; and don’t let go of your hand only until the third part of the paper is burned, according to the manner I’ve said.
dou poil qui point l’oil	Of a single hair that points at the bone
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	There is no instance where the hairs of the bone are converted to flesh, and prick the bone, and then one does cauteries according to two manners: that is to say by fire, or with hot medicine.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals; et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their birth, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain; aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz; puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When they grow and are even, then place the patient in a safe location; after that, put on paper over the eyes a figure like the shape of the mirror's smoke, and the beginning of the sign from the hairs; then put cotton moistened in wax and musk-like odor on oil, then take out the cautery according to this form:
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit; et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil; adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi III jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	After cauterizing on the figure that you have marked little by little many times, and the edges are slightly heated; and the signs of the work's health is that you see the paper retracted, and the hairs lifted to the oil tip; then lift your hand, and let it be so for three days, then put cotton moistened in butter until the cauterization is removed; after the ointment treatment until the patient is healed.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers; et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	Instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte; puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien; et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz; et se li maladie tient en I oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en I, et se en ambedous ausi; et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef; et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse I poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz,
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	When you have done this for a long time, if the medicine has been paid to you.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision; et s’il est ensi, si est bien.	And when the swelling has passed, if you lift the limb, and repair it so that you see the paper lifted as it was lifted by constraint of fire or by incision; and if it is thus, then it is well.
Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point; puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If this is not so, then apply again the medicine to the limb or let it be inoperative until your wounds are even, and your eyes are fixed; then put on cotton soaked in butter until the wounds close up, after applying an ointment called "dyafenis" and other remedies, until it is healed.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.	And if it is necessary for you to guard well your wound by great care so that the medicine does not touch your eyes.
Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	If the paper becomes damp after, and the hair pricks in oil, then resume the medicine on that person who is softened by the pure paper, just as you did before; after the cure until he is healed; and this is the form of the fire cauterization.
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens; et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	And know that the eyes of men differ in size and shape, and according to those, your constraints; and do not be returned to the right path for one who has the study of this art.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	Of the cure for fistula by cauterization.
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you cure a fistula as we have said in the divisions of diseases, and your cures are not profitable, then it is necessary that you cauterize them according to this manner.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain; et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief; aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil; aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz: et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere; se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente; mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	Instruct the patient to put his head in a safe place; and tie the menisters (his hair) between your hands in such a way that it does not move, nor do you make him's head move. After, put cotton wool moistened with vinegar or persille juice on the oil; after this, heat the cautery which is tied to it like the shape of a quill feather, so that they are assembled together; if you see it (the cautery), it should be applied from one head to another; and if you see it, it should be done as well as a tent. But whatever happens, this is what is worth seeing for your sake.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche; et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe; aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie; et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	After pressing the fistula and if it opens, take out the pus, and clean it; and if it closes, apply more oil; after that, put the hot cautery in the shape, and hold your hand on the cautery at the place of the wound from behind the ear, so as not to make a fool of yourself; and put the cautery into the fat of the oil, and let it corrupt.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	If you come to the beginning of the cautery just before the bone, it would be good.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors; aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers; et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	If it is not done again just once, and you need to do it again, and you let it happen for three days, after that put cotton soaked in butter on the wound, and apply a drying ointment until the patient is healed, and if 40 days pass without healing, then put an acid medicine corrosive until the bone is uncovered; and the price according to what he will come to his chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	And I have one way of treating an abscess that none of the ancients said.
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu; aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	Make sense of the abscess, and make an incision in it; after that put in the wound a thin thread of beeswax of which this is the shape:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc; et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil; et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe: li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	Instruct to take the quantity of 3.6 ounces of powder; and hold your hand firmly over the cauterized area, so that the patient does not move at all, until the powder is melted and falls into their oil; it is necessary to put on the oil a warm cloth, soaked in wine or ashes: the powder will heal the fistula, and save the healthy person from marvelous sickness.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	But if the fistula is healed by the cauterization that we have said, then it's good.
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	If it's not so, then it is necessary to administer poultices on the wound, and bring the fistula back into its proper place in the body according to what is most suitable for each person individually.
des crevaices en levres	of fissures in the lips
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Often there are cracks in the lips called "poil", and similarly in the lips of children.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe I petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When you are treating these cracks as we have said in division, and the cure does not benefit, then apply a small cautery with a spoon-like instrument according to this form:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font; aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And apply it immediately to those cracks until it is fully closed; then, after cleaning with lard, so that the wounds are healed.
de l’aposteme de la goule	of the abscess of the throat.
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule; et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie: adonques covient il que tu aies I cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule; aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu; et fai ensi une fois ou II, aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	When an abscess comes in the root of the throat or under the uvula, or on the palate, or at the roots of teeth, after making it rotten and running and becoming inflamed and developing a fistula; and you treat it as we have said in divisions, but it does not benefit: then it is necessary to apply cautery according to the size of the fistula; after removing or draining the fistula, hold your hand until the iron nail comes to the root of the nail, and make sure you take care around the area. Then do this once or twice, after treating as we have said in treatments, until it is healed; and if it heals so, that's good; but if not, then it is necessary to discover the root and remove the corrupted bone, according to what you find in its chapter.
dou movement des dens	The joint has moved out of its place
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain; aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent; et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent; aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit; aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you treat with medicines but it does not help, then put the head of the sick person on a clean cloth; after applying the cautery which will come from there in this manner that you place a string around the tooth; and put hot cauterization inside hastily, and hold your hand so the patient feels the heat coming to the root of the tooth; after lifting your hand and continuing the cautery according to your desire; after filling the patient's mouth with vinegar and salting it for an hour and keeping warm fires.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in this way the teeth that were moving are fixed, and the gums are restrained, and the moistures are corrupted and dried.
de la dolor des dens	Of the pain of the teeth
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc II manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	When pain of the teeth comes from cold, or there is cold in the ear, and medicines do not help, then it is necessary to cut according to two ways: and fire cautery and butter cautery.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain; aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez; et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus I fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	Butter cautery if is such that you apply butter of wool, and the end in a iron or iron tongs; after taking cotton and wrapping it around the tip of a tent, and the pus in butter boils, and puts on the painful tooth hastily and holds until it cools; and so does this many times until its virtues come to the root of the tooth, and if you see that wool and cotton in butter burn, and puts on the tooth bleeding, and puts on iron hot until the heat comes to the tip of the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide; aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez; fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	Instruct the patient to hold a burning cautery, such that you grasp a iron or hemp chain, and it is thick enough so that the fire does not reach the patient's mouth; after heating the cautery, because its form will come later, put it on the tooth and hold your hand until it cools down; do this often, because the pain will be removed the same day or the next.
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it is fitting that the patient fills his mouth with good butter in the haste of applying this cautery, and then they rush to heat it up; and this is the form of the cautery:
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir; et c’est li forme de la caine:	And make a cautery of whatever thickness you like, and according to your power; and this is the form of the chain:
des scrophules	Warts
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie; et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume; et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors; et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee; aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	When warts are swollen and moist, cold, and not subject to digestion by medicines, then apply the cautery to the hair because it follows this form afterwards, and make incisions for the humors to come out from the cautery on the other side; and put the cautery hot above the abscess once, or as soon as it serves them, until the abscess comes to a boil; if the abscess is small, apply cautery according to the size of the abscess, and leave it so for three days; and put cotton soaked in butter on top until the swelling goes away; after treatment, allow the patient to use ointments and poultices until they are healed.
Li forme de la cainne:	The shape of the cauterized area.
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives; aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	When the moistors (moisture) win over the channels of the body, and especially when it comes from cold complexion, then it is necessary that the patient be voided first by medicines soluble; after applying fire cautery to the root of the throat, and beware so that you do not come near the throat again, and do not burn with heat but just a little.
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant; et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	After applying fire cautery to the joint of the neck at the head of the spine, and apply cautery to what is called "the claw" (clavicle), because it has this shape, treat as we have said before until it is safe.
de la toust	From the throat
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai ij cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis; et I autre cautere emmi le pis entre II mameles; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	When all the sickness of the pimple is due to cold moistures, and the patient has no fever or scorch, and the disease is old, then apply two fire cauteries on the skin in its veins; and another fire cautery between the two nipples; and apply cautery according to what we have said before, which is called "the claw" because of the shape.
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles; et soient li poins jusc’a XXX, ou enqui entor.	If you see it, do fire cautery by pricking at the total cautery that is called "points" because of this form being before in the illness of the ears; and be the points just a thousand or more.
Aprés cure le leu selonc ceu qui est devant dit, et soit li cauteres a III rains selonc ceste forme:	After healing the wound according to what is said before, and if the cauterizations are three times according to this form:
Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais III a cop.	And because these cauterizations are lighter, because you do three at one time.
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	of the shoulder joint.
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit; aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre; et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners douqueil ci est li forme:	Instruct the patient to lie on their back and on their chest; after take care of the cut that is inside the fistula (with two fingers from your left hand); and if the joint is dislocated, apply the cautery (fire tool) which has the form of II ners douqueil (I don't know what "II" refers to here as it was probably some sort of abbreviation).
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble IIII cauteres; et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a III ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres; et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a III ners:	and cauterize the cut so that it pierces just to the side of the chest, and comes with the figure of the cautery which is made of III ners (I don't know what "III" refers to here as it was probably some sort of abbreviation); for this is done with a cautery having III ners (same issue as before) because the figures of cauterization are these three cauteries; and they have nerves according to the subtlety of a tent, which is the form of the cautery having III ners:
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce I nerf por coi il i a VIII cauteres.	And sometimes they press against this nerve because there are eight cauteries.
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil; aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	After putting the cautery on the raw flesh with a cord; after putting him to rest, and not letting the limbs lie for a long time until he is well comforted.
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant.	And if he is dislocated, such a thing often happens little by little, therefore do cautery on the thick part of the clavicle, or many cauteries in pricking.
Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	Because the joint is closed, and the moisture and the bone are healed, and the patient is cured.
Quant en l’estomac vienent froidures et mout de moistors tant qu’il l’estraient a sa complexion, et sont multipliet li catharre a lui, et es manieres de cures acostumees et il ne profite mie, adonc covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son dos, et estende ses jambes et ses mains.	When colds and much moisture enter the stomach, such that he extracts them to his complexion, and many catarrhes appear to him, and in the usual treatments he does not profit, therefore it is necessary that the patient be covered on his back, and stretch his legs and hands.
De ceu en aprés li fai III cauteres I desoz la cuillier dou pis per la quantiteit d’un doi, a tout le cautere clavile, et II cauteres defuers les II costez tant que li figure des cauteres soit a III angles, et ait teil espaice entre l’une et l’autre qu’elles ne soient jointes ensamble quant elles giteront porriture; et soient li cautere si parfont qu’il porpreignent les II pars dou keur, et soit li figure des cauteres selonc ceste forme sens ajostement:	In the aftermath of this fire cautery, make III cauteries I below the nail of the finger by the quantity of two measures, to all cauteries clavicle, and II cauteries before the II sides so that the figure of the cauteries is at III angles, and has a space between them as long as they do not come together when they get dry; and so that the cauteries be done so that they prick the II parts of blood, and the figure of the cauteries according to this shape until touching.
Et se tu vues cauterize d’un grant cautere enmi l’estomac selonc ceste forme; et celui qui avra paour de cest cautere, cauterize en poignant et seigne sus l’estomac i. point selonc la quantiteit que tu vues d’enche; puis le cauterize a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if you see someone being cut with a large cautery in the stomach according to this shape; and if he has fear of this cautery, cut at the point of the sting and sign above the stomach i. point according to the quantity that you see from the needle; then cut all the way around what is called "poins".
Aprés le cure de la cure que nos avons eut devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the treatment of the treatment we had before, until it is safe.
Quant au foie vient dolor de froit et de moistor et de grosse ventositeit, tant qu’il est fuer mis de sa complexion natureil per les superfluitez; et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne li profite mie, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son haitereil; et signe d’enche III cauteres selonc ceste forme et ceste figure et ceste quantiteit sus lou foie, defuer les ypocondres, lai ou li coutes de l’ome vient; et ait d’espaice entre chaicun cautere la groissece d’un doi; et soient li cautere dou lonc dou cors, et ne presser mie mout ta main a tot le cautere; et soit arse tant soulement li moitiez dou keur, et soit li malaides drois sus ses piez; et s’il ne peut, si soit gisans, et estende ses jambes, et lieve ses brais; et c’est li forme:	As to the liver, when it has pain from frost and moisture and great swelling, so that it is forced out of its natural shape due to the accumulation of superfluities; and patients are cured with what we have said in divisions, but it does not benefit them, if the patient must be shaved over his hairy area; and sign of performing three cauteries according to this form and figure and quantity on the liver, excluding hypochondriacs, at the place where the pain is located; and there should be space between each cautery the thickness of a dole; and let the cauteries be long in body length, and not press hard with your hand all over the cautery; and burn only the moist parts of the heat, and make the patient stand upright on his feet; and if he cannot, so that he may lean, and extend his legs, and lift his arms; and this is the form:
Et se ta volentez est, si cauterize ces cauteres dou cutellaire, se tu es subtilz et saiges en l’art, et te warde que tu n’ardes mie tout le keur, car tu feroies sechier tout le cors; et qu’il ne viegne jusc’a boueil, car li keurs est mout subtilz lai endroit, et lou saiches por voir.	If you wish it so be done, cauterize these cauteries with the cutlery, if you are subtle and wise in the art, and beware that you do not burn your entire flesh, for you will dry out all the body; and if it happens before I burn, because the blood is very subtle at the point, and you know how to see.
Quant il a apostume au foie, et tu vues savoir s’il est en la char dou foie ou en la toile: s’il est en la char, se sent li malaides dolor ne mie trop fort; et s’il est en la toile, si sent dolor forsenee.	When there is an abscess on the liver, and you see if it is in the flesh of the liver or in the membrane: if it is in the flesh, the patient feels pain that is not very strong; but if it is in the membrane, he feels sharp and severe pain.
Et lors quant ceste cure desoit les mires, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus sa teste; et puis seigne d’enche le leu ou li apostumes est, et puis chaufe le cautere qui est semblans au rais, de coi ci est li forme:	And when this treatment should extract pus, it is fitting that the patient be seated on his head; and then gently remove the pus where it is, and then heat the cautery which resembles a knife, for this is its shape.
Et cauterize I cautere tant que li keurs soit ars, et viegne jusc’a syphac, tant que li porreture soit toute fuers; aprés la cure selonc la cure des essues tant qu’il soit sanez; et ne covient mie que de cest cautere use nuls fuers que cil qui ait estudieit longement en l’art de medicine, et par cui mains cestes maladies ont corrut aucune fois.	Instruct the patient to cauterize until the hairs are dry, and it has just begun to be sucked out, so that the wound is completely healed; after the treatment as per the treatment of wounds, until he is cured; and it is not advisable to use any fire from this cautery on anyone who has studied long in the art of medicine, and through whose hands these diseases have been cured at some time.
Adonques puet il hardiement ovrer, et toutevoies il me semble que mues vaut li laissier.	And therefore he can be strongly applied to, and it seems to me that you should leave him.
dou cautere de pleuresin	For the cautery of pleurisy.
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere: pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois; et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize I cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et II petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe; et II cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc; et I cautere emmi le pis, et I autre sus l’estomac, et I entre II espaules, et II as II costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre II espaules; et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	The ancients said that for pleurisy you must perform cauterization with roots of Aristolochia, in this manner: take a long root of Aristolochia, the largest you can find, and make it dry, and just as thick and as long as your thumbs; and apply olive oil to it, and press it into fire, and cautery between the navel and the neck, and two pokes down from the chin; between the fifth rib and the sixth, declining towards a little; one cauterizes on the hip, and another above the stomach, and between two shoulders, and two along the lower ribs on either side of the cautery between two shoulders; and do not press with your hand, but make it as open as in the odorant.
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a I raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme; et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l’aposteme dou foie.	And they said an old man that no one uses cautery of fire like the razor, and the flint and put it between the ribs, until it comes to that place; and the fire burns the pain, as we have said in the passage about the liver.
Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	But in this work there is fear or the patients are dying now, or a fistula comes that cannot be cured.
de la mice	of the mouse.
Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent III manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin.	When you cure the mouse disease of those who we have said have different treatments, and it does not benefit, then there are three ways of cautery that all are good.
Desquelz li une maniere si est que tu faices III cauteres, ou IIII, en lignant selonc la longor de la mice, selonc la figure dou cautere dou foie que nos avons dit devant; et n’apresser mie ta main a tout le cautere, et soit li malaides sovins sor son dos; et une autre maniere de cautere si est que tu eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners, si com nos l’avons mostreit en la dislocation de l’espaule; et lieve le keur qui est endroit la mice, ou li coutes dou malaide vient devers senestre, et soit li elevations dont tu lieves le keur selonc la keur, selonc la longesce dou cors, et li cautere soient selonc la largesce dou cors.
