There are two ways of cautery: one is that you do three cauteries, or four, linking them according to the length of the mouse, according to the figure of the cautery of the liver which we have said before; and do not hurry at all with the cautery, and let the patient suffer on his back; and another way of cautery is that you fire the cautery that has two nails, as we have shown in the dislocation of the shoulder; and lift the wound that is right over the mouse, or the cost comes to the left side, and so lift the wound according to the wound, according to the length of the body, and the cautery be according to the width of the body.
Aprés i boute les II ners enflamez tant que li keurs soit perciez de l’autre part, et puis trai fuers le cautere, et ensi en i avra IIII Et se tu vues, si cauterize a tot le cautere a III ners.	After the II nerves are inflamed, fire them so that they become perceivable from the other side, and then apply fire to the cautery, and thus in four there will be. And if you see, cauterize with the entire cautery for three times.
Aprés le cure quant il a geteit porriture par lonc tens, et ce vaut mues que li autre des cures devant dites.	After the treatment when they have gotten dirty for long time, and this is what it means that the other treatments I mentioned before.
de ydropisie	of dropsy
Cautere ne vaut a ydropique, fors c’a la maniere qui est apelee «asclytes».	Cautery is not useful for dropsy, except when done in the way called "asclytes".
Quant tu la cures selonc les manieres que nos avons dit en divisions, et ta cure ne profite mie, adonques covient il que tu li faices IIII cauteres entor la boude, et I sus l’estomac, et un sus le foie, et I sus la mice, et II derrier le dos sus l’espinee, et I endroit le pis; et soit li cauteres bien pres de l’espés dou keur.	When you cure according to the ways we have said in divisions, and your treatment does not help, then it is necessary that you make four cauteries inside the swollen area, and one above the stomach, and one above the liver, and one above the groin, and two behind the back on the spine, and one on the lower part of the leg; and let the cauteries be very close to the affected spot.
Aprés laisse le cautere aovert por giter porriture lonc tens, et ne lassier mie la cure dou malaide aprés le cautere; et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les II ententions avec l’aide de Deu.	Instruct the patient to leave the fire cautery open for a long time until it is full of pus, and do not finish the cure on the patient after the cautery; and healing will be hastened, and the two humors will conjoin with God's aid.
Li forme dou cautere por le ventre soit li clavile que nos avons devant mostreit; et cil por le dos soit olivaire, selonc ceu qu’il est ci devant mis.	The form of the cautery on the abdomen is a nail that we have shown before, and this olive oil on the back, according to what has been placed there previously.
de l’enfleure des piez	of the swelling of the feet
Quant li piez sont enflez a celui qui est ydropique, et sont plain d’awe citrine, il covient que tu cauterizes sus le dos dou piet entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire; et lieve ta main avec le cautere sens torner.	When the feet are swollen in a person who is dropsical and filled with blood citron, it is necessary to cautery on the back of the foot between the auricular and ankle joint, and lift your hand with the cautery as you turn.
Et n’entrer mie trop em parfont, ensi sarrait fuers li awe citrine, et soit li cauteres selonc cest forme:	And do not enter too deeply into it, as this would cause the blood to be wasted like burning one in fire, and so let the cautery be done according to this form:
Aprés fai sus II jambes II cauteres en chescune jambe a la pointe dou cutellaire; et soit li cauteres dou lonc, l’un desoz le genoil devant et l’autre defuers, enmi la jambe; et laisse les cauteres aovers longement sens curer, que li awe en isse; aprés le cure des autres cures que nos avons dit.	After doing this twice, for each leg make two cauteries at the point of the blade; and let one cautery be long in front of the knee and another behind it on the leg, so that they may stay long enough to heal before proceeding with the other treatments that we have mentioned.
de la menoison	of the wound
Quant solution de ventre vient de froidor et de moistor, tant que li vertus retentive et digestive qui est ou stomac et en l’intestine est afleboie, et ne puet estre curez par manieres de cures; et tu vois le malaide bien soffrant et de fort vertut, si fai I grant cautere sus l’estomac selonc ceu qu’il en a parleit ci devant ou cautere de l’estomac, au cautere circule; et IIII cauteres entor la boude subtilz a tout I cautere clavile subtil, et II cauteres sus les hainches.	When an inflammation of the belly comes on from cold and moisture, so that the virtues retaining and digesting which are in the stomach and intestines are dried up, and cannot be cured by any treatments; and you see the patient suffering greatly and with great swelling, then do a large cautery on the abdomen according to what he has spoken of before or the cautery for the abdomen, after that make four cauteries beneath the small intestine subtle and all over, and two cauteries on the groin.
Et se tu vois les moistors habundans et le malaide soffrant, se li fai cautere sus le poignil, et I cautere sus chaicun yle, et II petis cauteres sus l’estomac delez le grant, car li cure est profitans quant il i a bone aide.	If you see the moistors abundant and the patient suffering, instruct the patient to perform cauterization on the nail, and cauterize each finger, and ask for cauterizations on the stomach under the great pain, because the cure is beneficial when it has good aid.
de la cure des emorroydes	Of the treatment of hemorrhoids.
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres: III sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et I cautere desoz la boude II dois; et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on I grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et I autre sus le foie, et I autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile; et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens.	When hemorrhoids are found at the fundament or one or more of them and are old and large with frozen and corrupted cold moist humors, treat as we have said in divisions, but if you do cauterizations: III on the spine behind the back, where it is all turned away from the almequade, point by point in triangles, and I on the buttocks II; and if you think that its stomach is cooled down and meat does not cook, and a face swells up, then grant a cauterization on the stomach, as has been said before, and another on the liver, and another on the mice in all directions with clavicle cauterizations; and let the cauterization remain for a long time.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After a cure, let him so that he becomes healthy.
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	of the fleshiness which is called "theleul
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit; et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort; fai ceu une fois ou II, et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit; aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez; et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	When you cut the flesh (theleul), if it seems like a knife is cutting through it, and then put everything on fire in that place cut by the knife, and let your hand be enough so that the cautery comes to the navel of the woman, for this will not cut; do this once or twice, and if there is much flesh (theleul) there, cauterize each part as we have said; after cure with bandages, profit from ointments until they are healthy, and if you cauterize a great cautery on the catim (i.e. the groin), it will give more aid.
de plaie mal curee	of badly treated wounds
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	When the patient cannot bear torture or opening, which we will tell in his own words, if it comes to this illness that cannot be cured except by cautery.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont.	As for a fistula, and being old and rotten with pus and moist corruption, if you gently probe the whole thing, and keep in mind that you know how deep it is.
Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou II ou III, selonc la quantiteit de som besoing; et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes.	After applying the cautery that seems like a razor, and pouring it into the fistula according to the quantity that the instrument has entered, and repeating the cautery until the corrupted flesh is burned off once, twice, or three times, according to the extent of the wound; and take care not to burn the nerve that are involved, and great pains.
se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	In case the fistula remains in the body of the intestine and in the intestine, watch out for these signs, and do not perform this fire treatment unless on a charcoal bough, and think that it is not pure; after healing, keep him so long as he is healthy, and if the signs indicate that he is still sickly, and the substances are ossified for a long time, then know that he has become entirely healthy; and if the substances are not ossified, know that he is rotten, and the bone is corrupted in the form; and so as one of these we will tell you on your behalf.
de la maladie des reins	of kidney disease
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit; et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra III cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	When pain of the kidney comes with great vomiting, and there is no relief from women, then it is necessary to perform cautery on both kidneys, one part on top of the other, at the cautery chisel that we have previously mentioned; and if they cauterize in the middle, so will require three cauteries in line, and will give more relief.
de la vessie	of the bladder
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et I a destre et I a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce; et li fais I cautere defuers le dos, ou II se tu en as besoing; et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	When the bladder is weak and soft from injury and moisture, if the patient holds urine in, then he should do a fire cautery on the part that is facing upwards on the bladder, where the hair starts at the root, and both left and right sides, so each one does it long as one finger's breadth; and he makes them cauterize behind the back, where they are needed; and so, make the cauterizations in the shape before said.
de la marris	of the uterus
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde; et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor: adonques covient il c’on li faice III cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et II cauteres defuers le dos; et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	When the uterus is cold and moist, and does not allow conception, and the flowers are corrupted and their ends are late; and when they come, so it causes great pain: therefore it is fitting that one cauterizes inside the womb, just as we have said for the bladder cautery, and also cauterize behind the back; and make them cauterize in the shape as we have said.
de la hainche	Of the groin
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a I cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	When the moist viscous substances descend to the groin, and because of this he is unable to move, and it is found that his crotch is longer than the other when measured together; and it is discovered that there are many swellings in the departement (of the crotch) as a result, so it is fitting that you cauterize the patient under the groin at a cautery similar to a circle, and sign the line around the groin as it turns, so that the groin may be within the circle; and if it has been cauterized in such a way as when one cauterizes the stomach.
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai III cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if this cautery is not present, then he makes three cauteries of the large olive tree, and they are cauterized as deep as all the others; and the physician until he is healed.
de la dolor de la hainche	Of the pain of the groin
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When pain comes to the groin, and it is caused by coldness and moisture, and the patient is cured according to what we said in division, but the cure does not work, and the disease is ancient: then it is necessary that you purge the patient of heavy humors, or fetid pills, or other hard pills that resemble them.
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu.	After you cut [the patient], and the method of cutting is according to two manners: that is to say, assembling hot medicines, and cautery with fire.
Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz: que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche III cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire; aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a IIII selonc ceste forme:	Cautery with fire is according to many manners: of which some are such that you cut [the patient] as follows: you cauterize on the groin three times, and you cut according to this form, and make a deep and narrow cut, and leave space between each cut equal to twice the thickness of two fingers, and it should be olive-shaped; sometimes one makes a cautery at the midpoint above the head of the groin, because there are four such manners:
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	If you see, such as the fire cautery on the cauterized area that we have before mentioned in the dislocation of the hamstring; but do it in a manner that the circle contains the entire hamstring, and all the flesh around the wound be burned.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe.	And that's the way to do it in sciatique, when the pain is in the hamstring and does not reach as far as the thigh or as far as the leg.
Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai II cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et I cautere desus la cheville IIII dois, a la partie senestre un poc; et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur; et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor III poins ou IIII au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if it comes as far as the thigh and the leg, he makes two more cauterizations on the place where the patient says the pain is, and four cauterizations above the ankle, to the left side one point; and whether it's a cutlery cauterization or sear of the thick flesh; and if the patient feels that the pain extends up to two feet or nearly to his foot, he should cauterize where he feels the pain three points or four at the cauterization which is called "poins".
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	And if the skill is present, if he makes more; and if he knows that the pain will be below the knee towards the thigh, he does fire cautery with a cutlass or circular cautery, and keeps well guard in all his cauteries so that you do not make the cautery too hot as to burn the nerves and great arteries, and you do not cause more annoyance and contraction for the patient.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez.	And I myself have seen others who did fire cautery on the ankle of the foot, and they left it so that the leg was completely swollen, and also the toes, and it became infected and corrupted all the toes.
Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	After a cauterization of the belly where he had the death.
Et se li dolors est en II parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere.	And if the pains are in both sides together, do cauterize in one and in the other, as this manner.
Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai I tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce; et soient li entrechetres aovers de II pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait I mainche de fer bien fait; et c’est li forme:	Instruct the wise ones in the cautery of hawthorn, for this is the manner, make such a nail and let it be as big as our sailor's thumb or a little less, and let it be set apart by equal intervals so that there are spaces like the length of an apple seed; and let the intervals be four times as long as one another, and let them be like nuts, and have a well-made iron nail; and this is the form:
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit; et lou cauterize une fois I cautere reont et lou laisse III jors; et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens; aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	And heat it so that it is completely red and smells of pitch, and then place it on the hawthorn stump of the sick person, and turn it towards their healthy side; cut once with the cautery and let them recover for three days; after, apply a poultice of butter and leave the wound uncovered for a long time until they are healed.
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent; et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	Albucasim says that we should use little of this cauterization because of the fear of its effects, and if you see few who use it; for all see are good cautersies, which can be endured.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant si est que tu faices I estrument a entrechetres en coi dessende li marge de la porte, et soit d’arain ou de fer a une paroit longe, et en la hautece ait II nous, et ait entre chaicun la quantiteit de la groissece d’un doi; et soient overt defuer et desus, et se joignent ensamble selonc ceste forme:	The cauterization of medicine burns if you make an instrument between crosswise in what descends from the edge of the opening, and is made of iron or of iron long and thin, and two nails, and has one on each side, and its length equals that of a half-dog; and so do not cut short and do not cut off, but join them together according to this form:
Aprés met sus la boiste de la hainche au malaide gisant sor suin costeit sain, et apresse ta main mout sus la boiste de la hainche; aprés giete entre les II cercles de l’awe chaude qui soit chaufee au feu I poc, et li laisse une houre dou tens, et soffre li malaides la chalor et l’arsure de li.	After place the flint on the patient lying on his side with his costlet unclean, and press your hand very much on the flint of the hawthorn; afterwards pour between the two circles of hot water which is heated in a little fire, and let him rest for an hour by ten, and suffer the pain and the burning of him.
Car il i trueve mordication ausi com de feu; et quant li mordications iert passee, se lieve ta main avec l’estrument et leve la hainche d’awe douce, et laisse ensi III jors, et met sus burre tant que ceu qui est noir de l’eschaudure soit osteit; et lou laisse III jors que porriture en istrait; et ceu serait li derriene aide aprés le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	For the mordication of teeth, just like cautery; and when the mordication has not passed, lift your hand with the instrument and lift the cheek from its soft flesh, and leave it for three days, and put on butter until the bone in the socket is extracted; and let him leave three days before the swelling disappears; and this would be the hindmost aid after the treatment of ointments until he is healed.
Et se li dolor s’est estendue jusc’a la cuisse ou jusc’a la jambe, se li fai I estrument que teigne awe selonc ceu que tu as fait en la hainche igaument; et c’est li maniere de l’awe chaude, et je l’ai escripte ou traitier de la rectification de medicine.	And if the pain has spread just to the thigh or just to the leg, make the same instrument as you did in the cheek for a longer time; and this is the method of the hot cloth, which I have written about in treating with medication.
Pren alcali et chaulz vive, autant de l’une com de l’autre, et les broie ensamble, et les met en I nuef pot.	Take lime and calx vivus, as much of each as you have, grind them together, and put them in a new pot.
ou il ait I petit pertuis defuer se que li pointe d’un raisor i puisse entreir; et met desor celui pot I autre pot bien plombeit, et met sus alcali et chalz et awe douce sus, tant qu’il en i ait I doi desus les poudres cant tu l’avras bien preingte a ta main; et le laisse ensi tant qu’il en dessende awe ague et chiece ou pot plombeit, puis pren toute cele awe, et la giete sus chalz et sus alcali si com devant.	If there is no small opening to avoid, so that the point of a needle can enter; and place over the other pot with good fat, and put on calx and chalk and sweet oil upon it, as long as you have two fingers over the powder when you will take it firmly in your hand; and leave it thus until it comes out with blood and cheese or fat, then take all that, and put on chalk and on calx so.
Et lors si sera mout ague et est aministree en mou d’ovraiges de medicine et en cauteres d’autres membres Car elle fait auteil oevre com feus, et si a autres medicines dont on cauterize bien la hainche ensi com tesisie et miel anacardi et chalz avec savon, toutes ces choses mellees ensamble.	And when it is much swollen and is treated with the movement of other medical works and cauteries of other members, for they make all that fire work, and with other medicines where one cauterizes well the neck thus as with cauterization and honey acacia and chalk with soap, all these things are mixed together.
Et Galiens nos raconte une cure dont uns hons fut curez de la dolor de la hainche et de la voine sciatique, et lou loe mout, et dit que on n’i fist autre cure, et qu’il en fut sanez a une soule fois quant on ot fait ceste cure, et il se fut baigniez si com il l’enseigne ci aprés.	And the Gaians tell us of a cure for one man who was cured of the pain in his groin and sciatic nerve, and he had great praise, and said that no other cure was needed, and that he became whole again only once when this cure was performed, and he bathed as he taught it after this.
Et dist en teil maniere que tu preignes dou litargire vert fres et sec, et le broie mout avec I poc de graisse, et met sus la hainche et sus la cuisse et sus la jambe ou la dolor tient, et la lie; et li laisse III houres et par la quantiteit que li malaides ne sente plus l’arsure.	And in another way, he says to take a green and fresh gallwort, and pound it much with a little fat, and put it on the groin and thigh and leg where the pain lies, and bind; and let him for three hours, by the quantity that the patient does not feel the burning.
Et puis le fai entrer ou bain tant que li cors li soit un poc arousez, et lou fai entrer ou lit, et li dolor s’en ira toute et sera sanez.	And then he puts him in the bath until his body is a little moistened, and he puts him to bed, and the pain will go away altogether and will be healed.
Et saiches que nuls ne doit user de cautere de telz medicines, se ceu n’est aprés l’evacuation de cors.	And instructs you that no one should use fire cautery on such a medicine unless it has been evacuated from the body.
Et Dyascorides dist que quant li voine sciatique est cauterizee de fiens de chievre, si i aide mout; et doit estre fais li cauteres en teil maniere.	And Dicyscorides says that when the sciatic vein is treated with horsehair cord, if it helps a great deal, and must be done in this manner.
Prenez lainne et la beurez d’oile vielz, et metez sus la fossete qui est entre le pouce dou piez et l’autre qui est apelez foscile.	Take linen and anoint with old oil, and place it on the crevice between the little toe and the other one called the fossicle.
Aprés pren fiens de chievre sec, et l’empren a feu tant qu’il soit charbons, et lou met sus la laine, et le laisse tant qu’il soit estains; et refai encor ensi, et ne cesser de faire ensi tant que tu penses par sens qu’il viegne jusc’a la hainche, et que li dolor soit cessee; et cist manieres de cautere est apelez «cautere de chievre».	After taking horsehair cloth dry, and wrapping it around the object so that it is charred with fire, until it is stained, then put linen on it, and let it be in that state until it stains; and repeat again in the same way, and do not cease to do so until you think by sense that it has come just up to the joint, and that the pain is ceased; and this manner of fire treatment is called "cautere of horsehair".
de la dolor dou dos	of the shoulder pain
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, or from falling or percussion, or by excessive bleeding, or because of the spreading out of cold matter, none of these things are worth cautery, except for those who come from an infusion of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne V cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai III cauteres ou IIII au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	It is necessary after this that the patients be void of fetid pills or other similar things on their back, as long as the pain lies there, three lines marked with "enchel", and in each line, perform cautery or more according to virtue and quantity that the patient can bear; and let the cautery be done according to the cautery called "poins"; and if you see, do III cauteries or IV at the clavicle midpoint according to this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	This illness comes often to small children, and the signs of its onset are that they have a narrow spine when they lift up, and fear; and you find in the lower back in the spine on their back and in this appearance which comes above the other spines.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this and you see it being cured, if you cauterize with the cautery of a cell according to this form.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument.	If the cauterization turns purple in each part of the spine equally.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant II lignes ou III, et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre.	And if you see, if cauterizing inside the spine with the cauterizing needle in two or three lines, and they are pointing to one another.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	After the cure, let it be so that he is restored to health according to what we have said, and guard so as not to administer cauterization in swelling which is in the grasp of nerves.
de la dolor des jointes	Of the pain of joints
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When pain of joints are swollen in each member of the body, and when pain comes on to the foot, they call it "podagre" exactly, and when it's caused by cold and medicines can't cure it, then it is cured with cautery in this way: make a mound of cautery around the joint of the foot, and use olive oil according to this shape:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point».	And if there is a sore that you prick on the face of the foot, make a cautery all around the point.
Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil III cauteres ou IIII de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if the pains come just to the knees and other joints, and this often happens, make a cautery on each knee three cauteries or four of each part, all around the olive oil cautery; and if you need more, make more, but don't hold your hand too hot until the spasm of the knee is burned.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre.	And if the pains come down just to the knees and back, serve the fire cautery that we have said in this chapter.
Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines.	And if the pains are in the hands, so that they become swollen for two lines; and if there is no pain after that, apply pressure on each joint and on each finger; and if pains come from the elbows or shoulders, cauterize each part, and give good treatment to the patient and prescribe medicines.
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	But if you give good treatment and purge the humors, he will be saved by God.
de la routure dou syfac	of the surgical incision of the abscess.
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When an abscess comes to the armpit, and the swellings descend to the joints and it is new, it is fitting that when you cure his eyes, he should not use those remedies the next day; and he should use things that calm the belly, so that the fever descends from his belly. After this, have him sit on his back between your hands, and command him to pull out his arm until the swellings are reduced, and then tie it up with your hands, and observe carefully to see if there is a sign similar to half of a circle above the bone of the elbow; then take the cautery in its shape:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	So long as he is white and his senses are clear.
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	Then tie the bowels to their place; and have the attendants apply pressure with their hands so they do not return immediately; work well on the patient's knees and put over them stockings and servants, and another on the legs that hold back the hands; then put the cautery on the marked sign with all your force, your right hand and your left as long as you pierce into the bone, and if you miss it the first time, do so again until you get to the bone; and be careful not to let the bowels escape while you are doing this cautery; lest you burn them; and in this way, the patients will not die from another evil.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	And know that when you do not come to the bone with the cautery, your work is worthless.
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	Instruct the cauters to be subtle according to each person's measure; and for children also as much as they are able; after three days of cure with butter cautery until the scab falls off; after the treatment of other ointments until the patient is healed, and apply warmth to the patient for forty days on their back until the wound is well closed; and it is advisable that their hair be washed long enough so that the boils do not burst when they come out to go to chambers.
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	And after forty days, when he wishes to rise, dress him with a well-made bandage, and pour it on for another forty days; let him have good rest, that he may work little and guard against excessive drinking and eating, and from drinking too much; and if he follows this instruction, he will be entirely healed.
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And I will say this after the treatment of cutting in its chapter.
de la routure dou ventre	of the operation on the abdomen.
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	When other incisions come in the belly and are known, and you see that they do not grow again, then apply to them according to their quantity, and burn out one third of the heat; after the cure as we have said; and none of the ancients has said that it should be cauterized at three angles according to this shape:
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile.	but first mark the spot of the incision and make a line above it to indicate its width; and then with your own hand, bind tight all around the cauterized part.
Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	But the first incisions are lighter and more tender.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	From old pain in any member
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	When pain comes to any member, or from a fall or an injury, and the pain lingers for a long time, and medicine cures are not effective, then it is necessary to cauterize with the "pins" cautery, and do the cauterizations according to the length of the member, its smallness, and its weakness, and its virtue, and its location of twists and of pain.
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	If there is safety from the first cautery, that is well; but if this term does not serve, repeat another cautery on that same place, because it is a custom to let it move towards the nearest member, so that you make cauterizations until the patient is healed.
de meselerie	Of poor workmanship
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	The problem is not cured by cautery with great help, and the disease that comes from the rotting of swine and melancholy.
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief: I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	You can see the cauterizer, take care if the disease is at the beginning, and if it's cured according to what we have said in division, and do not cut or stay, and you doubt that the corruption will infect the entire patient, so make cautery on the head: I make a new cut on the head, and another towards the front of the ears; two above the two horns, and one behind the nail; and leave your hand there until the cautery comes to bone, and until the scabs come out so much that the vapors of the large humors can come out; and cauterize on the mouse according to what it is in front.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et I cautere en som lou neis, et II cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et VI cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et I grant sus la crupie et I autre delez, et II sus les II espaules; et II sus les coutes, et II sus les tendrons dou pis, et I sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et I autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et I autre sus lou foie.	And if the ulcer is spread all over; and it manifests itself, so you should cauterize with these cauterizations that we have mentioned earlier on the head, and in some of the nails, and two cauterizations above the spine of the neck, and six above the spine of the back, and one on the crupel, and one on the other flesh, and two on the shoulders, and two on the loins, and two on the tendons of the foot, and one on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the fosses of the hands; and you must guard against the ners that are above the skin burning, so they do not burn; and never cauterize on the bone of the finger, and one on the bone of the stomach, and one on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	And know that when you do more cauterization, the patient receives more benefit, and the pain increases; and know that the sick person feels no pain from cauterization as long as they are healthy, because the body is completely corrupted.
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	And it is fitting that the fire cautery should be large and small according to the members and joints, as you will find in various iron instruments.
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	After treatment let the patient eat flour several times with honey and other treatments until he is safe.
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	When inflammation arises in any member and is treated with medicines, oils, and plasters, and it is not safe, then make fire cauteries on the member according to the size and shape of the member; and if the cautery goes inside the flesh of the wound, a little into the sore place, then treat with bandages until he is safe.
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	And at no time should one do cautery by hand and on the foot and on the back, to the end of the nerve where the member is mute, and thus if the inflammation exists; and let none get involved unless he knows the members and their exit points for moving the joints of the body.
de albaras	of hairs
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease called "albaras" is old and the art of medicine is worthless, then apply cautery with a cautery knife by half to its depth, according to the quantity of the fat that is taken away, until the flesh is exposed, and is moved in color; then treat the cure with flour of vinegar and lentils with olive oil and leaves of plantain, and blood from chicken and blood from almonds, each one a part; and mix everything together, and tie it up with a bandage, and apply to the patient until he is cured.
li cure de chancre par cautere	the cure for the chancre by cautery
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	When the chancre comes on at the beginning, and you look at it stop, then apply cautery to the cautery that seems like a circle, all around the turn of the chancre.
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	Instruct the wise men that we should apply fire cautery to the middle of the ulcer; and I do not think it is good, for I fear that it will cause ulcers and corruption, and I have never wanted to come across this before; and there is no more urgent thing than that they be cauterized inward, at the "circle", as we have said in many cauteries.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of the swelling which cannot die
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi.	When some have a disease called "adubelati" which cannot die because of its superfluity or because the old man is too weak and has little blood or time, and you see it hastening to death: then cauterize inward with many small cauteries on the point; after that.
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	It will soon die.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see it pierced with the cautery at all of the cautery, so that the cautery is hot.
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	And put your hand in the middle of this disease which is called "adubelati" until the cautery pierces the liver, and so that the cautery is applied in such a way that the patient feels pain on the side it will cause inflammation.
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	After the cure, until he is perfectly healthy.
li cure dou feu par fer	the cautery by fire with iron.
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	Another kind of disease is called "corrodens", which is nothing but a gangrene of the limb, because it corrupts the members as much as fire corrupts dry wood.
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	If you see this sickness in one who can suffer fire cautery together with fire, then take small and large calipers to the patient according to how much the sickness is; after cauterizing all parts until you reach all the corruption, and nothing remains, so that everything corrupted is burned out.
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	And then let him be for three days, and put on the patient's cauterized area a broken stick with oil until the scalding of fire is burned out, and all the corruption.
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	After the treatment of the painful kindled wound.
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	And if you see after three days that no healthy thing is born, it's good; and if not, resume the cauterizing on the one who has remained corrupted.
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	Instruct the patient that this remedy is never cured by medicine water, but that cautery of fire is a greater aid; and I have already said the remedy for medicine water in division: take the amount you need.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	Of worms that come to the joints.
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	Often at the joints due to disease, there is born a malady called "closure" according to our intention, and it is a great thing that causes great pain.
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	And the remedies for this disease are according to two ways.
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	That is to say, cautery of fire and hot water cautery.
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	Cautery of fire is that you heat the scalpel as if it were a needle, and so make one from good iron to fit into every part, and have subtle margins; after that place it at the tip of the wound, and turn your hand all around the wound until the blood begins to flow; then let it be left for three days until it starts to putrefy; and then make a poultice of fresh mallows crushed with salt, and leave the poultice on the whole wound overnight, and the lump will come out and be dislodged from its roots.
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	When treating a dislocation, apply binding to clean wounds as long as they are open.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	And if they have come out through the body, and many times occur in hands and feet, so it is suitable to apply hot cautery water: thus, take a cane of iron or wood, or a needle of copper, and set on the nail and the wound; that is, to burn warts; and put the cane so that it pricks all around, then put a little cold water on it, and hold well your hand, and press your hand turning so that the margin of the cane comes to the root of the nail, and finds the hot water deep enough to the root; and let the patient suffer for an hour with the burning of the hot water; then leave him as is, and he will come out all its roots.
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	In this manner, do one after another, until you are sure of all those that are in the body, then treat the limbs that constrict and choke.
li cure dou trembler	the treatment for trembling
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices IIII cauteres ou IV sus l’espinee dou dos, I cautere entre chescune espinee; et I cautere ou pez, et I sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When some shiver from cold, or from fever quarter, or from another cause, it is fitting that you make four cauterizations on the spine of the back, and one cautery between each spine; and one on the flesh, and one on the stomach at the olive pit; leaving them to tremble, and hastening their recovery from the cold disease.
des pustules puans	of pustulent sores or boils
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.	Never do they appear from chance on the body's baths, or pustulent sores, that come from great corrupted substances.
si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.	It is fitting to do the first one as soon as they appear that on every head of the pustule: a subtle cautery of fust of myrtle, so that the point may be grasped by fire, or from the root of aristologe long, or with the lenticular cautery.
Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	And at no time are the cauterized from the beginning when they appear, according to this method, and it cannot grow more in front, but breaks off the superfluousness that comes out, and is cured; but it is fitting that this be done after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	when the artery is cut.
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Often there are great hemorrhages of blood from the artery that is cut at the wound that comes to the surface, or at the incision of the abscess, or with the cautery of a limb, and similar things; and it is much painful to stench.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren I, ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	Instruct the patient to hasten so that you apply your index finger on the wound of the vein, and pull it out with great force until the pain is appeased under your finger; then put olive oil cautery more small and larger ones until they are all red; then take I, or great or little according to the wound and how the artery is routed, and apply the cautery on that vein where you hold your index finger, and keep it there until it does not remain.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement I autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	If the fire is extinguished when you lift your finger off the vein, and the cautery has gone out, then take it hastily, another cautery that is on fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des IIII manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not cease doing this one after the other until they (the veins) are closed off; and beware that you don't burn the nerve which is near, and that no further harm comes to the sick person; and know that when the artery cuts off the flow, it cannot be properly closed itself when the artery is large, unless by one of the four ways we have mentioned: by cautery, or by extraction since it has not been treated, or by very tightly tied with thread, or by medicines applied which have power to close the veins; and it happens that they are tied and strangled.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Who will put a stop to swelling of something tightly bound with cloth or wrapped around, or doing other similar things, if it does not relieve itself.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if this happens without any aid, and he has not oil or medicine present, then he must put his two fingers on the wound of the vein as we have said, and properly dress it until the swelling is reduced from the wound and from the vein; and he should not move him, but let him stay cold with hot water so often that he becomes very cold and stiffened, swollen, and congested; and do these things in front to what he needs of cauteries and medicines.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	This begins the second book on treatments for wounds.
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	As we have said in the first chapter all diseases, whether it is necessary to cautery with fire or with medicine around, and ointments, causes, pus, and forms of cauteries; and I put this chapter from his head down to the joints, and I will go through this same way for that which one finds more easily.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And thus as I begin this, it is necessary, dear son, that you learn that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first cautery, and therefore you must be more careful.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	And I warn you that you must not be foolish.
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	For many kinds of people come in for treatments.
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	But those who come from people who have suffered so greatly from their illness that they die quickly due to the severity of their sickness, and the great power of their evil, and for these one must have fear.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse.	And when it comes to you who does so, and says: "Wait, I am cured"; and the sickness is hard-hearted.
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	It is not for your own benefit that you allow those who come to you and have this manner to do so, but rather put greater care in your honor than in your covetousness, and be neither idle nor foolish about what you are certain of and about which you have taken possession; and use pronostication and indication in the treatment of your sick patients to see if salvation is converted; for that will help you to gain a good reputation, glory, and memory of praise.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Three dear children, Our Lords entrust to you good understanding and righteousness, and if you wish to aspire from the holy inspiration of His hand, Amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Instructed you in this chapter by division into chapters, according to what is before or after the chapters of cauteries, which I have devised for you from the head to the toe, because it is easier to find what you will need.
dou chief plein d’aigue	Fill a cloth with water.
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	It is often the case that this illness comes from time to time in children at birth, and when the baby holds it too tightly around the head of the child, and no explanation is known for it.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I have never seen this illness except in children, and for all those who I have seen it has been the cause of death, and therefore it seems to me that it would be good to take out the work in parts.
Et je vis I enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com II nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	In the child because the shoulder joint is full of water, and the head engorges each day so much that it cannot bear; and he believed so much in the moisture that he was dead, and this moisture is assembled under the bone above the suture, between the cheek and the bone; and the wound is like that if the moisture is between the cheek and the bone, and the abscess is small, that you cut open the head with a large incision; and be so long as II of us, until the moisture runs out; and see there the shape of the spatula:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai II fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is deeper and the abscess is larger, then you will make two incisions in the shape of a cross, according to this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief III fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the moisture is under the bone, and you see the signs that you see the edges of the head opening up on both sides, and the water starts to flow when you press with your hand into it, and it does not return: then it is suitable to make three incisions in the head according to this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	And after the incision, remove all moisture completely.
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	After holding the incision closed with bandages and powder, and applying wine and oil, let it be so for five days; then open it, and treat the wound by stitches and ointments, and let the head dry out, and feed the patient dried meat until the member is comforted and healed.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another way of incision is to look at or open the size of the abscess and the assembly of the water; for it is sometimes before, sometimes behind, sometimes on the right side, and sometimes on the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	Measure then according to the size of the abscess, and the fulfillment of the water, and make the cut as you have the power; and beware that you do not cover the artery; and if a drop of blood flows, so that the patient dies from the accumulation of blood and the evacuation of moisture.
de reume	of the reume
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les II arteres.	When any disease called "catarre" occurs in the eyes or is very painful, and the disease has been present for a long time, and medicine does not provide relief, then the last resort is to use the cautery with what we cut off both the two arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	It is therefore necessary that when you cover the eyes, the patient makes a face towards his head; after he strokes it with a rough cloth until the arteries appear, then remove the mucus from his neck using a whole cloth; then look where the vein swells, and the veins of both are after the ears, and they take some time to recover; then sign the swelling with ink; then cut one and the other of a well-made spatumile for two parts, until the vein reaches just above the bone, and so it is done by the width of his forehead.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com II dois au traver.	And if you see, pour out the spatula on below the artery and cut above it as well, in cutting just like that across.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is cut, so it does not continue to bleed indefinitely.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de III dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est VI c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins, selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And if the artery does not open to feel, it is advised that you measure the space of three times, then cut deeper and go into the bone; because what needs to be put into the wound should be six or a little more, according to how much the patient can bear, and the replenishment of the artery; then look at the wound: if the point of the bone is still on top of the spot where you sewed it, then cut that again since it does not seem to have been healed, then strain the wound and tie it, and provide rest until it is healed.
de emigrainne	Let goes of
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When the old inflammation comes, and coughing is good, due to moistors of tears and heat in the temples and an ancient sore and similar things, and he is treated with various medical cures and medicine, but it does not profit him, so we extract the arteries from the temples and the cauterized areas, just as we have told.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And the way of extracting them is that the patients pull their hair back from their temples, and listen to the artery opening in the temple, because it opens well with its pulsing, and is not repaid quickly as in some people who are too cold; and if it is repaid, then he pulls his patient’s neck with certain cloths, then rubs the skin with a harsh cloth, and raises the skin of someone hot water until the artery appears manifestly; then take the spatula of that shape:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des II chiés.	Instruct the patient to scorch the skin lightly until you see the artery, then take it up towards the head with pincers, and pull out well all the threads that are below these parts; and if the artery is subtle, then twist at the point of the needle, and cut off this part according to the quantity of two fingers.
Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	But if she is not cut, let her go without pain or discomfort in any way.
Et trai dou sanc des VI c/, jusc’a III; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en II leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les II liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And take out the blood from six cubits, just as three; and if the artery is large, it is fitting that you tie it with two levers of a strong double thread of silk, so that no discharge occurs before the wound has healed, and the blood appears in a steady flow; then cut the surplus tissue between the two levers at this hour itself, and if you see, then cauterize with the cautery knife just as far into the bone until the joints are cut; and it is the most effective work, if the patient does not have fever and he has a hot complexion.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For the fire cautery, is aid to finish the moistures: because of this it gives more aid to the moistures.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de II pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	Where it is necessary to extract arteries, fill the vein with old cotton and put well-made tamps on top; and when you remove them, if they are cured with dry medicines that make charcoal, and tamps, until they are healthy again; and if without any injury to the artery as much as you do work, then hasten to cover with cautery, or use a leaden vessel and strain it in your hand so that the blood is not spilled; and if you don't have this present, put on the vein your must (or plug), so that they are not frozen, and draw the vein with cold water until it congeals, and straining it as necessary; and what is moist and lighter to extract from the artery is to cauterize the vein of this cautery with two parts, but the parts be well-spaced to keep its heat longer.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	When the signs are too dense, they hold less heat.
Et doit avoir entre les II coutelz I doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les II leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en II leus; et soient esloigniet entre les II chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And the two incisions should be large enough that one needs a thick iron rod, and then when you have cut off the two ends, cut hot metal along them so it comes to meet at the bone, and strike the vein in two; and let them be separated between the two incisions because there is no soldering of this cautery all over; and this is the form of cautery:
des larmes	of tears.
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When the tears of the eyes are flowing onto veins that are on the forehead near the top of the head, and it does not benefit from any medicine that we make, and you see the face of the sick person become flushed, and feel or sense a dullness in front of the eyes like numbness; and if the hairs of the eyebrows are wet and moist so that the eyebrow skin is burnt, and the skin is scalded by the heat of the tears, then it may be necessary for this treatment.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins; et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	And they called the ancient 'cure contused', and you should repeat to the sick person who has this disease the hairs on their face; then you do III cuts or evenly according to the length of the front; and one of the cuts is as II do it all towards the chin in the direction where a pain is, and the other II are as II cost them by above the papers, and be careful not to cut the arteries that are at II these costs by above the papers; and keep your hand away from continuing II mandibules, and each wound should have III fingers through it; and take an sponge piece with a lot of cloths to absorb the blood, then pour the good spatumile in II parts of this is its shape:
