des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les II fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	From the cut that is made towards the temple right up to the second cut; and burn all the wound that is between II cuts, to the extent of lou syfac which is above the bone, then make another part from the lower incision right up to the other second cut, and then pull out this spatumile.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	If you prick with the instrument called "cutting needle", and it is sharp from one side, and soft from the other, it's not sharp, and this is the shape:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	And cut the bone towards the raw flesh to the spot, and the soft part towards the bone, and prick it until it comes to the middle split.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And cut off the vessels that come out from the head to the eyes until the incision is continuous just as far as the spot where it opens; then make another cut in the middle split just as far as the other division; and then extract the blood evenly, and press out the flesh caught; then put a tent of clean cotton into each split, and cover with moist cloths of wine and oil and wax; and keep away any pus from coming out; on the third day dislocate the bandage, and apply great quantities of watered-down plant juice; then administer the Basilicon ointment with olive oil, and other cures for wounds, until he is healed.
dou reume des eulz	Do not move the eyes
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When any vein is swollen by habit and custom, and you see the eyes clouded and small, and weakened the sight, and the papers burn; and the hairs fall out, and pain is felt in the head, and the patient coughs; then observe by these accidents that those materials and this swelling come from many veins, and the mother's cure if it is so.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And instruct the patient to cover their forehead, then make a deep cut on both sides of the forehead and another one less wide near.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And begin from the wound of the left temple to the right temple, and make the incision just up to the bone; and keep your hand away from the nerve endings on either side of the temples that move with pain; when the bone is exposed, sooth the bleeding with a sponge; then sew between the two lips of the wound and apply cotton wool and linen threads; then wrap dressings moist in wine and oil, and beware of infected pus; when it is healed, if you massage the bone until it starts to swell, then cure with remedies that draw out the swelling.
En teil maniere: pren II parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine IIII parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In this manner: take two parts of poppy flower and four parts of colocynth, and make it infuse; and administer it in these wounds to prevent pain for all.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the bursting of the ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des IIII choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	All that comes out of the ears is one of four things: grain, animal matter, stone from a mine, or similar thing like metal; or seed, such as thistles, fennel, etc., or something flowing out like water and pus, and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When it comes out of the ear stone or some other kind of thing that does not fit into the ear, nor grows in the ear, if you put the ear to the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus.	If you see the stone, then distill a little violet oil or sesame oil, and perform extraction; and let it be ejected by condensation, and wipe the nostrils when expelling comes, and put pieces of cloth or wool into the ear, and put the ear up on top.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	Often by this cure comes forth blood; and if it does not come forth, take out the extraction with subtle fingers, because in this there is form:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it jumps with the fingers, that is good; if not, take out the extraction on an onion-like swelling with a small double fold; and if it does not jump by this, make a candle of flax and pour the chief into the candle or ear canal very tightly, so that the vein cannot enter through the candle with wax; then pull forth the form, because often comes forth as we have said; and if it does not come forth in any way, grab with glue because you take out the ears, and put on some device that has a point for this purpose, and put a little cotton inside; then press the glue above the stone or whatever it is, and pull forth.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if she will not heed all that we have said, then hasten to pierce the ear so that it bursts open as an abscess does, and spasm; and the manner of the piercing is such that you first make the patient whole again of the head, and extract the blood according to its virtue, then place the patient between your hands and turn the ear upwards, and make a small opening in the root of the ear at the fat or what depends on it; and make the opening as big as a moon, until you reach the bone, then pierce according to your power, and suck hastily into your mouth; and the cure will last as long as he is whole.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre I spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it is pus and it swells, administer the extraction; and if it will not come out, administer a slow-seeping poultice according to this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	and let him make an incision of that flesh.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	But do not cut me so when you think that the flesh is moist from the moisture of the ear, until you have made many pieces; then pull it out with fine fingers and a spoon, as we have said, so that the extraction may be eased.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	In water then what is poured into the ear should be used with sterility of clothes first, and fill the ear with old cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And it may also fall on that same ear or when water is used.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	If she falls through because of this, it's good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	If that's not the case, so he pricks many pieces according to how long your nose should be and soft, and takes one of his fingers in the ear, and pushes on the other side, and sets fire to a piece above the bone in the ear; and does not cease to prick this joint and bone until the water has all fallen out, and so it falls out entirely; and if you see, prick the joint again, and stick one of his fingers into the ear, and the other takes fire from the other side, until the skin is burned red; then do another piece of joints as long as the water has fallen out, just as we have said in the bone.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the extraction of a lump, if it is small like a pus or similar thing, cure as we have said in division; but if it is large that you can feel, then extract with pincers; and this is the lightest thing to remove which is in the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	In the extraction of worms, mark the ears when you cure, just as we have said in division and in treating distillations; if the cure does not help, then it is fitting that you look at the ear in the sun: if no worms appear, take out with fine pincers; and if they do not appear, take out a ring because this is the shape.
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And sometimes narrow beneath, and wide above.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	And let the most subtle thread in the ear according to the quantity of the patient's suffering; then form all the way around the ring. Do this often until all the worms are extracted.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	Instruct the patient to let them prick if they wish, so put a cotton thread inside as I said in the pier; and if they do not come out like we have said, administer dilutions as the ancients have proven in the operation of worms, and you will find or treat with dilutions; and if you distill your oils and medicines into the ear with this instrument, because it is that form which you see:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a I petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a I estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren I raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations I poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And whether it is of silver or of iron, put inside at the little holes, and above on the distilling, and to press into the distillation with the well-made instrument of iron, for if you see a razor and pass it through the cotton in anticipation of the point, then pour your oil or your juice, and what you see of your medicines in the canal, and the cotton be in the ear; then put the razor inside all the cotton, and press your hand temperately until the oil is distilled or just out of the ear; and let the patient feel it inside, and that the distillations should be heated to some extent like when they are done in the ear, and be careful that they are not too cold, for the medicine will not be good.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	When the eustachian tube is burst.
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born who does not have some defect in the ears; and this same thing happens to adults by bursting of a wound or a splinter inside the ear, and these ruptures come from deep into the ear, unless one can see it; and sometimes there is such a big hole that it's hard to look at; and sometimes the hole is small, and you can't see much.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	This one that comes deep into the ear, if you can't see it, is due to pain in various conditions, and when you look inside, you should put the patient's ear to the sun; and look: if you see a visible opilation (i.e. inflammation or redness), then this is the shape:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And if you prick and cut all over the face, in front and back of every spot, so that it does not strike the ear; if the operation is on a nose or bone of the ear, then take care if you have fine points, and carefully cut so that those bones are completely hollowed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the operation is deep inside the ear, take a fine razor light and carefully shave it, then put on the bone of the ear.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	If you feel that there is an operation in the ear where the patient feels severe pain in the ear, carefully pierce, and keep from spoiling the nerves of the ear; then put into the ear a tent according to the width of a perforated drum, and a poultice in the Egyptian manner.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Instruct the patient to do nothing until the wound is healed, or you take a poultice made from lard and rosewater, and powder with vitriol on top of it; if you see the ear swell, then cover yourself so that you treat the poultice and move another one moistened in cress oil and wax, until the swelling goes away; then attend to the patient until he is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if the swelling returns, then soak an sponge in cold water and apply it to the ear, and use other treatments that reduce the swelling of blood, which are for treating bleedings.
de la char des papieres	of charcoal from paper
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	Place a piece of charcoal on the eyelids when they are moist and dry again, if it is needed to spread them with tongs and tweezers, and cut off one of its roots with a spatula; then put powder made from vitriol on top.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	If the fire cautery is not cut off, then the cautery will burn the fine lens, and after the incision it will be painful to move; and many times are healed, but no part remains of its roots; and when those roots are burned by fire, they do not return.
de la gresle	Of the gallows.
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Many times come worms in paper under the eyelids which seem like gall on their shape and hardness, and because of that this sickness is called "grandine", and it is an assembly of thick moisture above and below; the workmen are such: take care if the grandine moves from one side and the other, and it's a light thing to know; do then with a broad knife, then scrape off lightly from each part lightly, then take it with pincers, and cut.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	If you cannot cover the wound with skin piercing slightly on the paper, do not grieve the patient; and if the fissure is large, assemble it with a seam, and cure until it is healed; and if it is small, do not make any force, for the ointments will restore it immediately and relieve pain.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the smallpox is coming down into the ear canal towards the upper part, pierce and press paper from above, and let the smallpox spread on pincers, and cut and squeeze from both sides; and if the paper is pulled away by the incision, it will not grieve; and when the smallpox is cut, clean the oily salt water, and cure the patient until he is healed, relieving pain.
de la graisse des eulz	From the fat of the eyes.
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	This is a fat that is woven in mesh of paper threads, and this happens to children who have no one to care for them. It causes great pain to their eyes, and they come with catharres (diarrhea) in the mornings, and cannot see into the light of the sun because the tears are running out of their eyes; and because of this they lie down on their faces afterwards, and sleep under their noses, and have moist paper above their eyebrows that the inflammation makes and the appearance has been covered with the exinach which opens in the oil.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press on it with your two hands and feel the exinach inside.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren I drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the method of opening is that the sick person places his head on your healthy one; and then take a linen cloth, and prepare a tent in the shape of a circle according to the quantity of exinach contained in each part, and place it thereupon; and press with your two hands from one side and the other, so that the exinach is assembled within the circle; and then make an incision at the midpoint of the moist area up to the spot where you cut into a vein; and let the skin be sewn in such a way that it does not become large like the wound you made on the healthy vein; and make the leather according to your will until you reach the exinach; and in further arrangements, comes out of the incision a piece of white grease.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Take out then as much cloth gauze as possible between your two arms at once and turn your hand to right and left so it is spread; and keep in mind that you should not add more to the wound than necessary, lest you come to the point where the whole shoulder is raw until the oil is gone.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the extraction does not open up at the beginning of the wound, then cut slightly on one side of the wound so it appears; then cut as we have said, then bind with cloth easily and wetly, and put the limb on, and tie with bandages.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And if some such men who break silken thread and place it to corrupt that moisture which is left.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then the cure until he is cured.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it comes to the artery hot, then the physician should apply ointment soothing until he is healed.
des poilz des papieres	of hairs from paper
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc IIII manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When hairs of paper are born and are other than their nature, and have become diseased, they cause the eyes to be injured, and bring about various kinds of diseases such as tearing and softening of the eyes, and the presence of larmes (likely meaning "blemishes" or "spots") and albugine (likely meaning "ecchymosis" or bruising), until it is the cause of the destruction of the eyes; and a cure is done in four manners: either by cautery with fire together, or by medicinal water according to what is before the chapter on cautery, and they are made either by incision and sewing or by caning, as I will say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai I fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai I fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	It is necessary that you put the head of the patient on your table, then turn the paper of oil at your left hand; if it is turned, it's good; if not, let him prick with an arrow through all his hair; and take the thread from above at whatever distance from these hairs, and turn it up to the razor; then make in the part under the paper, near the hairs gathered, all around the circumference of the scab, from the large laceration just to the small one; then pull out the thread, and put over the paper a small tent of cotton and lace, then sign on the paper an image like that of mirte, and whatever is fitting according to what you see lifting the paper which is devised for all.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	Et if to anyone with a serious matter you copy a great quantity of the paper according to what the paper is moistened; then make on all the surrounding area up to two lines that you have signed, and start from great sharpness at small; and let it be one of the cuts near the natural hairs in the size of a root, then pour it into one of the two angles where there is warmth; then scrape it all away; then bring together the two lips with an sewing needle to one fine thread of flax, and clean the wound, and make it dry on both ears at all sorts of things stuck, if you have seen this done before; and if not, do not bother, then leave the sewing and the threads just for three days or four; then treat the wound with dried and tied things, because the paper comes to life at the moment of the wound and the assembly of it, but the sewing is tough (as the ancients have said), and this is a wrong doing with fear; and if you do it in another way: and is that you take the paper of a figure which is just as like the handle of myrtle, as we have counted, at three times according to the shape which is here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	Then cut off that which overhangs equally, according to its shape, because.
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And if you have no power to hold the tongs, and that thing is not even, take a needle or if it has a thread, and tie it around the figure; and tie the other thread on the larger seam, and the smaller thread on the one, and assemble between your two hands the threads equally; then lift your hand equally, and cover all the skin where you have stitched, as we have counted, then assemble the two lips of the wound by suture, and cure until it is healed; and if an abscess comes to your incision, sooth it with cerote and similar ointment soothing; and sometimes happens that the hair on the scalp are changed: if you must use what we have said about cutting; but the stitching in one and another is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The cure of the fractures is as follows: and it is that you convert the paper and the flesh inside according to what I said, and then do II caines by art, and II subtle ligatures also long as the paper and the wide stretch of the spatulate tool are; and cut off II fingers of II parts where you hold the strings; then assemble one and the other subtly above that which lies under the paper of the oil, and strain the two caines from the two parts form; and leave it like so for some days, and the skin that is tightened will wither, numb, and prick, until it falls off by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it is late, if you cut with one hand a strong force, then the cure until he is sane; and when the wound is healed, and the paper is lifted, and the pain will not come again to the hair; and this is the form of the two caines that you make according to this figure, and according to this quantity of length and width:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	Instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo II jors ou III, tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	Instruct the one who chases to treat and let the hairs grow if they do not come forth with it; then chase after it under the skin all the way down until it comes out at the wound, so that you see it by the vision of oil; then chase and the thread, and close the oil and leave it closed for 2 or 3 days or more, until the hair grows in its place and falls out with the char on top; if the hairs are small, accompany one long hair from the cheekbones nature, and raise them along with that one, until they become long and then lift.
de la porriture de l’oil	of the oil's spoilage
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	When this disease which is called "aleacrati" or the spoilage comes into the oil, it occurs in two ways: one natural and the other unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And happens by sudden wound, or incision, or cautery, and similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	And the method of opening it is that you cut through the sore, and open the lips, and put linen tents inside, and tie so long as they are healing; and it is not advisable to use in the treatment of it only things that dry and constrict.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	For if you do this, the disease will return worse than before; but to overcome it with softening things, like fenugreek; and boiled rose water or ale, and seed of flax, are cooked; and ointments of melted diaquilon are applied in any of the oils, and a tent is wrapped up, and the cure of this.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasures of your cure are that you take care not to melt it again in the same form as it was before; and this work which we have mentioned is only a similar cause of this disease, which returns in the same form as it was before.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	Of the flesh which comes from the oil
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This sickness that is below and truly is called "axacrati", and it is natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	The accident comes from wounds and cuts and cautery and similar things; and the vein in the work is such that you prick an arrow, because it has two threads, and the needle pierces into the flesh, and you make it pierce to the left shoulder so much that the thread comes out through two joints of the flesh; then take the flesh up to the top with all the needle, and cut off one spatumile wide.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the skin of the paper returns to its place as it should, that's good; but if not, then take a razor and put it in the wound, turn the paper, and make two cuts on one side inside the paper; and so that the joints of the two cuts meet at the angles of the incision you made, and that when they are assembled, the figure will be like the figure of the letter "I griesche"; then take away that flesh according to the quantity that its sides are below from the paper, and then join the two parts together with the threads of a linen thread; then give the cure for what we have said about the medicines softening, and cauterizing, until he is cured.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les II leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	Et if the sickness comes from cutting or sewing or cautery, it is fitting that you cut an open plain wound below the hairs of the paper skin, and according to what has been said; then cut between the two fingers of a tent, as I have said; and must one do the work according to the form of the illness, for it is much diverse in form, and the wise masters make a machine from all possible means by which he makes the figure return to its natural shape; and the sick themselves, according to what they need treatment and instruments for more cases.
dou soudement de la papiere	Suddenly from the paper
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	So that the paper above is stuck with oil white and cannot move or do its natural work, if it so happens then you should put the point of a razor under the paper, and raise it up; and the cutting is done according to the lines, until you copy what is correct on the stylus subtle, which should not be too rough nor too sharp, so that the patient cannot suffer from the stylus being too rough or bleeding oil; and let your incision, where you scrape off that assembly, gently, so that the paper comes back according to its natural form; and it is cured of that entire assembly, and never happens again with astringent oil salted, and lye brought in fresh water, and vinegar; then put between the paper and the oil a linen tent, and put on the oil wool moist with lard; and after three days use the lye and other quick remedies until it is cured.
de l’ungle de l’oil	From the unglet of the oil
Saiches que li ungle est selonc II manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a I dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	There are two kinds of joints: one is nervous and appears like a thick fur, and the other is not nervous but resembles a white frost congealed, when touched with iron and treated with pan, it does not bleed; and both kinds seem to approach the great vein, and slowly increase until they cover the whole view and all light and the movement of the oil.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met I poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et I fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the method of incision is that the patient places his head on your clean cloth, then closes his eyes; and lifts the paper to his hand, then cuts the joint as stitches of small double sewing, and stretches it upwards; then takes a needle, and puts in horse, or calf, or ox hair, and strong thread; and doubles the point of the needle slightly and pierces into the joint, and fills with all the needle, and ties the joint with a thread and stretches it upwards, and scrapes off at the whole length of the skin on the cost of the joint that follows the vein and the silk to the hair just to the head, then chops away the remaining in the root of the vein up to the fine and small forces, and leaves the natural color of the vein, if no blood comes from it; and sometimes stretches only the joint onto a lump, and on thread, as we said; then scrapes off with all the fine and smooth spatumile of why this is like.
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	Instruct the patient to keep the scab from touching the raw flesh and let it break, and do not perceive the purpleness; and after the incision anoint with oil a little bit of crushed silk, and make a poultice on the neck, and leave it until the other day; then the cure should treat as much as is necessary so that he may be healed.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the nail is not stiff and you cannot pierce it with the needle, and the unguent cannot enter, this sort of swollen nail is often cured by medicines; and it will grow as I have described in division, and if you see it covered, apply oil to the patient, and take the scab lightly according to this form.
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And remove the swollen nail carefully, and if you see that it is not softening at all and the infection advances, then distill from your mouth into oil a poultice made of crushed lead and red lead, and apply it to the neck; leave the oil until the next day; then continue with another operation according to this same method until it is entirely hollowed out.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If there is no inconvenience to you in the oil, as with foot pus, then apply the poultice and treat the boil until it is healed; and then resume work on it as before, until it is healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the skin is marred by great inflammation in the oil due to a swelling, if one pricks at an abscess and not too much, that no blood flows; then dilute red oil in the oil, which is made from litharge.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	from the charcoal that is born under the eyelid
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre; et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	But if the eyes of some men never produce any red charcoal, and cover the eyelid and restrain under paper towels and bandages away from it, and seem like a rose of balsam; and wounds are such that patients place their head on your healthy side, then work on the eyes, and apply all that charcoal has suitable unguents to it, and support it with force; then make the first incision, and continue cutting as long as the raser is near the end, and be careful not to bleed the oil at the wound; and perform the incision of spatumile, just as we have said about the incision of the ulcer, and with small forces so that one can open the swell; just like the form after this chapter shows. And when the incision is completed and all the charcoal has been removed, apply the oil of silk broken or distill red collier and similar corrosive medicines, and place cotton on the oil with linen wool, if it will be secure to have an abscess; and if nothing remains, and the swelling does not go away, then leave the oil and treat the abscess with soothing medications for abscesses. Then return to your work until it is healed, and do so as I have said that charcoal should be applied in this manner.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	But it is necessary that you balance the treatment of each case with a gentle touch in both the natural way and the accidental way, in work with iron; and do not put your hand in any of these works until you see if this member is suffering from that injury.
des voines des eulz	of the eyelids
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	They are red veins that cover the flesh, and they take away their work and weaken the flesh every day.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	It is then the duty of the first thing you observe that there are veins, in what state they are, whether swollen or not, and if there is no other disease than swelling; therefore, the coil in this manner: instruct the patient to put his head on a clean surface, then suspend those veins as long as possible according to your wisdom, and let the subtle ones double up in that form:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en I cors selonc ceste forme:	And let them be two times one by degree in the body according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	Then cut as gently as possible those veins, and apply the blood hour after another, until you see remove the veins from the oil; and guard that you do not strike the oil with the points of the lancets, and perform this work at hour of noon in front of the sun, and be very fervent in your work so that you only cut those veins; and when you have done this, if you distill oil colored green and red to corrupt what remains on the liver.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you do not have power to cut all that in that hour, then apply a poultice on the oil with soothing things to ease the pain of the eyes, and let it be for some days until the pains are eased and make sure there is an abscess hot, then resume according to this manner until they are healed.
de la fistule de l’oil	of the armpit abscess
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	The wound which they name "arissati" fistule: when you treat it with cautery and medicine hot according to what I have said, and it is not healed, then there is infection in it that you pierce above the abscess, where it must die, and remove all the moisture that is in it, until the bones are uncovered.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a I chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bones are uncovered, and you see the corruption and blackness, if the abscess has the same form; and it is called "aspre chief", and make it from fire on the cheek, as it was in this form: point it out like a knife just like it is in the present condition:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And place on the bone of the corrupted part, then turn it between your two hands, and press your hand a little so that you know when this corruption is reduced; and do this once, then restore to its normal form with medicinal exorcisms.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the joint is swollen and it inflames, and the body of the bowel is swollen, and remains like that for 40 days, and does not heal, and no infection comes, then know that he is healthy; but if this is not the case, if there is no other cure than to bring back the fistula to the perforated part according to this shape: and it is so that you uncover the bone the second time by iron, with medicines sharp, and when it heals uncovered like this, take a bow of three points, and the fist be softened just above the head as you see here.
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	Then put the bow on top of the bone, and keep your hand away from the wound for a little while, then turn to the whole forest until it pierces the bone and you feel the patient's pain as he comes in with his hand on his nose; and when he swallows and hardens the joint, then direct the matter onto the nose; this is a lighter thing for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	From the issue of oil
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil I liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en IIII, et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eyes are fully opened and do not come out or become lessened, if it is necessary to cut off the patient; then apply, now the remedy, now put on ointments with oil, made of ice and aloe and incense and sarcocolle, and then strain the oil, and anoint on a plaster with bands and cloths; and the method of the cloths is that you take cloths soft enough, and double each one in four, and then put one over another according to the quantity the eyes have need of; then strain by the braid of a strong band, and reapply the ointments to suck; now remove the ointment and let the oil be strained day and night, and if it is bound with thread, so that you tie it much; then remove the thread after the day and the night, and if you see the oil repairing, this is good; if not; then reapply the plaster and the cloths and the ointment and the suckers until they are well.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	The downfall of the eel-like shape
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When the veil of the eel-like shape comes undone, and opens up, and comes out through the paper as if from a grain of resin, it is truly astonishing to see; therefore if you look at it carefully, the wounds are such that you need to insert an awl into the root of the part under the jawbone to one side of this position, then insert another awl where there is the double thread from the inner corner; and pierce it, and leave the first awl according to its disposition; then cut off the long thread and tie a portion of the vein around it, and bind it well, then pull out the awl and apply oil with linen soaked in more oil of dates; and let it remain until the threads contract with the vein, and treat the oil on soothing things so that the wound is healed; and sometimes the wound is bound by the vein each part in a circle of cloth, until it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eyes do great appearance, so you should perceive in the spot below subtle which is coming from the oil, and chase the moisture that stains and down descends the eyes, and enter as soon as possible; then extract them until they are healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	from the oil in the bowel
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	This illness called "alcunnati" is only in the bowel which is assembled in oil, appearing like flowing water but it's not really water; and the way of its appearance is that you should seat the patient on a special seated bed straight, then take his head between your two hands of II parts, and let him move until you see the bowel coming up to your eyes; then fix it, and don't let it descend or break loose the light, and observe the patient's things as they usually do; if it doesn't descend below, know that it's water, and if the bowel's movement isn't assembled like we said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If you sit the patient between your hands, then take the spatula and put it up to the cornea with the continuity of the conjunctive with the cornea and the crown, until the bow is; and when it has come out, distill into warm oil mixed with melted honey or boiling fenugreek, or milk, then be cured with another cure until they are healed.
des aigues de l’oil	of the oil
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	We have seen the likeness of water in division, and that which is needed to pierce; if we operate according to health.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	It is necessary to sit the patient between your hands crossed, with the light of fire by the sun, and tie a strong oil-based bandage; then put a piece of the oil-soaked paper in your left hand if their eyes are on the left, or in your right hand if they are on the right. Then take the instrument called "almagda" in your right hand if their eyes are on the left, or in your left hand if they are on the right; then put the point of the instrument near the crown by the thickness of a thread into that thin layer of oil at the inner side of the membrane; then pour the "almagda" instrument virtuously and turn your hand until it pierces into the oil's thin layer, and feel when "almagda" comes to the empty space; and it is necessary that the measure of "almagda"'s passage be equal to the full length of the span which is from the apple's pit to the end of the nail's edge; and this is the crown of the oil; if you see the bone in that paper by the clarity of the cornea, then put the instrument just next to it or into the aching part, and press with another passage after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	If the water is flowing now, then he sees the patient before him and the instrument in his hand.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	After resting for a little while, and the water starts flowing again, put the force with the instrument, and when it is stuck and does not rise, gently pull out everything lightly in rotating your hand a little bit; then put back into the oil a small piece of linen gauze, and clean that within.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then put by force the oil into a cloth or linen soaked in olive oil and an abundance of rue, and bind with clean oil.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	And so, as for those of our time, let us put on a poultice with bruised comfrey and an abundance of rue.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the milk cannot enter into the oil due to its hardness, because there are several men who have hard eyelids, you must take the instrument called "alberit", so that it is in the correct form:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And therefore pierce the conjunctive alone, and do not move too far forward, but make it subtle, then put in milk, as we have said; and when you complete the work, the doctor attending comes along, because he sleeps on his back in the dark room; and be careful of all movements, and give light viands, and do not move your head or right arm or left arm, and be bound according to its disposition for three days a day; then release it in that same dark room, and examine his sight, and make him see some things, and then set the bandage for five days; and it is not advisable to do this in the house of cure now or after the incision, but it is necessary to alleviate it, because the water rises quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	In case of an abscessed limb, instruct the patient to let it be opened on the seventh day, and the advice of one who has soothed an abscess; and when it is appeased, then release the eye and put on its face, a woolen cloth for covering each day, and stay in that dark house.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	And then they come from the house little by little, and it converts into his case; and one learns that no disciples should intervene in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And one came to us who was from the East, who said that in some other land people do alchemy, with which they make water, but I never saw it or heard of it in any book of the ancients; and by chance, this may be a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the signs of the forms of alum, because those who do not know them see them as if they were impure. And so be cautious:
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	And let the head of this same subtlety be cut off at an angle of three.
de la char sor le neis	with charcoal on the nails.
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	Never has charcoal grown on the nails in diverse forms, so that some seem like scorpions from the size; and when it is of such kind that it is studded with foreign material and colored flesh, and then with soft-colored bone.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	In such case, of the soft charcoal, which is not studded with anything, it is necessary that you sit the patient between your hands against the sun; and open their nostrils, and let fall upon those chars, the fumes; because, as long as you can sustain them to the subtle powder good at the spot, until you know that all the charcoal has fallen out.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	In case some thing remains that cannot be covered, if you apply all the subtle instruments lightly, so it does not stay anywhere; and if there is no swelling or abscess, cut the swelling as needed; and if it's a malignant abscess, hasten and cauterize until the blood stops flowing and the bones are exposed completely, then remove it quickly.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If there is no discharge and moisture comes just to the palate, it is considered a sign of healing; and if moisture does not come when needed, it is considered that there is a bone fracture in the above place, where the instruments do not come for cutting: then it is convenient to put a thread of linen in it, and tie it securely with fingers, and put some space between each other so much as to allow; and apply the sick person's head with the thread to the wound powerfully, until it comes through into the mouth; and this is an easy thing for him who wants to do it; then hold the chief that comes by the thread in one hand, and the chief that comes by the mouth in the other hand, and feel one after the other as we are with the thread.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	Instruct the patient so that you know the truth about the flesh, then take care of the child, clean the wound, and pour Egyptian oil into the wound, and put it straight onto the skin as before; do this for three days or more, until the ointments corrode everything remaining of the flesh; and then apply a bandage made from linen on no other day than necessary until it is healed, and if he needs dried medicines, use them; this is the form of the instrument to purify the head, because we distill oil and medicines in the linen:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And if it is made of silver or lead, resembling a lamp with an overhanging handle, like a lantern, and so conducted; and if you see one, make a lantern-like bandage, and let the instruments be open to purify the head; and have one hand on the head to hold it when the oil or any liquid is heated.
de la char sor le neis	Of the charcoal from the nose
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	The disease named "telul" often arises from the nose of a child and grows into large abscesses until it becomes visible; therefore, you must apply a poultice to the beginning, and burn hot medicine on it; and if it is delayed for too long so that it becomes large, then be cautious with it if it is hard and of bad smell, from dung color, and poor flesh: do not touch it with iron because this is an enchanted abscess, for once you cut it, great evil will come to the patient; and if the abscess is soft and of foul smell, but you see that it can be covered, then take away the poultice and apply it again with fear, and treat the abscess with dried things and binding.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	When the nails are struck and pounded
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Saying that when some solution comes from one of these old cartilages, it benefits little, whether in men or women.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is therefore necessary to examine this carefully if the wound is fresh all through with its blood; and then add two stitches to it, and treat him until he heals; and if the lips are cut off one side and the other, it is advisable that you burn all the parts of his skin where they are damaged until they heal, then reassemble the two lips to a suture, and tie them, and powder with powdered dragon's blood and incense, and apply a piece of emplaster of strong or another plastering compound, and let him rest until he begins to cough up it, then treat him with ointment until he heals.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The way of sewing is that you assemble the sutures: either with needles, as we have said in sewing around the belly; or with thread, as I told you.
des apostemes des levres	of abscesses of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.
