With the help of the hands it goes into the lips abscess, similar to grains of sand, small and larger; therefore you must return the lips, and cut each one open, and take out with tweezers and strike in each part; then apply liquid after the incision with vitriol broth, until the abscess is drained; and then clean and treat the wound with dry things until it is sane.
de la char des gencives	of the gums' flesh
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Here is the translation:
des sordens	of wounds
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	There are no cases where the roots of teeth are gathered at the top of the gums inside the mouth between the teeth, with rough and unpleasant scars; and there are no cases where a black and yellow tooth and root come out, until corruption reaches the gum, and they become foul. It is advisable to seat the patient in your hands, so that their joints remain still, and remove the roots or scars whenever you see them, until nothing remains; and thus perform blackening and greenish tinting, and jaundice, and other treatments, until they are clean. If one thinks that it is at the root of a tooth, this is good; if not, if it recurs on the second day and the third day, until you have removed all of them; and know that teeth need various forms of instruments to remove them, according to what the work shows, because the razor used for cleaning teeth has different forms than the one used between the teeth. These forms and others should be prepared with you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when you cure the tooth of its pain that you wait as long as you can before taking it out, because this should not be done slowly; for it is a very high substance just made hence and therefore we have no excuse for delay.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Therefore when the patient is constrained to take it out, it is necessary that you be certain about the soundness of the tooth.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Often the patient suffers pain and thinks it is a tooth that needs to be extracted; so you should treat the good tooth instead. And if this does not alleviate the pain for him, watch out in case the evil one is inside because we have never wanted to do this before with those doctors; and when you are certain about the soundness of the tooth, it is necessary to scorch around the tooth all the way to its end, using a strong instrument to prevent the gums from becoming inflamed in all directions. Then pull out your two fingers or use pincers very subtle at first, taking them apart until they are well cleaned, and then firm up the pincers; and hold the patient's tooth between your palms, with his teeth inside, so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After extracting the tooth directly towards the break, and if it doesn't fall out, take any of these instruments and put them inside each part lightly, and move it as you have done first.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And if the tooth is perceived and extracted, it is fitting that you fill the space with cloth, where or when the gap is; and if you tie it gently with pincers so that it does not break while being tightened; and it is highly recommended to moisten over the gum for loosening the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And do it well in guarding that you break it not, and let remain a part, and return to the patient by the root with greater pains of the first.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And guard that you do not do as the ignorant physicians who by their haste and boldness break the chariot every time, and do not bring them those things which we have told, but sometimes they come from the oquistion of this great malady through the roots that remain, or because they break the cartilage; just as we often wish; and when the tooth is weak, wash the mouth with wine or vinegar and salt; and if bleeding comes, it often happens, so apply the lead plumb to break; and if this does not come, cauterize.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The forms of the tumours, for which one must remove the bone first, are those with long points and large hooks, so that they do not double back when you pull out the bone; and these are:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And are large limbs such that they do not bend when pulled, and are made of iron well-crafted, and have teeth to hold them.
de la racine des dens	of the root of the bone
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root remains at the pulling, it is advisable to place on the limb moist cotton soaked in butter once a day or twice.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	As long as the limb is softening, then it's advisable to apply the tongs called "algefry", because the head seems like a care; and they are made in such a way as a file and that's the form:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out through all these cuts, so it is fitting that you uncover the whole flesh around the root, and then place the instrument called "althal", which is a scalpel, in such a way that this is its form:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And even if it is big and hard so that it does not break, and if the root jumps out because of this, that's good; but if not, then help with all the instruments, for then the forms will come after:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if one helps with this instrument that has two knives, for it is the form:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other instruments that are placed in front of the reason for the teeth, and with this instrument that resembles great pincers, for it is the form:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And so be this instrument firm that it cannot break, and know well how many instruments of bone are; and also other instruments, which are not counted; and the skilled masters discover by themselves their own instrument, according to what his works and illnesses show, because there is among them some diseases for which they do not teach any instrument due to the diversity of such cases and if it breaks neither on the bone nor on other bones, or it pierces, so I seek the instruments that are needed, as I have told you, and help with movements, because this is their form.
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And so be these instruments large and well-held to hold the bone, which will not break but can hold it and remove it; and then restore the patient with medicines that are suitable for this, and if there is corruption in the bone, and it is small, if it is restored with all these instruments.
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the teeth appear neither in their natural form nor according to the body's nature, and the shape is ugly, and even in young girls, it is fitting that you should know whether the teeth are set after the tooth, and not in the right place, and one cannot soothe or calm them: thus the line; and if it is crooked with the tooth, then take this instrument whose form is as shown, and is like a small beak, and is made of iron well-suited for this purpose.
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the cope (or chisel) is used little by little for a few days for the hardness of the tooth, and because you do not move the other teeth, and if it seems possible to straighten it, then take a piece of lime whose form is as shown:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	and is also like the lime from which one makes needles; and in lime, the tooth is polished a little by little with gentle movements for days, so that it does not move until it chisels; then the smooth surface at the end has no sharp edge, and if the teeth are too sharp, they will cut the tongue; therefore, it is fitting to sharpen them so that they become even, so that the tongue is not cut or corrupted by bad speech.
quant li dent lochent	When the teeth loosen
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the teeth loosen, either by percussion or by falling out, and the patient cannot press down on it so that it does not break, and you have tried to cure them with medicines that restrict it, and this doesn't work; if they need to be restrained with a thread of gold, because the threads of silver turn green and rot, but gold never moves; and whether the thread is too thin or too thick or too small, according to the quantity of space between the teeth; and if you see that the teeth are receding, then take out the thread and put it back double between the two healthy teeth, then insert the pins between my teeth, if there are one or more, until you achieve a proper fit; then resume covering where you started, and carefully release your hand so that it does not move; and let your ligature be close to the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Instruct the physician to cut the nails with a needle and assemble them, and then put them between the healthy teeth, so that they do not bleed on the tongue; and then let it be tight until it can last for as long as possible, and if it comes loose, or the thread breaks, tie it with another thread; thus it will remain and serve him as long as he can, and this is the form of the nails and the figure of the alignment of two healthy teeth and two crooked ones, as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth falls out, if it is put back in its place, of fresh to fresh, as we have said; and do not let anyone else who does not know and suffer, for at no time is the shape made like a bone of a cow's teeth, and then put it in where the fault is, and tie it on as we have said, and keep it there until such time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	Covering the ligament of the tongue.
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	There is no ligament that comes from below the tongue or naturally, unless they are born so; or by accident of a wound; and the marks are such that you open the mouth of the patient, keep his head in your hands, and lift the tongue; then cut the nerve of the large tongue, until the tongue is loosened from its place, and if there's scar tissue or anything else, and it's due to sudden injury, so inject something and cut on the large one that ligament; and make sure the cut isn't too deep, because of the artery that is below; and when you've done that, lift him into a warm rose-water and anoint him with oil, then put a towel made of linen under the tongue; let it stay that way for each patient at night, so they can recover.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if the blood is flowing again, put sulfur on the wound; and if it does not flow, cauterize with the fire cautery, which is good for that, then treat with another treatment until it is healed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see the wound be red or black or hard, but the patient does not feel it, and do not touch anything, because it is a chancre; and if it is declining to pus, and there is moisture, take away the lump, and make an incision on one side and the other, and if it does not flow again at your work, put sulfur on it until it is stained, then return to your work until you have treated everything thoroughly; then lift the limb with ease and with care, and treat him with other cures until he is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	Evacuation of an abscess from the throat.
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	No abscess ever comes from inside the throat where they call "godath", and the skin around it is called "amandres". When you cure it, if we have said so in division, and it doesn't heal, be careful: if there's a hard abscess of small size with a fleshy color, do not touch it with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if it's red and the root is big, do not touch it with iron, for fear of the bleeding; but let it be left until it dries up, and then you will cut it, lest it bursts on its own. If it's white in color again, and the root is subtle, have prepared the instrument to cover it, but first check if the abscess has dried up and calmed down.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Therefore fix the patient in front of the sun, and let his joints be clean, and he works the mouth and presses the surgeon's hand between his fingers, and presses the tongue down towards all the instrument, so that there is the form; and it may be made of silver or fine gold as well as our knife:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	Press the tongue towards all this instrument, and you will see the abscess, if take the lancet and cut in the almond, and pull out the pus until it can no longer be pulled; and pull off any thread from the wounds with, then cut at the instrument, so that there is the form which resembles a force; and look to see the head are curved, and one side towards another, and they are very good, and are made of iron or tin.
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument present, then use these pliers, for it is of this form:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	And let it be cut from one side and the other side, and when you have cut one of the almonds, cut the other in the same manner, and after the incision, gargle the patient with hot and cold water, or cold water mixed with grape skins cooked or dried leaves of myrtle, and similar things, until the wound is free from inflammation; then continue the cure until they are healed, and at no time do they produce more swelling in the throat than two almonds, cut them accordingly as the two almonds hold.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I treated a woman with an abscess that was in her throat, namely the small abscess; and had I tightly closed the entire throat so that the woman could not breathe through the obstructed passage, nor eat or drink, and would have died if she remained like that for one day or two.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscesses were deep, so high they had to be cut into two places by two openings through the nose.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I then made a cut in one of them and put in one needle, then I applied fire to it and took out three inches through the nose; then I cut another in the other opening and applied pressure to the throat and pressed the tongue; afterwards I put a needle into that abscess and cut off a part of it and only blood came out a little; and thus I cleaned the neck conduit for the woman, and she now began to drink cool water and then wine, and did not stop cutting that abscess for a long time; because it kept returning and filling with liquid until it was very large; so I took it out and cauterized inside the throat: thus she remained still for some time; and I left those parts to God afterwards.
de l’uve	of the eye
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When the nose descends to the eye and it is drawn in and extended, if it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is not large and rounded, but rather a swelling or an ulcer.
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is cut as we said in the division, and the cure does not benefit, and you see that the swelling subsides, and it is subtle, so it should be copied; and when it is rounded and not long, it is more painful; and if it is sanguine or dark red or black, then it is better to remove the incision.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	Because there is great danger for the sick person.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	Therefore, when you see it, according to the manner in which I told you, the shape and length of the swelling, you must sit the patient facing the sun, and press the tongue against the instrument we have remembered here before; then poke the needle into the eye, and draw it out so that it is not too tight, and cut with two instruments as I said for the incision of the two almonds.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	Instruct the patient to cover only the superfluity that is beyond the natural limit; for if you do more, it will grieve your voice and talk, and after the incision, use what we have said in the incision of the two almonds, and cure until it is sane.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient has fear of cutting, it is fitting to use oil at the cautery.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	The manner of the cautery is like ice water.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And the patient puts his head on your healthy one, and then presses the tongue with the instrument we have said about cautery, wrapped in hot, live wax, so that it is neither too thick nor too thin; and thus takes hold of the upper part of this instrument, for this is its shape.
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	Instruct the patient to put a small amount of medication into their mouth, as with a spoon, and place the instrument on top of their nose; and let the sick person sit upright so that saliva and mucus run from their mouth into the medicine, so it does not go down the throat, and into the stomach. Then hold your hand over the medicine and press firmly onto the nose, for half an hour's worth of time until you see the signs of the medicine taking effect and the itching subsides; and if you notice, take cotton and wipe off any instruments, and moisten the cotton in the medicine, and pour the instrument into the cotton bag above, until the cotton sticks to the nose; and do this often, until the cautery is complete, then let it dry, and clean up afterwards four days or five. If you need to restart the cautery of the medicine, restart it, and after doing so, clean off the medicine with cotton under the nose, in butter and flour, and cleanse that which was surrounded by the medicine.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is more safe than incision, whether it's cautery or not. If it's treated with fumigation according to this manner, take camomile and hyssop and origanum and rue and arnica and similar herbs, and assemble all or any of them in an oil pot, and put it aside, and make boil; and the pots should be well glued with strong earth, and in the pot have a headstone according to this manner:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And if of silver or lead, and either one of the headstones poured into the mouth of the sick man until the vapor rises up through the eye by the nose, until the eye is numbed; after that, repeatedly do so until the eye dries, and take care not to do this at the beginning of the rising of the abscess, because many things happen; and do it no more than when the abscess turns.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	If the fire cautery is not present, take a candle and put it inside the patient's head, so that their mouth does not feel too hot; for the hot candle does not weigh down the vapor in the mouth, and this is a good cure to bring health together.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Often it happens that a splinter from the fish or any other thing gets stuck in the throat, so it is best to treat what you can see, and press the tongue against the sun until you see the thing; and if nothing comes out and is pushed back into the throat, it is wise to make the patient vomit so that the meat is cooked inside the stomach; by chance, if it gets stuck again in the vomiting, or the patient swallows a piece of sponge, a piece of bread, a piece of lettuce root, or a small piece of dry bread, and ties it with a thread, and then glues it; and when it comes loose, you will pull out; and if it does not come loose as we have said, take an instrument from the plunger according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And so the curved instruments are made for the head if they can more easily enter into the throat, and if the head is lifted up high; and be careful that you do not touch the epiglottis, lest all of the blood come out, nor push the bone inside; and make sure that the patient puts in the instrument, because he feels it going through or on the thing is roughened; so if he swallows, or it is carried over for a whole instrument evenly, until it is done.
de la sansue de la gorge	of the throat without pain.
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	Never is the throat given medicine unless as I said in division, by the treatment of medicines; and when this does not help, then look at the patient's throat to the sun, then press the tongue against the instrument that I told you.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see a boil, so that it has all of its small hair surrounding it, or have fine nails that are worth those.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	But if it is not worth, then take a thread of hair and put it in the throat of the sick person, then pierce or cut off with hot iron, and do this often.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if they are drinking the sick all day long.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Then take a full glass of cold water, and open the mouth, and let it flow inwards to be swallowed, and move it with their hand often; and as soon as the boil feels the water, it vomits.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	And if it does not vomit as we have said, then perfume the sick person with asafoetida in the instrument that I have mentioned for fumigation of the wound; do this many times, because she will sneeze with tar.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	Et the manner of fumigation is that you pick up an empty pot in which there are hot coals, and cover it with a sieve pierced in the middle, and then in that hole, the nails of the instrument will fall; then you put your fumigation, and the patient puts their head over the can in their mouth, and closes their mouth so that the smoke does not escape, but comes out just there; and now the cough comes, and if it does not come, you continue with fumigation many times; and let the patient suffer thirst, and eat foul things and ashes, and do not drink water at all; and then they will be cured by this government.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the form of the instrument used to treat an abscess is when it can be seen, resembling curved tongs for nails to enter into the neck; and it has a resemblance to the beak of a swan, and it has roughness of lime, so that what takes hold of it cannot release.
li chapistres des apostemes	The surgeon of the abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	Many are like abscesses, as is remembered in this book, and they differ in perforation and size; and there are two kinds, one of which is similar to the other, and it holds moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second kind is for those inside the body or in their flesh.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	Because the abscesses in the head are different from those in the bone, and the abscesses in the liver have a different judgment than those that come into joints, and each has its own consideration in work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And if there are abscesses that should not be pierced, until the bone is dead according to its completion; and if of those types it is necessary to pierce them when they are believed to be true, and do not die according to their completion, as those which are near joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when an abscess comes from the joints and one leaves it until it is putrefied, by chance if they are corrupted, the ligament and nerve of the joint, because this is the cause of contraction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	If the abscess is near a principal limb and you delay perforation until it is dead, if it harms the principal limb; or if it's near the foundation, if it's pierced in such a way that it dies; and it's not wise to pierce an abscess when you're certain that digestion has been completed, for fear that the one near the foundation will rot through from within, and become fistulous, and cannot be cured in a great term.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And it is wise that you know the size of the perforation of the abscess when it is dead according to its completion, and this is when the pain is assuaged, and the departures of the fever, and the lessening of the pain and redness, and the softening of the swelling and the sharpening of the chief of the abscess, and other signs; and it is wise that you make a perforation in a place more distant from the abscess, and where it opens, and not in a long distance in the body, if the abscesses are on the hands or feet, or in joints and nerves and arteries, and wherever they are equal so as to have no more pain.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In these that are bent, by one of each limb.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when there is an abscess in the skull, if you value your life, so that you allow the perforation to complete until it is confirmed by completion of digestion, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	For if you pierce before it, so that the body is filled with venom of it, and is full of much filth; and by chance the lips and the fundament of it become hardened.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if any abscess is pierced according to the size of the body, according to what the limbs have need.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And it is fitting that you administer small punctures for small abscesses, small punctures for small ones; and for large abscesses, large punctures, and many wounds according to the similarity of their size. And if there are such abscesses where it is necessary to cut out the source, and cover; when they have become as we said, worn away like a torn piece, so it is fitting to do as we do for boils: and if there are those that are split into three angles, and those from which you puncture like the bee of myrtle, like abscesses in the joints; and if there are others where one makes a round cut, and other cuts, and similar punctures.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	In those without a head, as an abscess is soft and superficial, it is necessary to let the pain go through fully; and when the abscess is big, and has collected much blood, and you allow some of it to pass, so that not all of it passes in one hour, but rather only a part, then stop the abscess just the day before, then take away nothing from that place; do this many times with great care, until the bowels are whole; at the same time, if the patient is weak in virtue, or an elderly woman, or little child, or decrepit old man.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	So you expect to fail at times when the outcome of the blood is known, and perhaps the patient will die, and you should not be disappointed.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Avoid this chapter then with great care, and when you have pierced your abscess, if the wound heals, and look to see if the wounds from the abscess are small; and if it's a plain incision, apply tenths of linen or old cotton; and if there are large abscesses, and much pus, it is necessary that you put one tent in each so they come into contact with each other; and if you have pierced the skin around an abscess part by part, and bound it tight, then fill it with old cloth or woolen rags soaked in moisture, and bind it on the third day; then apply the ointment, and the dressing until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	If there is bleeding at the wound, apply cool and cold water and dress with moist cloth, and cover it with linen wrapped around many times.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the bleeding persists, apply firm and gentle treatment and cure, and the powders that I have in your hands in this book, if it is winter and the wounds or abscesses are very nervous, so cover them with linen soaked in wine and oil hot; and if it's still inflamed and the wound is charred, if it suits you to do so, put on soft linen soaked in water and oil, or in hot wine and oil every third day, as we have said; and then remove the abscess and clean it, if it seems fitting, until it is healed.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	In order to know this surely, instruct the patient to examine it entirely when treating an abscess: for you have said how one should act before performing the treatment of an abscess, and here the chapter is.
des soros	of sorrows.
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	Where cuts on the head come from small abscesses, and are of many kinds, such as those in cloth, like a mouse skin, and there is much of that sort.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	There are fat ones and those that are like poultices, where moisture is present, just like pus; and there are some that are hard and stone-like to cut into, without any doubt, unless the arteries cause a change.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the scars from the waist area are such that you should know all the instruments called "entremissoire", because of which they come into shape after, what is contained.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, they do it from above down long.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And when the moisture is empty, they scrape without leaving anything on the skin that contains that moisture, because it returns when you leave nothing there; then they plunge cotton in ointment Egyptian, if present; or water and cloth, and apply the wound, and let it rest until the next day; and those who are left overnight will correct those who are still present.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then when they reapply the cotton, just like before, the second day, and the linen, until you know well that it will not stay overnight; then treat the wound with ointment suitable to the patient, until they are healed.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the abscesses hold out not much fat, they make it according to this form, from top to bottom; and you apply ointments, and scrape all over, and put all your care of treatment on the shirt where it is; and if the arteries cause contractions, then do what I have told you afterwards.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And also do so with the abscess if it is a stone, and as you cut and cure as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And the cut on the stone abscess and the moisture, if it is lighter, because there is little blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And if some of these abscesses or the head are free from moisture, and of those I copied, which is a head of an old woman; and I found the abscess as hard as a stone, rough and white, and cannot be broken; and if any one had been burned with it, it would have done equally well the wound as if it were a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	In other abscesses coming or heads, whatever those which come with the head of children and the roots of the ears, cut them so that they are open all day until it comes out the bowel; and cure as needed.
des scrophules	Dead bodies
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Many times happen an abscess at the neck, and beneath the armpits, and in the groin area, and sometimes appear elsewhere on the body, and are very painful, and are stuck together.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And each body is in its proper place, as it was in the neck and under the armpits, as we have said; and there are many similarities of these bodies.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some that contain moisture, and there are also those that are malignant and will not obey the health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	In that one therefore which you see of good disposition at the toucher, and is similar to the color of the flesh, and mute in every part, and not inflamed as on the neck or artery or vein, nor too deep; then it is fitting to copy it from above, and scrape off each part, and make them both lips like those of a healthy one, if you have need; as we have said about incisions of the neck. Be cautious that you do not cover the nerve or vein, and do not cut with sharp objects, lest the hand fail, and see too far ahead, that you may only copy what you should.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	If you prick the vein or artery, and it will not stop bleeding, apply vitriol to the wound, or any powder that remains to stanch the blood, and hold the wound in place; and let it be so long as the abscesses are appeased, and the pain is mollified, and then start to dress the wound.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	And when the swelling is gone, it will return to its original state, until you complete it; then choose a suitable index if it does not show small boils, cut and lance them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	If the root of a boil has great inflammation, it is not advisable to cut that boil at its root alone, but rather tie with a double strong thread, and let it fall off without causing harm; then apply the wound with Egyptian linen soaked in ointment.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you scrape the entire scrophule, then it is fitting that you assemble the two lips of the wound and now close them, for there will be no remaining superfluity because of the great size of the scrophule.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	so it is fitting that you listen to the root of it and treat the furrow, and close it just as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those scrophules that hold superfluity, let them bleed where they open up; and treat it as described before, according to the situation, then apply ointment and similar things, so that what remains of the corruption is purged away; and when the wound is thoroughly cleansed, apply ointment to heal, until it is fully healed.
de squinance	of ulcers.
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancient people spoke and said about the cutting of the throat; but I have never seen it done in our land, and this is the writing of their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	It is necessary for those who have hemorrhaged that the opening of the throat, which is called "epiglote", be avoided; and one should not do this because all the veins and the swollen flesh of the patient are at those places where they have made a sharp cut in the mouth, or in the throat or elsewhere.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the canal of the swollen flesh, it is necessary to cover the epiglote to avoid the destruction that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	It is therefore necessary, when we want to cut the epiglote, that we cut it under three circles or four one small incision across between the two circles or according to the size of the incision in the suture, neither in the cartilage; and thus is preferred if there is no section of the epiglote because there will be no scar and the vessel will be long from it.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	If the patient's joints are swollen due to pain, instruct him to extend his neck as far as possible, then cut the vein up until it comes near the elbow; and remove the swelling of blood, if you see anything, and then strike the vein, just like we have said; and it is proven by the section of the vein's blood that came out when the limb was broken, and by the voice's failure; and let the wound be covered with a piece.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed because one doubts strangulation, gather the two lips of the wound at the vein, and pull out the entire skin with the cartilage; then administer medicines that make pus, until it is cured.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	All the more so since it is not done until the throat is completely swollen and the patient is pronounced dead and the defect in the tongue.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	Instruct the patient to hold his tongue since he cannot speak, and breathe through the wound, and so it is kept from death; for the ancients command that they leave the wound open until the malady is passed, and it passes away in three days or four, and then they commanded him to sew up the wound and cure it, until it was cured; and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I saw that a young maiden took out her knife and stuck it in her throat, and cut off part of the neck; and I was called to cure her, and I found her also dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound and found out that blood had come from it; and I realized that she hadn't cut a vein or inserted a needle anywhere but the throat, and the blood came out of there through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I have failed to translate the text.
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	Cyst or abscesses are called "throat hernia", and it's a large cyst in the color of jet, and it is often found in women; and they occur in two ways: by nature and by accident; for if it occurs naturally, it has no knot.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And the accident occurs in two ways: because one is like fat tissue, and the other is like an abscess coming from an artery; and there is fear, and it's not advisable to apply hot fires to anyone who is thin, but rather prove them and search at all the surrounding area: if you find it as fat as I mentioned, and do not seek a vein, then cut it as one cuts flesh, and follow its entire shape, if there is no point; and thoroughly search for it, and cure it as needed, until it is completely healed.
des nous	of us
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	There are many ways in which they (the bones) are united, of which I will speak all the similarities; and it is necessary that I tell you the difference between them (the bones) and their fracture.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that when the fever and the swelling remain as long as the bleeding has not stopped, and is accompanied by putrefaction; then the fever and the swelling will subside.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	But without a fracture, there is no swelling, fever, or pain, and it contains the abscess, which are its own sacs, and begin to swell in proportion to the size of the body, and become similar as if they were like a jar, and grow; and are similar in color, weight, moisture, and texture, just as I said in division.

It is fitting when you come to the treatment of this disease that you examine and inquire first about all the instruments called "entromissoire", as their form will become clear.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	And the way to inquire about the abscesses is that you prick or moisten it with a quantity of fluid you find in the abscess, and turn your thumbs slowly until you know that the instrument has pierced the core, then pull out the "entromissoire", and be careful not to burst.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	If the pus is cut, as it has color, do so as I have said for other abscesses; and if after the "entromissoire" does not come out with moisture, know that it is fat, then cut into a cross, and take hold of it with pincers, and lightly scrape off each part and wear a cloak where it lies, so that you may treat the wound clean with the nose; and if you cannot do so, pull it apart into pieces so that it does not stay there.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	For if it stays in place, then it will revert to its former position many times; and if it remains for a short while without causing any harm, apply the wound with some corrosive powders, and tie the wound, and put on soothing substances near the abscess, and cure other treatments until it is healed; and if it becomes large, cut two fingers off from the wound, and cure this one who causes inflammation.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	And if the vein bursts against it or another substance if you hasten and apply the lead of vitriol broken, let him lie for two days or three, until the wound becomes clean, and rests on the convalescence of the blood; then return to covering that which is left untouched.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	Here are the forms of entranced tumors, and they come in three kinds: great, medium, and small; and among them there are three quarters called "albaret", and one called "breb", and they also come in three kinds: large, medium, and small, to enclose fistulae apertures; and they are like the needles with which you sew suture wounds, made of citrin (gold), iron, or silver, and move as if they were yellow, because they are more suited for closing the black spots of fistulae; and come in three kinds: great, medium, and small, according to the width of the perforations.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The forms of tumors are of many kinds, as you see here: large, medium, and small; and if tumors have two bodies in three ways also; and if tumors that have three bodies, and are so in three ways; and if tumors with two bodies, and single body only, and are so in three ways; and all this is necessary for their treatment.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	The head of these is cut to make them sharp, and of such kind are those which do not cut through only one side, from which one must burn the skin, because you cannot lance the vein or the nerve; and of these hidden kinds are the swallowed lemons in handbags, so that the patient does not lose them at the opening of the abscesses; and they come in three ways: large, small, and medium, as you see; and one should not use only to cut for more than to treat with a chariot, like legs, arms, and nipples, and veins, and similar limbs; and sometimes another little instrument is made, resembling the cuts of fistulas, according to this shape, when it stains the vein.

de la routure de l’artere	About the cutting of an artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans. des apostemes des ners	Of abscesses of the intestines.
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Also when abscesses come into the artery and vein, they come into the intestines because of being cold, or from excessive labor, and similar things.

quant li boude ist fuer	when the boil bursts

dou chancre	A wound
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have said in the division of chancre, and how to treat it with medicines, and how not to use iron treatment; and we say that chancre inflames the breastbone, and great caution is needed in its treatment; and the ancients said that when chancre appears on someone who can be cut near the navel, as a breastbone chancre does, or in the groin, and similar places, and it should be entirely removed when it first begins to show up; but when it grows large and old, you do not need to approach it, for I have never seen anyone cured from this condition; nor has anyone else ever been cured from it before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide I boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the wounded ones, when they are in the place where it can be removed, as we have said, is that you never purge the sick person of black bile; then make them healthy if they show signs of repletion; and after, treat the wound to make the patient well; then apply your poultices or chancre, and the head of all parts, and the bone of all parts without leaving anything behind; and let the wound fully bleed, and take good care that the patient is healthy in your hands or with anything, and if they bleed from the incision of an artery or vein, cauterize as long as there is no stain; then treat them with another treatment until they are made whole.
de ydropisie	of dropsy
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	We have said in the division of symptoms that there are similar signs of dropsy, and how the assembly of water is made, and the signs of each one, and the treatment done with medicines, and the one cured by iron: if it is opened alone; and you should not touch with iron in these two similarities: this means tympanites and yopsarche, because they are a deadly thing; therefore when you do the medicine for this similarity called "eclites" of medicine, and the cure does not profit, look at whether the patient is weak or has another disease than dropsy, as fever and constipation and similar things; if you don't touch with iron, because there is doubt; and if you see the patient strong and he only has dropsy alone, and he is neither too old nor too young, then do this: lift the patient straight up on your hands, and the assistants press the belly towards the bottom of the abdomen, pushing out the water to its lowest part, then take the spatumile (a long, thin instrument) with a thorny end according to this shape:
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And let them cut two parts.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	Cut with a point and make sure it's not too close that it can come inside the intestine when you insert it; otherwise, it will cause bleeding. Then check if the dropsy is gathered towards the intestines: if so, cut into the third part of the vein on both sides above the artery; and if it's due to liver disease, cut on the left side of the third part; and if it's due to ulcers, cut on the right side. And make sure that the patient does not apply pressure on the cut wound so that the superfluous fluids do not flow to a weak spot in them; then pierce the whole skin with the instrument, pour out, and tie tight your hand around all the spatumile between the skin and the vein as if you were scraping when cutting to the amount of an inch or two; then pierce the vein until the spatumile is four fingers long, and that's the size of the juice; then take it out, and pour this instrument with which this shape is made.
