Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	And it seems like a chain of silver, and is made of iron or of an arrow lightweight, and in the lower part there is a small hole; and on one side there are three holes, and two on the other, and one on the other; and the head is cut so like a feather, and this is the form of the incision that the scribes shape the feather:
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort; mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit; fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	At the head above is the marrow, so that when the instruments approach the water, it now comes out from the instrument; empty then half or a third, because if you empty more than what is needed in that hour, by chance he may die of the resolution of his spirit with the arrow, or he coughs or approaches death; but empty according to the quantity of his virtue, and according to what the dispositions of his virtue signify to the patient, and his feet; then take up the instrument and hold back the water, because it is held now by the pressure that blocks the hole above on the cheek, which I have spoken of, so that you pierce according to this manner; then resume the instrument another day, if you see the patient suffering such, and extract a small quantity of water; do this one day, and beware not to be foolish until he no longer requires but a little water.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	If you doubt the patient, and let them drink much water, then take the cure of burial or hot sand, and after a great sweat or bath and in the sun, and make them drink beer; and treat with medicine desiccative until they are healthy, and cauterize on the stomach and on the liver and on the spleen after extracting the water, as I have said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	of the hemorrhoid.
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	No child is ever born without a single defect in the rectum, or if there is one it's small, and it does not fit its place.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	If they wish to pierce it immediately, so that they do not feel pain throughout the entire rectum, very subtle and according to this shape.
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	Instruct the patient to put or cut out the wound from its source, and bind it and tie it in this manner for three days or four, and when he wants to urinate, cut open the closed part, make him urinate, and then release it; and by chance it does not fall off, because the urine that comes forth does not let loose the closed part.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	If it is of the foot and there is a cut, then apply medicine to the cloth, as we have said, and it will widen.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	Those who do not have the cut in their own place are pale, because no one is born with a cut on the head of the penis, since they cannot urinate until they raise their penis up; and they cannot defecate because the matter cannot come down to the anus, and this is a bad disease.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	Instruct the patient to lie on his back, so that the chief of the instrument (verge) rests on his spine, and then the head of the rod is placed and struck as if it were the size of a pinhead, just as it should be; and take care not to make any incision when bleeding often comes, and if it happens, then tighten the one that causes bleeding, and cure the wound until it heals.
des pustules de la verge	from the head of the rod (verge) due to pus.
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a I oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	There are times when cysts appear on the rod, and it's a foul appearance, whether good or bad; so you should pick them off one by one with great subtlety, cut them all open, then apply cotton moistened in Egyptian ointment, and treat with diafinicon ointment until they heal.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	And if the humors are malignant, of a putrid color and smell, it is advisable that you apply cautery.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	When you have applied it, and the humors are in the belly, and some of them are inside the skin and some outside, it is advisable to remove the humors that are inside first; and when it is soothed, if the wound is outside.
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you are treating it altogether, make sure the joint of the vein is not perceived, for if it is not, blackness and corruption come to the vein and the spot; so it is advisable to remove all that which is black and corrupted, then tie up the plaster made of honey and flour which is made from the rind of sour plums and vinegar, then apply other treatments until it is sane.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	And if a swelling comes, then apply lunar cauterization according to this form:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars; et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	The cauterization is helpful in two conditions: it is to see swelling and corruption; and if the head of the finger is swollen and drawn back, so that you put or apply a linen bandage around it, and let the patient urinate; and when the hair over the head of the finger has dried up as in those who have not been circumcised, because of wound or abscess, then therefore it is advisable to scorch with a hooked instrument at the top of the finger, until the ligaments are loosened, and the head of the finger is freed from all parts; and if this is a painful thing to do, then it is advisable to scorch with a small spatula under the chin of the finger and hair. Then carefully apply two bandages, and put a subtle linen cloth soaked in cold water between them, so that the discharge comes directly.
de la circoncision	About circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not a source of continued illness like other wounds; it can be done whenever we choose, and is especially necessary for children, because it is their best and most gentle treatment.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	They did not say that circumcision should be done on their children, because they do not use it in their law, and we have only what we know by experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor I dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a II toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	Because I have taken the greatest part of the masters and physicians who practiced circumcision in school, with forces, and with great experience; so they would say it was better because it had two stitches, and by chance someone hit those above and kept that one below.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	For the recovery of health, it is certain that there is double pain and at the cleanliness which is not secure the point of the member; and at the cleansing of the wound by chance escapes the iron, and overflows the vein, and many times happen so they do not need further cleansing.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	From the cleanliness which is made with force all along the entire length of the thread I have found the good luck of the experiment, because the forces cut exactly both above and below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you press your hand, the cuts are equally straight in all directions; but if the thread is tied tightly around the skin; and the manner of the first operation is such that you think about what the child sees, if they see it, do not make a difference between tying the thread around the vein solely, and making it slip away in various ways that you can; then take the hand straight down onto the vein and breathe on it, and hold out your hand so that the stitches of the vein are exposed; then clean it well from the dirt that is gathered there; then tie a new signet with a double thread, then tie it underneath one another thread; and keep two threads by the second tied fast to the pouch and the toe index, and cut between the two threads, then tie the wound above hastily and pull up the head of the vein; then let the blood flow little by little, because it is the worst part; and put powder on top and powdered with rose water that is warm and moist, congealed with good oil roset, and fresh, and leave it there till the next day, and cure with another cure until it is healthy.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The form of the force at purification is thus: let the two shoulders be tied and are being cut, and let the shoulders be as large as the elbow.
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error of purification is when the keys inside are found at the incision; so it must be extended to your angle, in such a way that the wound opens; and cut equally, and if you cannot hold to your angle, if you have clamps, and then cut.
Et s’il trespassent III jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if they persist for three days, and that which is below the vein is swollen, let it be left until the wounds are healed, and lightly scrape; and cut as you can move, and guard yourself from the part of the vein, lest it harm none.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Cure then the joint of such sudden pain caused by powder, which we have said or treated as powders, and if it is struck with excessive force, and it goes up, so it does not harm; cure it then, just as we have said, until it is healthy.
dou retenement de l’urine	when retention of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	If the retention of urine is due to a stone, or frozen blood, or bowels, or gallstones, or similar things, which we have said in division; and if the urine does not come out, and you see that there is retention because of the stone lodged or near the neck of the bladder, then it is fitting to lean the patient on their knees; and put their feet upon the back, and make them stretch the belly from above the back, and restrain the patient until they can relieve themselves as much as possible; and thus constrains the neck of the bladder to expel the stone upwards, because the urine comes out; and if it does not come, just as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, then you should administer extraction for all the instrument called "siringue", namely: a silver thin leg like the feather of a bird, half a palm long, and subtle at the head.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals; et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.
des maladies de la vessie	De maladies of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When scorched things or blood comes into the bladder, or pus is assembled, and you see urine and medicine distill, then do this to all the instrument called "clepsedre", which is like this:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	It is closed, and if it has three perforations: two on one side, and one on the other, as you see; and the leather straps because the medicine can be applied well to the tip until the wound heals, if possible, and when you put the medicine in the bladder, put the cover of the container in the moisture, and draw out from behind it; drawing out the moisture from behind, and then push the container forward; if the moisture enters the container, and comes into the bladder now, so that the patient feels it; and this is the subtle form of the clistere where one clisters the bladder:
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	Et est d'argent ou d'archaut, and is the key more high; and below to I see where the ties are broken; then take a sheep’s vessel and put in the moisture that you see thickening the vessel, then tie between the two breasts of a good double thread, and heat it on the fire; then pour the head into the clotter in the stick, then strain your hand over the vessel until the patient feels that this moisture has come to the vein; and if you do not have the vessel, take a piece of parchment, and make a circle, and pierce round about; then pour the strong thread in those wounds, then assemble the circle as one assembles wool, and put inside what you see oil and moisture and water, and tie in the instrument; and do so as you did with the vessel, pressing with your hand until the moisture comes to the vein.
de la piere	From the stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have said in the division of stones, and the extraction of medicinal substances; and I said the differences between stone from honey and rain, and all signs, and in which stone one must operate with cutting; and in the bladder, and the penis; and I will tell you clearly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont IIII ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone in the bladder which is honey-like in the vessel occurs more often in children, and it's a sign that the water has burst forth from the bladder like water in its subtlety; and they bring out their kidneys, and excite the patient's penis, and cut them many times, and then swell up; and there are much swelling of the feet; and is lighter the healing of children until they are 4 years old, and is more painful in old age, and is like stone in those who are between youth and oldness; and the cure is lighter for those with a large stone than for those with a small one.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to the treatment, it is necessary to first purify the patient by cleansing, so that all the filth which is in his intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	But it blocks sometimes when trying to take out the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	Then take the patient by the feet, and push him downwards, so that the stone comes out to the bottom of the bladder, and sometimes it falls down to his chest; then make him sit between your hands prepared, and his hands be below his knees, so that the bladder is entirely inclined towards you; then look and touch inside; if you feel the stone in the space, take now and cut on top of the stone.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	And if it does not fall out at the toucher (the stone's edge), then apply to the first finger of your left hand with oil from that same finger on your right hand; if the patient is sick, or on your right hand, if the patient is a young man accomplished; and pour it into its foundation, look for the stone, and when you feel it on your finger, press towards it at the base of the bladder; then press with all your might until you see to cut.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	Instruct the minister to press the bladder with his hand, and he commands him to extend his right hand fingers up high, and to hold his left hand fingers under the nails, where they are covering the area where the operation is performed; then, he pours the spatula mixture into this form.
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	And it is placed between the nails and the foundation, not in the middle but on the side of the left shoulder; and it should be straight above the stone, and both ends near the foundation, and it should be cut through the flesh so that it is wide at the top and narrow towards the bottom, according to the size of the stone, neither too large nor too small; by chance the pressure may cause one of the bones in the foundation to break loose during work; and observe whether there is part of the stone with angles or edges: if it sticks to come out easily.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	For the angles and margins of this cut, make the incision larger; and if it doesn't cut, it is to be strained with the nails as sharp as a knife on the forehead, so that you strain the bone so that it does not escape; or you pour through the subtle instrument curved at the head; and if you cannot do it in this way, expand your poor body, and if it has not been cut off, strain with vinegar; and if it has more than one bone, first put the largest into the neck of the bladder, then strike above, then pull out, and the small ones afterwards if there are more.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	And if it is very large, it should be sewn on and a larger wound made.
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	For these two things happen to the patient: either he dies, or urine comes out again because the stitches cannot hold; but in any case force yourself to treat, or to debilitate the nails, until you sew it piece by piece; and when you have completed your work, apply the wound with resin of dragon, aloes, and bloodstone, and bind it, and place above a moist cloth in oil and wine, or in oil and rosewater and cold water, to calm the burning abscess; then revive the patient on his back, and do not unbind the stitches until three days.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you release it, so that the limb moves very well again, apply oil and water to it, then bind with linen thread or gauze, until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	And if abscesses come into the wound and cause corrosion and frost of blood in the bladder, and it is retained there because of urine congestion, which is known in this manner that without urine: put then your poultice on the wound, and extract that blood, for if it remains, the bladder will corrode, and rot; then lift up the wound with water and asphodel and salt, and help him with all the ways you know, until he is healed; and it is fitting that all the treatments you give to him, tie his two legs together, and assemble those medicines on the limb.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	In case the piercing is small and it has come out of the rod and stuck, and urine cannot come out; so if I say again to you that you must measure it many times, then excuse yourself from this measurement for this treatment.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have already proven this way.
Pren I foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a III angles fichiees en I tison:	Take iron of this shape and fix three holes in the girdle.
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	Then take the thread and tie it around the rod under the stone, so that it cannot come out after in the bladder; then push the iron into the rod lightly, until it comes to the stone; and turn the iron by hand to the other side of the stone little by little, until you can pierce the stone on the other side; if it comes soon afterwards, then press your hand upon what is left behind of the stone that is inside the rod.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is broken now and flows with urine, and the patient is cured; and if you cannot do this for any reason that prevents it, tie I finger below the bone and I another above, then make the spear point towards the bone between the two ligaments, then draw back, and release the ligament, and clean the wound which has congealed in the injury; and care for him until he is cured.
de la piere des femmes	of a woman's bone
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por III choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	It rarely happens that a bone is incarcerated in women, and if it has ever happened, the cure is difficult, and is forbidden by three reasons: one is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; and the second is that we cannot find a woman who knows how to expose herself with mirrors, especially when she is cast down.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere; et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	Instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	If it is swollen, so it should be moved from the entrance of the bladder to the under part, until it comes to the root of the thigh; then strike on the stone in the root of the thigh against the middle of the bone, where it is moved around, and feel the bone in that part; and do not move the dog above or below the bone, and let it be tied to the first part small; then pour hot water into the size, if you feel the bone so close to the wound as long as the stone can come out, and know that there are many kinds of stones: that is to say, small and large and rough and smooth, long and round, and which have holes.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	if you know the similarities to know the outcome.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	And if it is not swollen, then apply vitriol paste to the affected area, hold for an hour until it is stained; then return to your work, until the stone comes out, and you have the substances that I told you in the extraction of stones from men to help you in your work. And if it is not swollen, and it's a vein that has been cut, apply powder on the patient and the strained tulle and bandages, and do not start again, let the stone be left alone, lest the patient die; then treat the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the wound is calmed, and the pulse is good again, he returns to his work, until the stone is cleared.
de hernie carnouse	of outward hernia
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit I autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	It is nothing but a collection of moisture or white suture, which is under the knee, and contains blood; and it's called "suture", and sometimes it's not properly attached to the skin if one thinks it's something else; and it's the cowhide of the joint between the white suture that we've said; and such things do not happen unless one has suffered.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the growth of this suture is weak that it comes to the joints, and spreads out that material.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And sometimes it comes from percussion on the joints, and this moisture has many colors: or it's color declining to yellowish, or it's without red, or black, or white, and there are more of such; and these are the signs of recognizing this collection, because if it is the suture we've said, then it's the abscesses returning, for a short time like the shape of an ear, and it doesn't open the joints, because it has moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	If he has moisture in his own skin, then the abscesses grow with a part of the flesh; and so it is thought to be another wound; and if the moisture is between the hide of the thigh and the white skin, he feels pain well; therefore, when you see that you should exercise caution on all the surrounding area, for this is what has come before.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	Therefore, those who come after the surrounding area judge what is inside.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when we cut with iron, it is fitting that the patient be healthy according to our power and the replenishment of his body; then place on his back, on one point a little high, and let him lie down heavily; then sit above his left side, and command the minister to sit on his right, and extend the rod to one of the two costs of the thigh; then take the spatulate, clean, and cut the skin of the thigh from its long joint until its white flesh, and make a straight incision along the skin of the thigh up to the joint, and carefully scar it according to our power; then perforate the white plain with water to a large puncture, and extract all the water, and then put your nails, and stand the white flesh upward; and do not touch the skin of the thigh, but only the white flesh, cut it throughout or in pieces equally, so that if you do not cut well, he will return the blood; and if the flesh falls into your work, put it back on its own joint when you have completed the perforation of the white flesh; then assemble the two levers of the thigh skin to a costure, and cure as with other wounds, until he is healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	If you find the corrupted blood of another disease, it is fitting that you should tie off the vessels that are suspended above, doubting the decrement of blood; then strike the clot at all the suspended area, and extract the blood, and treat as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	If the wound is assembled in two parts into one assembly, knowing that they are two branches; then strike the other part as you did the first equally, and bleed the blood, and put a moist linen in the wound soaked in rose oil; and put apart another linen soaked in wine and oil, and place over the two clots, and cover with double draperies, and tie it above to all the thread that is according to this form:
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	Then take the two draperies and apply them according to this resemblance and are assembled by sewing in the throat of the braies, and one of the knees is pulled upwards on the ground behind, and the other towards the elbow; and another two above the two armpits, and the whole assembly is tied together in a bow around the waist; and sometimes this branch of cautery is given in place of iron binding, where you take a fine surgical saw, and strike the flesh of the clots, and burn as we have said so that the white substance contained in the blood is revealed; then take the cautery according to this form, and pierce the clot with needles, and scorch with this subtle cautery hot:
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille; et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	Instruct the patient to look at it all sorts of ways while you examine; and be careful that fire does not touch the eye; and know that this work is more safe; and be cautious of accidents of blood and wounds; and if no other thing troubles you, or an abscess on your hand or wound or another thing, cure what troubles you, according to what has been said beforehand.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit; pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer; puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee; et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	But if the patient is afraid and does not want to endure this work due to its horror, perforate it as I have said, and because when you are certain about the water's meaning, just sit the patient upright on the high bed; then pierce the abscess in the lower part all over the wide space, and make the perforation deep into the body; and if the wounds are large enough so that all the fluid can flow out, then put cotton on the wound, tie it up, and let it drain the remaining fluid for a while, then treat until the wound is healed; and if the scab will not come out of the mouth of the wound, it's necessary to insert a needle or the instrument used to treat dropsy, as before, because that form is what we have previously described; and enlarge the wound a little bit, and know when the fluid returns, and gets assembled after six months or sooner, and just like before, so will the patient pass its days.
de l’aposteme des coions	Of an abscess of the joints
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	Seeing in the section of this branch that there is fear of many deaths, because it seems to be worth not cutting; and I will tell you about the work and the signs of an abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	I say then that most abscesses come from the body, and to the joints, and this happens in many cases.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	It is to be known that this happens because of superfluous acid and water that spreads to the joints, or through percussion; and the color of the abscess corresponds with the color of the body; and there is no pain, but it's an abscess causing a trouble; and sometimes these are grievous and piercings, with a foul color, and never comes from elsewhere than an artery, or swelling of the vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	When it is not caused by an artery, so it is found by the shape of the abscess, when you press on your two fingers; and it does not happen that you touch it.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	This one that is formed by an enlargement of the vein is found by its shape at the point where you touch it gently with your two fingers; and one can easily make the size increase on this appearance, and on other swellings; and thus you should cut the exact spot on the swelling, then stand the edge up high, and remove the suspension from all parts of the edge.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope; et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	If the vein is already swollen with those swellings, then it is necessary to treat the vein and make the cut; and if there is any area swollen at the surface, or inside the vessels, it is necessary to release that entire area and make a round cut.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the hair grows at the head's back on you, then it is fitting that you copy it all, and extract the root, as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your wounds are completed, apply the dressing of woolen cloth moistened in oil rose and wine, then cure with other cures until it is healed.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscesses of the tonsils
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	This is an abscess that has burst from an enclosure similar to the gallbladder, with the softening of the tonsils, and the patients suffer greatly when it appears; and the treatment for this disease is as near to fear-inducing as what was previously stated, and we will tell you about its work according to what the ancients did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment; puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples; puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief; puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues; puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions; car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz; si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	Instruct the patient to sit on the elevated siege and then let him pour the suspensory over his shoulders, up to his elbows, down the arm, and outwards; so that the masters may see them extend; then strike with a spatumile cutting large through the place, until they are uncovered, and then scrape from each part, as we have said in the extraction of arteries which are at temples; then put an awl or where there is a double thread, and tie it to the first joint or where the vein has come, and tie directly to the other shoulder; then strike straight on, according to the length of the body, and get rid of the corrupting moistures; then cure the wound as the others do, so that none of the vessels might bleed again; for by this there will be no harm, and all the vessels come forward if you take care of them, so it is fitting to treat all the vessels.
de la routure dou syfac	Of a cut from the skin
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses; et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement; et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	The dangers of this wound come from the section that comes out through the skin, or from the extension on the belly in the region of the navel, because the intestines descend from that wound to one of the joints; and this wound is either from the section or from the extension, and both come from two types of causes: either from striking, jumping, burning, or lifting a heavy load, and by similar things; and there are signs when it comes to an extension of the skin wound, which are that they appear little by little, over a long period of time, and do not happen suddenly; and the abscesses are equal in size until the end, because the skin wound presses on the intestine.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the signs are when it comes to a section of the skin wound that brings sudden pain from its beginning, and the abscesses have different appearances under the skin, close to the flesh, because they come out through the intestine and from the body at the site of the skin wound.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And sometimes from that place with the intestine, it is retained in the bowels, and causes great pain to suffer for the patient, especially when it presses.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these iron treatments with fear, because one must beware of them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir; puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes; puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc; puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir; puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars; puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille; et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement; et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz; puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz; puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars; puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne; et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi; et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant; puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	And the manner of opening is such that you command the patient to tie his intestine in his hand inside the wound if it can be drawn out; then sew on his collar between your hands, and lift up the knees; then apply the knife to the top, and cut through all the skin down to the bone; then pour into the veins an amount of linen wool according to what you have need for to open the wound, so that it may come out; then scrape off the flesh that is under the skin of the bones, until the white skin is revealed from all parts; then put your right index finger into that which follows the bone, between the white skin that is under the skin of the hoof, and between the second skin; and pull with the main hand inside the wound to the knife of the bones, and lift up the hoof along with all its skin towards the belly; and command the minister to extend the hoof upwards, and release what is behind the knot; ask whether there is any intestine wrapped around or white skin dry, and if you find nothing, pour it into the belly underneath; then take a needle or one with a thread made of four threads, and put it in the back part of the skin, which is after the skin of the bones; after the belly, then cut through the tendons that appear from the thread, until there are four threads; then assemble them one on top of the other in the shape of a cross, and tie the skin with a strong bond of two parts; then pull out the threads, and tie them together again with two parts, so that none of the servants who suckle you can enter into your body, lest there come worms to you; and put the bond directly according to the first bond long two doves of it, and after all, another according to the rounds that the hoof carries; then cut in the part under the skin of the bones, until without flesh or bone, as we have said before; then apply soft wool linen soaked in oil to wounds, and put it inside, and put the bond which we have said.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And sometimes we cautery the white flesh to what we have said, after the incision, by doubt of blood coagulation.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece; puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	For this happens often, and let the ligature be tied to what it sticks to; and if it lingers in the wound, so that it may come loose; then rise up from the cold water, and apply the same thing as we have said, until it comes loose. Then treat the wound with another remedy, until it is perfectly healed.
de hernie carnouse	of a flesh hernia
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this matter I have never seen anyone who dared to make the cure with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz; puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the ancients said that it is done in this way: as if you tie a ring to the nose, in such a manner that you fasten the straps after the head, lightly downwards, then strike me, and treat the abscess of what hurts, until the straps come loose; and cure it as we have said, until it is healed.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit,
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When you strike the hair, if it muffles and stops the wound, until it is healed.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The syphilitic is constricted, and has no appearance in the operation, and the cautery is more muffled in this place, and closer to safety.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of softening of the skin at the joints.
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a III costures ou IIII fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Many times the skin of the joints is softened in people, because the chars inside are softened and can be seen, and it's a matter, when one wants to treat it, one must make the patient lie on his back, and strike the soft skin on top of the natural skin; then join the two lips with sutures, and see if you want, cut through the stitches, and the cure as in other wounds, until he is healed, and the flesh falls off.
dou chastrement	Let the cautery of fire command the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	Know that cautery is forbidden in our law, and it pleases me to not speak of it in this book; and it needs only two ways: one way is that the barber should answer questions when asked, and know the cure; and the other way, because we have often needed cauterization for some animals to help us, such as oxen and sheep and goats and other animals.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	I say then that cautery is done in two ways: either by attraction, or by cutting.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	In the way that we make by attraction, we sit the best in warm water, until the flesh is softened and done with it; then prick them with your hand, until they are removed and you no longer feel them.
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Du chastrement de taille: it is necessary that you tie the bestiary, and press the skin of the chest against your left hand, then suspend the above, and strike on each one to a certain number, when you have well scorched them; and leave any small spot of flesh uncovered, and subtle flesh that is under the vasa; and this manner of chastrement is more gentle than that which is done by attraction, because at the attraction some thing may stay among the fingers, because the bestiary desires luxury. Then cure the wound until it is healed.
des hermofrodites	Of hermaphrodites.
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	A hermaphrodite is in two manners of houses: one is that between the two sexes are open like the figure of nature of a woman, or he has hair, and at no time does he have any urethra.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And thus another manner is in women, and has on the finger like a spike and also two points.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	And the cures for fever and famine are that you copy the joined limbs all, and cure as other wounds; in the second manner, for men whose urine springs from the skin of the finger points, there is no cure.
de la tentigene	of the pustule
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	A pustule is a joined limb on the natural part, so long as it is ugly to see; and some women have it even larger than one hand, and this is the cure.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	It is necessary to dye the superfluity of the pustule with your hand or on some part, and cut it lightly; and do not go too deep, lest blood comes forth from it, then the cure is in other cures until it is sane; and for another wound that has been in the mouth, the cheek, and perhaps has sprouted, which resembles a cow, and thus they call them "cow disease", the ancients.
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	It is necessary to copy it, as we have said about the test, and the treatment until she is healed.
de erratique	of errors
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	There is error when the nature of the woman is not perceived, or the part is lost; and it is due to her birth, or an accident by illness that occurred during delivery; or if it's because of a fall, or a sharp stab, or something done deeply in the vagina, abdomen, or elsewhere, and it prevents conceiving, and childbirth, and sometimes the flowers (i.e. the menstrual period) come; and knowledge of this is acquired through observing pain in the belly.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If there are signs of hemorrhage near the exit, choose either your right or left side.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	If it is thin and splits into two halves close to the two fingers, which are near the two-lever marks, then hurry up and do this: place your two fingers together, and have the woman lie on her back, spreading her legs; then straighten the two-levers until they are firm, so that the thin cuts split, and the ointment sticks well to it; then take flax, oil, and the mucus in it, and put it on the limb, and let the woman stay at home every day, so that she cannot rejoin.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the cut is hard and thick, it is better to sew it with a small instrument resembling a leaf of myrtle.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the ointment is of black iron, put on a poultice and sew it; and apply the medicines stained with blood, as we have said before, equal parts of vinegar, dragon's blood, incense, and oil; then bring in a large cloth soaked in wine, so that the wound cannot close; and thus be done for a long time, and put on a linen sheet to cover it; then cure with other remedies until it is safe.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when the arrow is found on the body, so it must be covered according to this manner; if it's not a poison in the arrow.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For when there is poison in the arrow that is in the body, one should not touch fire.
des emorroides	of hemorrhoids.
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	Hemorrhoids are openings of veins that do not usually occur, and when they become old, they swell; and we have said in the division the signs and appearances, and I will tell you which ones respond to a cure.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I said that hemorrhoids and the swelling occur when they are inflamed in the body, and if you don’t notice by feeling them, it's only with iron treatment.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those who are at the mouth of the mare, can be felt, those can be cured.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	It is therefore necessary that you put the woman in a cold house, then test her at the altar with nails, and cut them at their roots, then powder on medicines restraining blood, if it soothes and stops the bleeding, like dragon’s balm and incense, and similar things; then pour water into her feet for an hour, then put her in cold water; and when she stops bleeding, take her out of the stew and make her sit on a decoction of sumac and pomegranate rinds and gall, and with flour and honey, and let it set on her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if it stops bleeding, that is good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	If it is so, if they make hot air vents on the back and harm the nipples; then take linen, and apply the pus in the juice of plantain or in the juice of angelica with wine vinegar, and let it dry on the patient.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the abscess is covered up, so that it seems to have healed just like I said; and if the "albathir" appears, which is red, and resembles a rough head, then they must cover it just as I've told you; and then let them cure until it heals.
des apostemes de la marris	of abscesses from the marrow.
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many kinds of abscesses come from the marrow, such as carbuncles and pustular abscesses and herpetic lesions and fistulas and hemorrhoids and hot abscesses, and many other diseases that I mentioned in the divisions.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	It is therefore necessary that I say in this treatment the abscess that comes into the marrow, which is not an abscess that only forms bowels; and if you wish to see its origin by iron cautery, then examine if the abscesses are present at the beginning of its arrival, and filled with heat and fever, and if it becomes red then you can see it.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	Therefore do not pierce immediately, but let the pain be eased for as long as possible; and then place the patient on a stool, with two petis sieges or so that he can recline, and support his back and assemble his feet towards the lower leg; and make his knees spread out, and put his arms under his shoulders, and tie them well with a good bandage; then take the ball from over the right side, and insert it into the mouth of the marrow, because this comes after; and it is necessary that when you see insert this instrument, that you poke it in first to know the depth of the marrow, so that what enters the instrument does not go more deeply than it should, and does not harm the patient; and if the instrument is larger, it is necessary to cover the depth of the marrow with cloths, so that the instrument does not trouble the patient; and it is necessary to put the horn of the instrument on top, and bend the instrument.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	Instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is covered with gauze, it is advisable to avoid applying iron cauterization, but treat it as we have said in division.
de l’enfantement	of birth
