de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess of the elephant
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	A boil occurs on the elephant's skin near its hoof or foot, or sometimes it appears in other places; and when it is small and no attention is taken to it, it will develop into a boil, swelling and ulcerating until it bursts as long as one runs along its root. Sometimes they burst entirely; and soon there are corrosions just at the bone, causing strong pain, and are the swellings of both feet wide, and have a red color.

Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	The fire cautery is a great aid when the bones are sound, and the joint is healthy; and if the joint presses the cartilage, and begins to puncture, and bleed, it is wise that you put the bone below the joint so as not to point the cartilage, and push it up high, and strike that cartilage subtly and gently, and apply the rest of the medicine on burning and corrosive matters to remove all; then treat the pain of ointments until he is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	And if the corrosion is in the bone, if you strike it and pull out, for as long as the bone is corrupted, it cannot heal; and if you see the corruption spread, if you strike at the root as previously said, then treat him until he heals; and if he has iron and bleeding, and he feels great pain, it is wise to first heal him; then strike the joint with a small knife well made in cutting across above, and be careful that the cut does not come too close to the cartilage under the joint, because the patient will feel too much pain.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	The pain comes from a sour throat of the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois. Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The soundings that come when the two joints are assembled come from birth or by sudden injury of a wound or by burning with fire or by similar things.

des vils	of old men
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	These are large venous swellings filled with melancholic humors that come to more of the members of the body; and it is more common in those who go on foot and work and carry heavy loads than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	It is therefore necessary that you administer no cleansing of gall, and then the healing of the basilic.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer. Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	The cutting is done in this manner: first the doctor raises the leg to a hot water, very strong, so that the fat is not subtle; then he strains the leg of the sick from above the chest to below the knee; then he cuts the vein in one, two, or three places, with a wide cut, then cleanses and treats the black wound with his hand from head to toe, so much as the virtues of the patient can bear; and then ties it and commands that it be dressed with meat in order to prevent the gall; and repeats the evacuation and healing when the veins are full, and hurts the sick man.

de la voinne civile	of the civilian's flesh
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	This vein is located in the thighs, in warm areas where there are no herbs or trees, and on dry land where there is no moisture; and by chance it may appear elsewhere than in the thighs, and this happens because of putrefaction that comes from below the skin, as it moves into the body through the skin and then between the skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of the beginning of this vein cutting indicate that there is a great inflammation in the leg, then the swelling comes and changes, and then the vein begins to force its way out, like the root of a plant.

des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	of worms that are born between the skin and the flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This disease is called "bovine illness" in our land because it has often affected cattle, and it is a small worm that is born between the skin and flesh, and goes up and down the entire body, causing pain from one member to another, until it bursts through the skin or leaves, and runs out; and is filled with pus of some humors, like serpents, lice, and insects, as well as worms in the stomach; and people doubt its malice, because when it goes throughout the body, it climbs up to the head, and enters the eye, by chance, it returns, and destroys the eye; and this has happened many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you treat the cure and tend to it, if there is no fever that will appear, then it is necessary that you tie the limb above and below with a strong cord tightly, then strike up and treat it, and if the vein breaks out in front of the arm, and you do not find it, then cauterize with fire on top, until it dies; and the greater evils that it does are that it runs oil, as we have said; and if you see it coming towards the head near the oil, then bind below it the seal form, then strike up, and treat it; and it is necessary to use the patient of purgative medicine body, with soluble medicines for bad humors poured, and if he warms of rotten putrefaction.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	of pain that comes from windy conditions
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This disease is called in our land "vakirir", and it causes pain that arises in some members, and it moves from member to member; and I have seen this, which I tell you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was summoned to a sick woman, and she revealed to me that there was an inflamed vein on one of her arms; and after a while, I saw it move as a worm at the shoulder, faster than anything, like quick silver when the knife cuts through the flesh. The pain departed from that place, and settled in the shoulder, and then it ran across the whole body, until she came to the other arm; then she told me that it had turned again around the body, just as I saw her.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was amazed greatly at how it moved from member to member, for I had never seen this disease in that manner.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	Toutevoie, I have seen many that have suffered from great pain of their own movement but I do not want to, as I saw in the woman; and I thought it was because of this that women had a hard body and uncovered breasts, and because of this they appear constrained; and those who are delicate, and have moist bodies and exposed veins, do not seem according to this reason.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And when I see treating this disease, and the patient feels that great pain, if it opens like we said, then let them hold it so quickly, and then strike above so that the constrained breathing stops in the body; and cauterize the body; and if you do not see that with your eyes, then the cure for those who bind the veins, such as fetid pills, serpent pills, and similar others.
des saiettes	due to arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	The arrows are various, according to their appearance and according to the type of body or where they pierce.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	There are different types of arrows, depending on their shapes and according to the parts of the body where they pierce. There are those with large points, small ones, and spiky ones, and those with sharp edges, and those with tongues, and those that cut into pieces; and some cut in two different ways: either in a principal member such as the brain, liver, stomach, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When an arrow therefore pierces a non-essential part of any of these members, and the signs of death appear to you as I will tell you later, then it is necessary that you remove the extraction of this arrow, because death comes after in various dispositions; and when this evil sign does not appear to you, and the arrow does not pierce to its full length, take it out and cure the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, and when the blood comes out and hits the bone, and the syphilitic fever which is above the brain, is when there are symptoms such as scotomia and seizures and delirium and redness in the eyes, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and convulsions and difficulty with understanding, and vomiting of bile; and by chance it may occur without any pain in the nose or ears; and by chance it may be near the throat and voice; and it appears as if there is a white pus coming out from the wound like ants, and jumping around like the sound of burning charcoal; and if this sign appears to you, then take heed of the cure, and pull out the arrow (if it’s not already) when it's not present.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The sign of the arrow when it bleeds or pours blood, is that it is near the left breast, and it feels as if it were stuck in something hard, not empty; and by chance the bleeding stops like ants, and comes with cold sweat and cold fever, and fainting: perceive this at once, for you are sure of death.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	The sign of the arrow is that it comes out without any bloody foam from the wound, and the throat becomes swollen, and the patient changes color, gasping deeply and sighing with a bitter pain.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	But if the arrow falls into the cover of the breast, so it is near the little ribs; and it comes out with a great pain and a great swelling, and the patient gasps deeply and all the limbs move except the shoulder.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	But if the arrow goes into the stomach, by chance it comes out from the wound with nothing of undigested flesh.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	But if the arrow goes into the belly and does not go through the intestines with a piece of cloth, then there is no hope for recovery or extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrow flies into the bladder, and the urine falls out in a sudden manner and comes forth from there, and the patient feels great pain: see that the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other limbs are safe according to the various conditions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or artery, and it is not venomous, as I will tell you because of what has happened to me, so that you may do the same.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	It happened to me at a house where an arrow had struck the skull or temple near the root of the nose: I tried it, and pulled from another side under the fatty tissue of the ear, and it was healed suddenly.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	Instruct the patient to tie an arrow in the fat of oil under the paper under, and the arrow is tied back, and you should not touch anything except the tip towards your fist, and it's a great Turkish bow arrow, with all iron going lightly near ears; the game was safe, and no bad accidents happened.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And tie an arrow to the neck of a Christian, and it was a Turkish bow arrow under the ears: I tied the beards, and made it so subtle that I tied it, and the Christian was safe.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And tie an arrow to a man who was pierced or stabbed in the chest, and I thought he was dying; but after thirty days passed, without any change in his condition; I cut up the arrow, and pushed it out, and nothing bad happened.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	If you see a man with an arrow shot into his shoulder or back, and the wound is closed over; and the arrow remains inside him, and he does not change his natural disposition, nor finds any discomfort in any of his works naturally.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And see another man with an arrow shot into his face, and the wound is closed over; and he suffers thus for a long time great pain; and many other similar things.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And there was an arrow shot into the man of the princes, the king's man, who had been wounded in the neck, and was beginning to decline on the right side; and the wound was completely healed three days after.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	If I found the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I sought with great subtlety for it, and did not find it; and he felt a point and pain beneath his left ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought it was the point of an arrow I placed upon his left side, belly and digestive system, because the lungs were inflating; and they appeared as if there were arrows in the chest.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I placed the poultice on his hands every day, and solved the wound directly; and he remained thus for a long time, until he felt the arrow inside his nose; and he told me.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I placed on the wound medicine with corrosive properties by hands daily, until it was broken open, and I tried it; and he felt the head of the arrow getting dry in his lungs; then I opened up the wound further with that medicine, so that the arrow appeared visibly; and after four months, the wound was closed again, and I tied it tightly from one side and the other; and he could not come out; therefore I did not stop to be subtle and ingenious with instruments, until I took them one day, perfectly made, according to what the form of this chapter would bring at its end, until I tried it, and restored the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And they judge that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored: I will restore it then, and the wound was healed, and the patient was completely cured.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	Or I will tell you the quality of extracting arrows, so that you take your cure on what I do not say, for the books cannot understand everything; but the wise masters comprehend very little, and only on what they are present and failing, find new ways, and new instruments, to deal with the strange things that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that arrows do not issue from the limbs where they are fixed except in two manners: either through the joint or through another part; and when it happens that an arrow enters through a joint, now it does so for the first time.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	Instruct the patient to let it lie still until the flesh is putrid and decomposed, and let out its issue; and similarly if it is fixed in the bone and cannot come out, let it remain so for some days, and move it every day; and then it will come out, and if it does not come out, pierce into it through and through until the bone is enlarged and then take it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	If an arrow is fixed in the bone of the skull and is stuck just above one of the ventricles of the brain, and all the accidents that I have mentioned to the patient: if you do not treat it, but let it lie still for some time, because if the arrow comes out through this spot, it will be death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	If the arrow is fixed in only one bone and does not come out through that spot, but the patient remains still for some time without having another accident, then it will take effect to be cut.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if she is much cut off in this way and cannot come out properly, I administer more tartar inside, as I have told you; then treat the animal till it is healthy.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the arrow is put back in the animal's body, so that it cannot be seen, and it has taken up residence completely; and if you feel for it, if it sticks to something useful; and if you cannot see it because of the tightness of the wound and the depth of the arrow, and there are no bone or nerve visible; then carefully feel as long as the wound is large, and if you can feel it, take out the arrow as much as possible, and if it has ears in the arrow shaft, where they are stuck, break off or fold the ears of the arrow shaft, so that you can pull it out; and be careful not to break the arrow, so that you can pull it out more firmly.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	If you cannot do it once, if the pain is within the limbs until they are torn apart, then take them away, because the extraction hurts greatly.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	And if you take a vein out in vain, then follow what we have said about the cure of this chapter; and beware of the incision on the nerve and the vein, and put into practice how you should treat the arrow wound, whether quickly or slowly, firmly or gently; and put the patient according to the shape he was in when the arrow pierced him, because that is the greatest aid there can be, and if you cannot do it, then put him according to what the signs show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	If the arrow comes from the other side, or if there is something opened in it, or if the skin is swollen to the point where you see or feel it, then take a larger size, until the tongs can grasp it, and then extract it; if now it happens.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is retained in the bone, so turn your hand round completely, until it enters the bone, and expands the bone, then take it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if it cannot come out, so leave it alone for now, and then start extracting again until it does emerge; and if the arrow is stuck in it, pour a full dose of the medicine; and if it has fallen to the ground, and you see administering a poultice, do administer an instrument of horsehair, so that the point of the arrow enters into the hair of the instrument; and then pour out, and if the arrow is embedded, pour the instrument with pointed end inside, for to alleviate the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow is embedded, it is to your advantage that you copy the entire arrowhead or where the poison is, so that you can, if possible, then treat the wound as needed.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	Instruct the patient to cover the wound when it is discharged or bleeding outward, onto the skin or in the belly or bladder or at the chest. And if it is close to the vein and you can do so without causing more harm, then cover the vein and the nerve, and then extract the wound; and if necessary, cut the bandage, as this will be; and cure until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the tongs used to remove arrows are similar to the beak of a bird, and look like this:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And they come in many sizes: great, middle, and small, according to the amount of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the hook that grasps hair is like the feathers of a bird, to grasp at the tip of the arrow, as it looks like this:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the shape of the pincers for pushing and for catching is here:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of veins on the body common
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	Of veins that bring health are XXXI, because there is one head XVI, which is namely: two branches behind the ears, called the "soft herb", and two arteries in each temple appearing; and two veins in two ear canals, called "spurs"; and a vein at the forehead; and a vein on the brow of the head; and two veins that are around the neck; and two veins above the lips, which are called "jugulars"; and two veins below the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	There are five veins commonly in each arm: one is the cephalic vein, and is located on the left side of the chest, and they call it "vein of the head"; and the second is called "fast", and is composed of the cephalic and basilic veins; and they call it "vein of the heart"; and the basilic vein is on the right side of the chest, and they call it "vein of the belly", and is located above the spleen; and it is that vein which heals, which opens up clearly in the pouch.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	The saved vessel is the vein between the auricular and anular bones, and there are two veins. And in the leg and foot there are three veins: one below the curve of the pocket on the left side of the left costal margin, and the second which is located at the ankle bone on the right side; and the vein called "nese", that is located in the other ankle bone; and in the other leg there are three veins below those ones.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	The vein after the ears that is used to treat old catharsis and migraines, if applied correctly as I said, and it is that you raise the head of the patient, and rub the skin where the veins are rough; then tie the patient's neck with a string so that both veins appear behind the ears in two places below: if these do not work, then go to another spot, and when you feel the pulse beneath your navel, make an incision; take the lancet, and pass it through under the vein until just before the bone; then lift your hand up the entire vein, cut and the skin and the vein well two must be traversed, and bring out the blood until you see; then tie and bind, so that she is cured; and I have said incision and cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	The sick of the two arteries that are in the two temples, so value to emigrainne ancient and slow, and obtalmie accustomed, and at the eyes of the watered, and the qualities of the healer are as I say: And it is that the patient straining his neck, until the two veins appear openly; and feels the palsy under the toe, and then takes out the lancet; then lifts up the vein in the high place to the foot index, and buts it down, and lifts up the vein, and cuts, as you have done in two other veins, and do bleed according to your need; then release the patient, and put on the foot above the vein for an hour, then put on cotton; and then forms and leaves him until he is cured.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	The sickness of the vein in the front is worth as much as the sickness of the head, and of the ancient diseases, emigraine, and roujor; and those who have such qualities are so that they strain their neck by twisting, until the vein appears; then take the instrument called "fosseur", whose form is:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	And put the point above the vein, and thrust upwards of your hand, or with another thing, and let the wound open as far as you see; then deliver to the patient the neck, and tie the vein so that it is healed and never again will bleed with a flame wide.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	It is not advisable to let the wounds be too open; and the healing from across, because the bone is near, and by chance breaks the wound when it is subtle.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	The patient with two veins in the arms that are near the elbows should hold the hands and fingers, and the wrist, and the redness, and the swelling, and the orifice of the vein, and the diseases of the face; and those who have their illness like this, will strain their neck by twisting from any bond, as before; then the treatment, and let the treatment pass through, a little deep into the bone, a little long, a little wide, for there is no harm.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the swelling is subtle, by chance it may break; then make a quill of blood, as much as you need, and then tie up the wound, and tie it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	The swelling of the vein in the neck is valued at ague, and at a strong fever, and at diseases of the face, which cause emigration and redness that comes on the face, and painfully when it is old; and those who have this illness are bound with a knot, then strangle their neck by your left hand, and take a long, thin quill, and strike it into the flesh between the two nostrils, because the vein does not open well in that place, and now the bleeding will begin to flow; and do not go too far, and make the treatment of blood according to your need, then tie it up for one night, because she is very quickly restored; and this is the form of the quill.
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	The sainie of the two glands aids in the tightening of the vein, and at the beginning of incision, and with a great number of diseases, and gangrene, and corrosion, and herpes, and it is said that the quality of the sainie is such that the patient strains his neck away from one side and the other, as we have said; and if the masters are standing above the chief of the sick person, and the sick person sees in one siege, then cut open the vein long enough to make a small incision, and apply temperately until as much is done as is necessary; then redo another opening in the other vein, then release the ligature, and tie tightly around the veins moderately, so that the patient does not strangle; and leave him thus till morning, when the wound will be healed.
de la sainie des leivres	Of the wound of the liver
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	For the wound of the mouth of the liver above is aided by applying coal in the mouth, and corrosion of gums, and splits in lips, and does not heal.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	And the quality of the wound is to have the patient sit in front of you, and hold his neck so as I said; then turn the liver, and look at both veins, where one is on the right lower lip and the other on the left, and they can be recognized by their color, for they have black veins that are smaller: hit either one or both, and if you do not recognize them, and you are in doubt, hit the largest of each part, just as with the others above and below, because it is the same manner.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	Of the injury of the throat below the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	The injury of the women which are below the tongue should be treated after the head injury, and it is due to constricting the throat, and because of diseases of the eye, and of the mouth; and those who know how to treat such injuries are those who place their hands between your fingers in front of the sun, and they lift the tongue, and look into each direction one vein black: then heal both of them and do not go too deep for under them are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	The veins of the shoulder which are commonly treated are treated in two ways: either by pricking at a large mitten-shaped mark, or an olive tree-shaped one, as you count them, and they are called 'anesil'; and they are wide and subtle according to the width and tightness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The fiery form of mercury is very famous and is as wide as you see.
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And has the need to open the vein cheek plains of large blood visible, which contain large blood and trouble; and it is the form of fiery olive.
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	And is more subtle pointed, and is for healing small veins, or it has subtle citron blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	The basilic vein, which is one of these veins, greatly helps in diseases that are beneath the throat, and near the neck, and near the liver, and the stomach; and it suits the physician that he heals with basilic, and that he warms himself from the artery that is beneath.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And if he cuts the artery and blood flows out, then it is fitting to stitch, as I have said; and let not be painful the fiery form, but make it like honey.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And if the basilic does not open immediately, it is advisable to remove it and change another one; or if you want any rain from it, or if you heal in its place on the arm: it opens immediately; and strike at the flame again, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And if you see the vein of the wound, it is also advisable to remove the arm, that you touch the vein until you know the pulse; then mark the point of the incision, and then bind the arm, and strike again at the vein with a flame; and be careful not to cut into the artery when you see the vein swollen, for that's from the artery: skip it then.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it bulging up just like the urine of a child, and there is no redness or subtlety, know that it's not from an artery: hurry then, and put on your do (likely referring to a tourniquet), for many times have; tie off your arm, and let it be in that way, and don't move the patient's limb; and beware of fear, and don't move them until they are healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the blood is not stopped and he vomits, and you have no medicine for him, then cut the artery when it opens, because the head of the bone recoils; and stop the bleeding.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	Take a piece of sinew and cut it, and take one half and tie it tightly onto the other half; if the blood does not stop flowing, that is good; if not, then as we have said, apply the powder that stops bleeding; for applying the ointment on the limb in such cases is not suitable for those with a small wound, because of the swelling.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	The sainie of the vein is often assisted in applying treatment to the head above, and to the body below, because it is composed of basilic and cephalic, as we have said; and it is fitting for the master that he should cut into the nerve that is below, and if he cuts too deeply, and the nerve becomes inflamed, and the patient suffers greatly, and by chance cannot be cured; and this nerve opens many times, and if it does not open in any person because of its subtlety, it is fitting to clean out the sainie with the instrument before using it; and pull out the nerve as much as possible.
Et se il a voinne entre les II ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if they have veins between the two fingers, then make a cut on long.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	The head of the patient is helped by drawing blood from the head, and assisting the eyes; and it is advisable to bleed at the flame of olive or at the flame of myrtle, because this is the safest of all veins, for it has no nerve or artery.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	In any case, it is advisable to seek out the lighter vein for treatment, and not worry about anything if you need to do it the first time, and then start again; but by chance the veins may become swollen at some people on the first attempt, but they won't be harmed.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the blood is according to your opinion.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	Instruct the patient to know that healing is not done for healing alone, but rather to preserve health and avoid future illnesses; and let the healing be done in one of the three veins: cephalic, radial, or basilic; and if it is done at the beginning of prayers after fasting, in autumn and winter after eating, when the signs of repletion appear; and do not perform the healing on the first day or third day, but rather two days or three days afterward.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	The healing that is done for illnesses has no fixed time determined, but rather when necessary, in any hour or at any time; and it is not advisable to heal children under 14 years old, nor pregnant women only during the first four months of pregnancy.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez LX ans.	They must not remain sick those who have passed 60 years.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	And when some wish to be cured, in what manner whatever it may be, it is wise that he makes the intestines of a light castor oil bag, if there is much bile retained, so that veins do not press upon intestines and cause superfluous protrusions to the principal members; for he will not recover those who are too salty with meat, or those who are ill with fever, whether it be from an excess of blood, or dropsy; and if he purges himself after colic, vomiting, and venter's decline, and multiplies his habits with wife, labor, watching, and marriage, and does all that can be done by the arm or body; then subtly he treats the humors, not too heavy by food and drink and medicine, as much as is possible; then he enters a bath, if none of these things fail, to treat the wound, and recover from the vein at the third time, just as we have said; and beware that day of work, and pain, and luxury, and similar things; be bound and rejoiced, and may you heal higher than those who are sickly, and rub the arms twice or thrice, then loosen the tie above moderately, for when it is too tight or loose, he cannot correct himself without; then rub the hands as they become swollen and painful; then apply a poultice of salt from an old rags doused in oil, then put on his bandage with his left hand under that vein until he wishes to be cured, lest veins fail him.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	For there are veins that flow like cords in the body, and some that are filled with windiness, so that when one places the flame on them, they retract to flame, and cannot open the vein, and thus is done to those; and if they cut the vein, it is because the wound is too tight, therefore it is advisable for the doctors to be aware of these things.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein opens for the first time, it is good; but if not, then again attempt to open it near that place or very urgently, so the veins are not inflamed.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And if the veins are inflamed and the patient hopes for it to pass, let them wait a day or two, and do not tie up the arm: by chance an abscess may come on; or they should not enter the bath, then reattempt the treatment as it pleases; and if the wound is small, or if they are cautious and you doubt that it will not be so bad as you see, fear not in the same place with all its heat directly; cut a little hastily, so that the veins may be inflamed; for this happens often when the injury is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If you see the swollen limb, do not resume the surgery again, and put a little bit of lard oil on it, for it alleviates the body from pain, and is moistened by the lard; and thus administer the lard oil to each wound that you heal, to quench the course of the pain; and similarly make a tracheotomy and a bowel when putting the lard on the limb; so subtlety does not harm and it saves when it is too big.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if it happens that there is a large abscess, which occurs often, at the same time when there is no surgery done except to open the vein, then hurry and put a moist sponge on the limb with a little vinegar and salt; tie it up for an hour; and it is fitting that you do this after the issue of the wound from the vein, and if it stays on the limb after some days without any blackness or greenish color, it will not harm; and if you see, put some aloes or mirror juice mixed with vinegar or calamine juice on it.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And many times occurs an abscess and appearance at the swelling of the basilica: put then your hand on it, and if you find the lump soft under pressure with your hand, that is a bad sign.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore do not put anything on it that we have said, for by chance cutting without an artery; but make the wound dry first to harden the lump, then apply another treatment until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And treat each person according to the quantity of their virtue, and by the color of the wound.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if it is black, let it be allowed to come out until it becomes red; and if you see it gross, let it be allowed to become subtle; and if it is too thick, let it be cooled.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And it is fitting for one who is weak and feeble, and needs the extraction of blood, to make a larger wound, and let the festerings be wide; and for one who is weak, do the opposite, and it will bring him healing quickly and often, and he should be healed by cutting across, not piercing; and this manner of healing is safe from the corruption of blood and the coping of nerves, and is better than healing with a long needle or a broad one.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And for one whose blood needs to be drawn during the healing, it is fitting to give him milky pain in grape juice; if he is heated, cut into the blood three or four times; and if he has a cold temperament, put in front of the wound milky pain sweetened with mead, or with aromatic syrup made with spices such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and cloves, a very fragrant one.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	If the hand has a wound, after a lot of blood has been drawn, it is fitting that he drink broth of char, and sweet smelling syrup, and use other things that we have said in the division or chapter on fainting, for the evacuation of blood.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wants to swell one arm and heal again, it is fitting that when he is weakened by great wounds, he heals little by little, according to the quantity of his continued virtue.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine VII houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And who wants to swell one arm after the first wound and has strong blood, will be healed in 7 hours after the first wound, or after the next hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And who wants to be healed of another part, if it is necessary that he should be healed the second day or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, and fait venir fievre;
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swollen, so let it be left and not tightened, until the abscess is healed.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if you need to treat the wound again, whether in the same vein or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein is moved to the arm because of its composition.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the manner of the vein if is such that the patient puts his hand in hot water, until the pulse is red; then it is bound slightly, so that the vein appears well; then the wound is now treated through it, not too wide or too narrow; and if there are large scars, they are sutured well near the joint of the hand, and if without any issue, then put the hand back in hot water, and let the wound heal in the water, until you have enough; and if this is so, do not put the hand again in hot water, because it is more useful in winter than in this state; and the healing of this vein is more safe than all other veins, with no artery or nerve.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	The sick of the savelet of the right hand is worth all the diseases of the belly, and this is the way: strain the hand, and pour in hot water, until the wound is empty, if it can be seen; and if it's twisted and you cut it through entirely, so that nothing grieves; and do not go too deep by the finger, for the nerves are very dry at first of all, and then put the hand back in hot water, if it has not frozen in the wound, and will not come out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have treated the wound as necessary, put oil and sinew on the vein to close it immediately, and do so for every cut.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The wound in the left hand is worth to the disease of the mouse, and do it as I told you for the right.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The ailment of the spleen is worth more than all other diseases that are within the body, such as disease of the marrow, and retention of flesh, and illness of the joints, and of the knees and legs old, and similar illnesses.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	And if the quality of his spleen is such that the sick person puts in some stone into a hot bath, and rubs over the vein until it dies, and ties above the joint of the foot; and the vein is on the ankle, and from above the foot goes out much pain; heal the donkey then whether it is more painful to break the bone, or on the ankle, that is worth.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you heal it above the foot, be wary of the warts that are below, and heal across as well as when cutting, so that the flesh may close.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if he cannot come out (of the wound) without it, then put his foot in the water, and let well-ventilate the vein.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	And if the suture is needed for the first time, then reapply it on top by a little less, because the glue is salty; do not doubt about the nerve, as we have said, and so apply equal sutures to the other foot.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The glue of the sciatic vein is located at the heel bone, and its stitches value for the pain in the hamstring, when it's caused by bleeding.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And if the stitches of its suture are such that the patient is between bathing, and extracting above the heel, four fingers in twisting, because otherwise the vein will not open; and if it opens, then suture it in all possible ways that you can, and across; and value your time, for the glue is lost, and it is much returned to hands.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	If you do not find it, then the person will have rain or blood on their head and feet, and towards the little toe, and beware of the bowels; and make as much care with the wound as you can see, and then release the tendon, and put on cotton and binding; now they are healed.
des sainies de ventouse	of wounded by suction
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Ventouses are made of horns, or thorns, or nails; and suction is done in two manners: either by hurting and attracting the wound, or by hurting.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And this suction when it is done by hurting and extraction of the wound is done in thirteen places on the body; for some are all in the head, others around the neck, and two around each shoulder; and one under the chin; and one under each elbow; and one above the ribs; and there are ventouses in both arms; and in both legs; and in both knees; and it is not applied to the wound, except for small veins scattered throughout the flesh, as when making a venous dressing; and it should not be done with heat or cold, in any disease that comes from overeating, until all the body is empty.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	Instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and myself when it is at its worst, we command the physician to let us swallow after three hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	The disease of the liver is helped by the application to the heat of the head… that comes to the eyes, and it should not be done after the evacuation of all the body; and this ventosation is in place of the disease of the cephalic, and it should not be used by those who have a hot temperament, or who have catarrh, because this hurts them much; and therefore it should not be used by those with head cold diseases.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who recover from it often become blind, and therefore they should put the ventoscope a little further down by the doubt of blindness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	The ventosation of the neck is in place of the opening of the chest and the basilic vein, and for this reason she values herself tight at the breast, and a cutting of the channel of the stomach, and with a thrust, and a filling; and it is necessary to poke little, because if she holds too tightly, so there ensues an obliqueness or a vomiting out of the stomach or the heart.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	The ventosations are in both costels of the neck if it causes pains of the head, oculars and emigraines, and strangling, and pain at the roots of the teeth, and are in place of the basilic vein; and it is necessary that you command the lord that he express his hand to put, that he does not cut the artery, and does not wait until there is a discharge.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	The windings below the chin is a sickness of the mouth, and corruption of the gums, and similar illnesses that are in the mouth; and it is near the sinuses of the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The windings on the shoulders are worth a sickness that comes from heat and congestion.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	The windings on the buttocks are worth as much as three veins in the arm, because it attracts blood from these large veins; instruct the lord that he should not strike too deeply with his instrument, for the skin is thin and sensitive to cold and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.
