The winding that is above the buttocks is worth emoroids from the fundament, and diseases of it, and it is necessary that the wound be large and made of linen, to treat well, otherwise if it were subtle, it would break, and cause great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The medical ventouses of the legs heal openly because they attract blood from the whole body, and are worth as old pains from the rain, and from the maris, and from the bladder, and they bring forth flowers; and they are in place of two sophenes, and two knees, and they all weaken the body after a long time, and bring forth pustules on more frequent occasions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The way of putting the ventouse is that you put it in first empty, and succeed perfectly, and then place it hastily, and move evenly, and do not cease to do this, until you see the skin red and swollen, and draw out the redness from the blood; then, again, remove the ventouses, and take care of the disposition of the body, because there are those who have contracted such a char, and clear pores: it is necessary to cut once only, and it is fitting to make large wounds, and deep ones as well; and suck lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if it is not large, he must strike it twice: once to make a small cut through the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if it is very thick, he must strike it three times: and when we try to cut through the small blood vessels little by little, only one time suffices.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if we want a lot of blood, we repeat the process often: and if it is thick, he must pierce through it deeply; and when we finish cutting, so that the veins are perceived suddenly, cut at one who has hard skin and is rough to the touch, with whom you apply the oil of apertif dissolving on the swellings of the fingers: if this is the case, use vinegar oil, or oil of almonds soft, or oil of cucumber seeds; and if it is wine, then use oil of cresson, linden, camomile, or any similar kind.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the swelling is great and cold, take olive oil, amberwort oil, or balsamite oil, and anoint it.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	But if to those who are being made healthy the wounds have small and fine pores, do not put oil on them, but instead wash with water of rosewater, or cold water, or mulberry water, or cucumber water, or pearlescent water, or another similar kind.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those who have much moisture, lift them up with hot air, or water of myrtle, and sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And those who have great swelling lift them up with old wine, or water of rue, or annetroot decoction, or other similar things; and should not be healed by suction before the bath, nor after the bath for one hour or two hours; but do not sleep afterwards, for it is necessary to ventouse when it must be ventosed, and when it is swollen.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	Instruct those who are healthy to be cautious of being choleric, and if they are not too hot and inflamed, then it is advisable for them to take cold things, such as pomaceous fruits like grapes and endives and lettuce, and similar things; and eat small portions, and wear a belt of leather, and moist meat.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And those who have a cold complexion should take honey syrup and fragrant wine that is between youth and adulthood, eating little, eating small portions of chicken, pheasants, and pigeons; and on the day he will be convalescent, he must drink more than eat; and it is advisable to give some men some vinegar or mustard at one time before convalescence, or after, to comfort the principal members; but be subtle in this without, for it is not wise for those who are hot to drink.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles qui sont mises sur le foie et sur la mice, et podagre, et sur le ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nous metons ventouses sur le ventre et sur la boude pour amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sur le foie et sur la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides pour sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensemble feu, et aucunes fois plaines d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude sole, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the cauterizing with fire given is this:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	And has two fingers of width and half palm from the root, and has a groove to one side of the middle finger a small puncture, like to insert a needle, and be made of iron or wood, soft in front so that it does not prick the patient while placing on the member; and have at the middle a crossbar of iron or wood, to hold a bandage, and they are large and small as per the diseases and age of those who take them; for the cauterizing of children is different from that of adults, and thin ones than fat ones.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And thus place this cauterizing instrument on the member: take a linen or wax strip and put it in the middle of the cauterizing instrument, through the crossbar that is in the cauterizing instrument, so that the clarity is at the bottom of the cauterizing instrument and does not burn the patient; and then place it on the member, and make sure the two fingers which we have said are above the puncture, so that when you take it out, if vapor comes out, do put back the cauterizing instrument; and take up the linen as before, and reapply often, if needed.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	In the winded one who is ministered to with the disease of pleurisy, has no pain and does not have a fever or an inflammation, and is taken care of only when it is full of pain, and is placed on the limb alone; and this is the form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	Veins are taken care of only in limbs where it cannot be put a catheter due to smallness, like lips and gums, and similar things; and in their nostrils of char, like two or four, and other such; and the qualities of use if is that when you find veins that are in clear, cool water without injury, take them; and put one nettle in clear water, until they become familiar with it, and have nothing in their stomachs; and then let be cleaned of vein and catheter, and then rub the member so that it is red, and put on the veins; and when they are full, and swell, if it can be put a catheter, put one, because this is very good after.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If the wounds of this chapter have often caused evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in treating wounds, and extracting arrows, and cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	If the wounds do not wish to be taken, then rub the limb with fresh blood, or prick it with a needle until the wound opens, and then place them on it, and immediately when they feel the blood, they will stop; and whenever you see that they start bleeding again, sprinkle powder on a little salt burned, or powdered silk, or ashes, so they will stop now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	This begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	These chapters are often necessary in the art of medicine, and are for the restoration of fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	You must know, dear son, that the methods of cautery are found in this chapter, which one never saw in the ancient books, nor learned from letters; and because of this, the science has been lost in our land, for I have not found anything good; and I know nothing, except through the knowledge of the ancient books, by studying which I have treated the science, and through experience, and by the custom of my life; and I have written out here what is contained in these chapters, abridged at the end, and shown clearly the forms of the instruments to be used, just as I did in those two previous chapters.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is therefore necessary that we say in this prologue of this book the number of words and chapters which the wise men place their understanding upon, and dwell on the truth, so that those who have been experienced learn and acquire this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	When any break or dislocation or twisting or constriction occurs in the body, it is necessary that you hasten to heal the sick person from one part and from the other, if no hindrance comes to you, such as weakness of body, or sickness, or old age; or if the limbs are too weak, or too cold; and when a chill is present, which is what I mean by frosty joints, and charmed with poultry and wildfowl meat, and do not drink wine, nor eat fatty foods, nor stuff yourself too much with viands that fill the veins of blood, until you have no doubt about an abscess or swelling in the member; then return the patients to their previous government when they used it.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bones begin to restore themselves, it is fitting that one nourishes the patient with foods that produce great swelling, or where there is viscosity, such as wheat cooked in water, and risottos, and tests, and pease, and pancake, and oysters, and fresh fish, and large wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For nourishment that produces swelling, it is more pronounced and occurs sooner in the breaking of the bone.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And know that old and decrepit bones cannot be well re-covered or soldered according to their nature because of the dryness of the limbs, neither can those which are too tender, like the bones of small children; but there is no cure: to the large bones that have been healed and joined together with the limb so that it becomes strong as it was before; and not all of its strength comes from work, and for this reason they should be nourished with great foods, just as we said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And finds that fractures are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fractures of the head are different from those of the arm or leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all kinds of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there are fractures that happen around the joint, and others that occur from cutting, just like the length of a single hair for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if with a fracture there is an open wound, and if a fracture has a small split or fissure.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And each kind has its own instrument and proper tool for restoration, according to what is remembered in its place; and it is known that the fracture of the bone occurs because of the joint being twisted, and opening well by itself, or by pressure on the finger; and if there is no tortuosity or swelling near the joint, and the patient feels little pain, unless there is a fracture; but they can still have tortuosity, fissure, or small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	If it is not fitting to move your hand now, but put up medicines that are coming after this, and then hold it now subtly.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And knows that the fracture which is in the arm, and are two parts joined, it should now be put into equal points, so that the abscess comes to an end; and if the abscess forms, let him leave one day, until the abscess is calmed; then place it into a joint as lightly as you can feel it, and knows that the restoration of this part is lighter than the restorations of those who have pieces.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if in the bone there are broken pieces, so that it is in two parts, then it should be done as follows: if it is in hand or foot, do it according to its natural form; if it is in both hands, or one foot and one hand, put the member accordingly; and when the parts of the limb that are broken are diminished, make replacements according to the size that you can, and take care that through your work there will not come a new lesion or pain to the patient; and do well the two joints of the bones according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And he feels well in the hand if it seems to you that it is not quite right: if the dressing is done beautifully, and not too tightly strained, nor pressed as those do who try to bring about with their work an intense contraction and tightening of the member, as we have wanted many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And when the limb is set at a point, instruct the patient to keep it still and not move, neither in waking nor sleeping, nor turning, nor by any other means; and be sure that the limb is so firmly fixed that he feels no pain whatsoever.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	For when he feels no pain, it is not at a point, and you must set him in the same position so that he feels no pain; and be sure to keep him straight, lest twisted movements come upon him when restored; and let the quality of the broken limb be as I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Things that break a limb are different in small, big, and shape.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	For small members, such as arms and hands: it is fitting to wrap up a bandage of soft, smooth linen; and for big members, like thigh and leg: one should wrap with a wide, hard rope, because the wide ropes encircle the entire limb, and tighten all parts equally, so that there is no gap; then tie lightly around the handles, three turns or four according to the limb, and bind with your hand tightly to the whole rope, then go above the break and tighten less, until the break goes away slightly; and soften the rope a little by little, as much as you can feel a healthy part of it, then take up another rope, and turn back over the break; then return to the lower part of the break, and tighten moderately, not too tight nor too loose, as we have said in the first line above; then put linen or cloths between the ropes, until they are all equal, then tie everything from top to bottom with a bandage, and then place your pins well made on it, if there is an abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	If it has an abscess or an aposteme, put a soothing paste on the abscess, and if you remove the swelling, let it stay for some days; then strain on your joints, using a moister of one-inch width, or a splint made from wood, or palm fronds, in this shape:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	but it is necessary that the splint put on the break be a little larger and wider than the others; and should be as long as it needs for either small or great limbs; then strain on the joints just like you did at first, then tie over with a thread, in the same way as before, so tight as possible, but not too much, lest it hurts; and the thread must be of a good quality, neither too thin nor too thick, made from flax that is not twisted or distorted, for if the thread is too thick, like I have seen with certain foolish people who make their casts with corded linen rope, it's a great error, because the cast can never be even if it's too fine, and it's better to leave some space between each joint.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	If the patient is sick from the chiseled stars after the binding in their healthy, then they put some linen cloths or a woolen bandage on them so that they will not bleed.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When a wound is with a fracture and the knees are broken, I will tell you the cure as follows.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And since it is not necessary to strain the stars on all broken members on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	For when the members are great, it is not necessary to put stars on them every day, unless after 5 or 7 days, or more, according to your safety and the treatment of the abscess that will be made; and thus I tell you how the ancient embalmers used to restore fractures, dislocations, and torsions: and it is that you take flour which stays on the walls of the mill, mix it with a great deal of egg, and make this confection, not too clear nor too thick, and use it, and this is the common way of restoring fractures in many conditions, and especially for women and small children, because it's neither too hot nor too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana V З.; alechil VIIII З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another method of plastering restores the break and dislocation and twisting: take onyx and lapis lazuli and amber and asafetida and gum arabic and myrrh, ana X; mirror and aloes, ana V; alechil VIIII. And make a powder, and mix with honey and vinegar; if the complexion of the bone is hot, use this plaster, because it is of good composition, and restores the broken bones quickly, and saves many lives.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another method of plastering that is good for twisting: take myrrh and visnaga, ana X; mirror and aloes, ana VIIII; vinegar and ACaice VI. Boil well, and confine with water or honey, and administer.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Another way to treat the joint and its bone, you must bring and clean them together, and soothe the following pain; and use the broken bone, and mend it: take a new linen, and clean it with fat and oil cooked, and put on its place.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	These plaster dressings do not restore, but they are good for soothing hot abscesses and proper cleaning of pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another way to treat plaster that restores broken bones: take dry leaves of fig and earthy leaves, and grind them together, and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another way to treat plaster for the restoration of broken bone and for relieving the following from the abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Instruct the patient to take roots of valerian, camomile, violet flowers, wheat flour from each, and pound them; and mix with wine, and put it on the limbs when heated, or mix with moist coriander water or vinegar, and use.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another method of applying plaster is stronger than the first, when an abscess has developed on the restoration of a limb.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take roots of valerian and seeds of flax, balsam, melilot, and sansucca, and flowers of violets and camomile, in equal parts; pound, and mix with salt water or sweet water, or with wine, according to the heat of the limb and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Iporcas writes in his book that you should not put on the broken limb for restoration with just cerote made of wax and oil, and nothing else, and that it should be between too wet or too dry.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems that one must place the broken limb above, to restore, moistening dry things with a little hot, as we have said and shown, and other similar things.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another way to treat wounds and pain: take the flesh of a dog, or bones of an ox, or quails' beaks, and equal them out, and crush, and make it into a poultice and apply to the wound.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then the limb is left for a little time afterward, and take care that the patient does not feel any pain, nor has moved his bones; if he does not leave it by hand, or if the pain comes to the bone, or prurites, with rest or swells, if you hasten, remove it, and remove the poultice now; and take a light bandage, and a sponge of moist sea water, and plunge into the water, and lift up the limb until the prurite ceases, and the pain is appeased; then let him rest for an hour, then put on a dry linen cloth, moistened in water or olive oil, and tie it above a nut, until you are sure of an abscess forming.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	If you see that an abscessed foot and red flesh pain and swelling are full of bone all around, and you have to plug and tie them, if it comes back again, as you did first time.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	If it does not come to the limb any of what we have said, then do not release it for more than 3 days or 4 or 5 or 7; and never let it go longer than 20 days, according to what one sees, until the fracture heals and approaches the joint near the bone; therefore restrain it more tightly than before, and feed its flesh well, as I have said before; and if you see the limb drying out more than necessary, know that serious consequences cannot come of it; then give the limb hot water treatment every time you release it, and do this one pound, and a little later; by this work therefore cut off seriously what is coming to the limb, and hasten what the foolish healer does, which will leave the limb twisted: this is bad, and it is an urgent concern, and I see nothing else but that of binding and overstretching it correctly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	of various kinds of breakage
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	There are many kinds of breakages and diverse forms, and the causes are determined; for there are breaks that are caused by the impact of a sword, and the collarbone is crushed all along with the bone just beneath it, as if hit or struck; and therefore this kind of breakage is called "haichure".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	Where the sword hits the bone on top of it and pierces through, and this kind of breakage is called "absolute"; and there are two kinds of wounds resulting from these two types of breaks: large or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if it has pierced embedding, or tearing, or fracture of the collarbone, or striking on the bone with a stone, or other similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is an ongoing fracture, which approaches just in front of the membrane that is under the bone, or above the bone, and this wound is great or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if the wound is covered with a thin layer like our hair, and the fracture is small, and because of that it is called this fracture "capillary"; and if the wound is made by striking with stone, or falling, or some other thing, and the bone piece falls into the joint space, and the joints are so swollen as when the cauterist heats up his tools over the pots; then the bone enters within.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And this happens to those who have moist bones in their head, like an infant's skull; and it has all sorts of fractures with small pieces broken off as if by stones; and I will speak about them.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we know all kinds of fractures by pulling them apart, and examining them, and by the corrupting flesh that is upon them.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The hair-like appearance is known because when we discover the bone, and we rub it above, if the fracture opens up.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of a fracture, take care for accidental evils in the patient, and if you see no evil accident, such as vomiting of bile, loss of understanding, stretching, paleness, fever ague, and eyes that fall out and turn red, and other similar signs, then he cannot heal without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see an extraordinary accident and you expect a cure, as you begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the winter comes to you, and it is time, if possible remove the bone in front of the eighteenth day at night that you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if this is the case, so be it that you hasten to remove the bone in front of the seventh day, otherwise the tissue under the bone will become corrupted, and accidents that we have mentioned will come.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if the break of the bone comes just to the covering of the brain, so be it that you cut off the broken part thus: and hold the patient's head firmly, and uncover the bone in all the ways you can, and on the face of the wound as well as you can, and when bleeding occurs from uncovering the bone, or abscesses, use what is necessary, and fill the wound with moist rags soaked in rose oil; and let the wound rest until the abscesses are quieted, and be certain that bleeding has stopped; then begin to remove the bone, and this is done according to two methods of work: one way is that you make a narrow cut at the breakage beforehand, and it is like this:
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then they cut into another part of the body more deeply than the first one.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second method is that you have various cuts, some are three deep and others wider, with points and ones made of iron; and work lightly so as not to hit the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is hard and thick, it is wise that you pierce it through, so as to administer cuts with chisels, not by boring but so that the point does not go beyond the bone of the cheek, and must have on one side a margin or a circle, so that the point does not pass beyond the bone; and you should have more than one, so that each comes in its own place from the edge of the bone, so that you have chisels for all your tests; and this is the form of the three kinds of chisels:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The qualities for piercing through the bone that is broken are such that you put more time on the bone, and turn to your two sides until you know that the bone is pierced; then set the tarry there again after a little while, and do thus all around, and later, cope the spaces of the incisions in the space between the parts, and do this more subtly than you can, and lightly, as we have said, until you take out the bone with your hand, or any of the instruments that you have, such as pliers, pincers; and be careful not to touch the brain or the soft flesh.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you have pierced the bone and cut it, if some part remains that has stayed in the bone at all other instruments resembling an incisor, but it is necessary to be more tenuous and subtle than the others; and if there are no remnants of small bones or scales, then gently remove them with one of the instruments; and then cure the wound with tenets and oignments as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other way of working is what the Greeks say, which is more so; and it is spoken with great force, and this is his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first that you uncover a part of the bone, where or at which the break opens up, so that when you have uncovered that part, you put down the head of this incision lenticular, because it is the form:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	And do not cut with one stroke, and it is the part that is troubled in two sides, so that the cutting is towards the bone; then, after striking with a small mallet above, so that you lightly copy the bone all around, and be well guarded from the cloth that is under; if it is rough against the bone, strike lightly at the bone, because one strikes the bone with little pain, but with much fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	If the head of the shoulder is broken so that it just fits inside the cloth and the bone is hit only from above and there are small pieces, then it should cover back over that roughness and remove the scales with a subtle raspener which you have many of, in order to meet each person's most convenient measure according to their work and figure.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you have more coarse raspers and after that more subtle ones, and do not cease to use them until it is well done.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other delicate procedures and subtle fractures, it is fitting that you meet each according to its direction; and this is something that no one has responded to, for he who has studied in this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	If the abscess is uncovered, it is fitting that you apply gauze according to its quantity, and soak it in rose oil, and put it on the wound; then take another gauze doubled twice or thrice, and soak it in wine and rose oil, and put it over the first one; and do this as lightly as possible so that you do not burden the abscess, but rather let it heal gradually; and leave it uncovered for one day or two, until the swellings are subsided, then remove it, and administer medicines such as lion's root, mustard powder, incense powder, and aromatics, and similar things; and make a paste, and put it on the wound, and administer the aforesaid medicines with mastication; and beware that the wound is fully healed, so that you do not leave any dressing or assemble any bowels, for when bows are assembled over the cloth of the brain, they will be infected and burst, and bring great harm to the patient, because when something sharp is put on top of the abscess, it causes inflammation under it.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take care now then no accidents happen to the patient, as we have said, since it is doubtful in every case.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if no burn occurs except for the medicine we have placed on it, because of its virtue, then you should take a part of honey, and three parts of rose oil, and in glue make a dressing, and put it on the wound; then treat with remedies as needed until he is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that no two times are the bones of the neck broken in two, or one by itself alone, because they are two bones; and this lower one is cartilaginous, and breaks not, unless it is bent or twisted, and then heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And if one of the two bones is broken, then you should put your little dough or paste on the broken part, and place it inside the broken bone with your thumb index, and in the pouch near as much as possible, until the bone regains its natural shape; do this gently, and beware that the patient does not feel pain from your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is in the upper part of the neck, and it cannot come back to its place, you must put an equal thing on the head of a straight stick a small one.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	And if the break is in two parts, do it again and hasten to restore the first day if you can; but if not, after the seventh or twentieth day, when the swellings are smoothed out, then bind on a cloth of linen around the neck if the break is in one place.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or if you put the other part on, if it is; and the bindings are so thick that they fill in the holes of the neck.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And said any healer that we must moisten the bindings in butter and move each one day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	It does not seem good to me, but it is likely that they are moist in the preparation of a mixture of wheat and oil, and powdered milled flour; then let the tent be stretched out until the bones harden, and the cartilages become hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And sometimes no cloth or linen of goose is used in place of the tent, and if it has a suffocating covering inside, and holds the injury, and blows on the patient between them; then first see what you wish.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	And if the abscesses come to a boil while you are working on it, then apply a poultice or cotton soaked in oil rose, or in half a pint of vinegar.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the abscesses do not come, then apply a plaster according to need, of flour of sesame and powdered incense, mixed with wheat oil; then place on lightweight stitches; and do not tie the linen; and if the break is small, and it breaks into very little pieces, then extract with suitable instruments as much as possible, then sew the opening, and the treatment for those with open wounds, and applying ointments, so as to be fit for them; and if it has no wound inside the linen, then cure with tent cloth, and apply plaster to a depth, until he is healed.
de la routure de la mandibule	Of the cutting of the jawbone
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jawbone is cut under, and there is no wound to cover it, and only a fracture without any breakage in two, unless there are splinters inside, if one finds it lightly.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	It is necessary, if the fracture is in the right side, that you put your two fingers into the mouth of the patient; and if it's on the left jaw, put your two fingers on the right hand, and put the fracture gently inside, and close it with what is available.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the jawbone is displaced outward from the middle, it is necessary that you extend two parts until they are even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if the movements of the teeth have come, or a fracture, then the straining with a thread of gold or silver or silk, put the broken mandible on the cheek, and put under the double flap; and put under the flap an excellent needle well made, or a piece of leather even, long and wide according to the mandible, and tie it above what you can do, and instruct the patient to rest, and serve light viands.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	And if you see that the figure has changed, so you set it free for the third day, and then put back in its place what is changing; and apply to it, from a powder made of ground mullet or flour of sasset, after you have removed the ointment; and apply over the ointment a linen cloth, if the ointment is applied, and the disposition of the patient does not change, let it remain until he is healed; often people are healed in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if an abscess comes to the foot, then follow what we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is both break and wound together, replace no part of the bone that has been extracted; for such subtlety of the extract is most suitable to those.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, then widen it as necessary according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have extracted all those pieces and there is not one remaining, apply the ointment to the wound if it is large, and put on some suitable plaster according to what we said so that it may promote healing until it becomes sound.
de la forcele	of the swelling
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The swelling often breaks several times over the shoulder, and the fracture is in three ways: either it is broken and deviated twice, with fragments, and is then lighter to restore; or there are fractures with wounds.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	Instruct the patient so that when the break is near the wound, you have two ministers, one who holds the arm to feel the fractured bone's force and the other extends the neck towards the part; then put even the break on your hands so that its form is as it should be, without any appearance or lump.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	If you need to stretch further, put a round spear of cloth or linen over the patient's shoulder, so that it is as big as your need requires; then straighten the bone and restrain the spear with your hand, so that you put even the break in its place.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	If you cannot treat the head of the fracture outside because it comes in from within, and is suitable that the patient lies supine on his back, put a medium pillow under the shoulder, and have the ministers pour oil down the shoulder, until the bones of the fractured part are lifted.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	And then direct the fracture to your two bones, and if you truly find the pieces broken, it is advisable to break them further; and take out the lighter pieces, and if the bone cannot be joined together for any amount of time, cut into one of the joints that you have; but put in this instrument with care, to avoid swelling.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	And it resembles a spoon, and is not hair, and is as large as you need, according to the size of the bone and the shape of the work; and has two handles, just like you see, and one should be wide, and the other narrow, just as is the nature of the wound that you made when you cut the bones; and when you are sure about the swelling, sew the wound, and if the swelling is small, or you doubt it's too much, then fill the wound with cloths and bandages according to its size.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if an abscess forms at the joint it comes to, then apply moistened linen in rose oil and ash and wine, and put it on.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	The straining of the bone, when it is sensitive to pain and swelling, is that you put up the bone with the plaster of powder from the mill and black pepper, and place light strips on top, and if necessary, insert a spear below; then take a very large bandage of a palm’s width, and apply double strips above the plaster; then take a subtle needle of three fingers’ width and one length, and wrap it around that bandage so that the head of the bandage is hanging; and place the needle on the fracture, and turn the bandage up over the shoulder, and from under the shoulder to the sick part, and straighten each piece, and when you see that the ligament holds the break immediately, and you clearly see that the needle does not move above the broken bone, if you reapply every day, and when the ligaments are loose, if so; then make the patient lie on his back, and place a small pillow under the shoulder, to lift the apparatus up high; this will relieve the fracture by the stretching of the shoulder, or when you tie his arm to his neck, and do not untie it in case of bad accident, for twenty days; then reapply the plaster, if you see that it needs it, and tighten and leave it thus, until he is restored; and he is restored within twenty-eight days, and in less than many men.
de la brisure de l’espaule	From the break of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	When the shoulder breaks or is broken in two, do not apply force to it unless by touch; if the limb appears according to the figure of the break, and is molded according to its natural shape, in all ways that you can; then put powdered flour from the mill with much wool, and light stitches, and put under the limb a double drapery; then place a large and subtle needle, one piece larger than the shoulder, and take out the thread at any point of the shoulder, so that the thread of linen is stretched equally; and then tighten it firmly to all a great band, so that the joint does not move from its place, and observe each thread daily; and every time you apply force, loosen the thread, and put on the limb as soon as possible, and lie the patient on his cost side, for the shoulder is restored in XX days or in XXV, And when this number is completed, he will be cured, for it is not a matter of bone that must be set lightly.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of the bone bursts outward, and the point below the curvature, so they make above, and the bone, and do as we have said in breaking the abscess of the hot pus.
de la brisure dou pis	of the broken foot
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	The piece is not broken in the middle, but this happens rarely; but it breaks often when exposed.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in the middle, so that it declines downward, and the patient feels great pain, and loss of appetite, and nausea, and sometimes vomiting blood, and by chance opens the wound into the broken bone, and the pain becomes more intense.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is thus: when the patient lies on his back, and you place a cloth between the shoulders, then press the shoulders, and assemble the two ribs to your hands, and do so subtly in all ways that you can, until the figure of the bone is as it should be; then apply plaster and bandages above the subtle part of salt, or some other light substance, and wrap them around the broken bone tightly, so that it does not move; and turn the bandage round to the back, and bind immediately, and reward him every hour for a little while, unless he becomes loose; and if you want to release him, because of corrosion or itching that comes to him, or pain or abscess, then hasten, and release him, and scrape off the plaster, and address what has come upon him in the treatment; then remove the plaster, and bind him until he is healed.
de la brisure des costes	Of the breaking of the ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	It is clear that the breaking of the ribs comes only to those who have a large belly after their back, and to the head inside, and they collapse only because they are hollow; and it is felt well at the inquiry in the bowels.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the treatments are that you put the break in equal measure, as it seems fit.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And then apply an emplaster, and tie with a stake if you have need.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the breaking of the ribs is bending towards the inside, it causes the patient great pain and puncturing, like pleurisy, because the bone pokes through the membrane; it's also painful to cough, and burns, and vomit with much bleeding, and it's a source of bad health, and the old ones have used many remedies.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if there are those who say that it should be administered foods that swell the belly to push the fracture away from the surface.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not make this, unless there is pus in the wound.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it has come, then let it heal.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And none of them say that you should put poultices on the limb, to suck out the pus, and it seems like a good idea; but there is doubt whether poultices attract the superfluities to the limb because of its weakness.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And none of them say that you should cover the limb with linen moistened in hot oil, and put tents between the ribs to set it straight again, then cure it with the treatment of bleeding, flesh, and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the patient feels great pain that he cannot endure by the bone which pinches the skin, and there is doubt in the patient, then it is fitting to break up the broken side of the rib, and it is fitting to place under it some instrument to ward off the splinter; and thus one must pierce the bone, and treat lightly, and then sew the two lips of the wound, if they are large, and cure with plaster, until he is sane.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If an abscess comes in, then place moist cloth soaked in rose oil on it, and put on the vein; and treat while the vein is swollen as much as it should be, over the costal side where it must be, until he is sane.
de la brisure dou col	of the broken neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	There is no breakage of any bone of the neck, and it does not occur when he bends; and also at the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this occurs without breakage, and you see if it will be healing or not, if you warn yourself that if you see your hands are softened, swollen, and dead, and cannot move nor stretch, and when you prick them with a needle, if they do not feel.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Know that it is mortal in more positions, and if they are mute and feel well when you tighten them and prick, know that the joint of the bone is saved, and the patient will be cured if you put a treatment on them.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	And if such a thing occurs at the spine of the back, and you see whether it will be healing or not, take care that if the feet are softened, and if there is an accident in the hands, and when they jump towards the belly, they jump with violence and excretion against their will; and when one has seen this on his belly, they jump with excretion against their will.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when he sits on his back and he wants to sit down again, so cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	Those who think it is fatal if they do not work on his cure.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if such an accident does not happen, then it is the lighter thing.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the cure is that you reward him if he has a hot abscess, so apply oil of rose or oil from milk or beeswax, until it is appeased; then put on a comfortable and dry plaster, and bind with a bandage, and command the patient to rest; and do not sleep on that part where he feels pain, until he is healed.
