Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if some bone is exposed, it is fitting to cover the wound; and take out the bone, then assemble the two lips of the wound, if they are great, with a seam, then the cure with bandaging and sewing, until he is healed; and if the head of the bone is broken, which is called "chiés de la kowe", pour some of your left hand's pouch into your right hand, and put it equal on the other side to your power, then put the plaster and needle above, if you have need; then tie, and if there is an exposed bone, make up, take out the bone, and cure the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	Of the fracture of the shin bone
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	It happens that the shin bone is fractured, and if so, even a little swelling at the head; let it be set long, and sloped to the bends, and it comes to the patient pain in the limb, and point, and swells as it breaks.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is that you extend your hand above, until you are over the fracture; and see which way it is fractured and what shape it is; and if the fracture is only at the head alone, then set equal that fracture, until it has the natural shape.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the fracture is long, or it declines inside, then have the patient lie on his stomach, until the restoration of that fracture becomes apparent.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	When you have made it even, then put on the plaster, and put on an iron or leather stake, and bind the break, so that it does not move; and apply to the joint below the breast, until it is even.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And instruct the patient to lie on his sound side or on his back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if an abscess comes on the foot, do not touch it until it is laid down, and put on what we have previously said; and then return to the restoration, and bind as it needs to be bound, unless there is any other foul accident; and this is the manner.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the shoulder joint.
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The joint of the shoulder is that which is between the elbow and the head of the shoulder, and if it is broken, then one must restore it according to one of two manners: for one manner is that you take a flat piece of cloth or leather, according to this shape:
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And bind with the two fingers and the two joints, and put them up high, and sit the patient on one side; then place the sick person under one side of the arm, so that the broken bone comes to an anvil, and a wedge of wood is placed in between, then take up any heavy thing upon which the servants extend the limb; then put the mires in the briseure equal to his hands together, until the briseure returns as it should be.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a II ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout I liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And another way is that you should put the patient under his hateryle, and bind the hand to his neck; then command two servants that one of them tightens what is above the briseure with his hands, and the other of them tightens below with all his joints, and stretch each one to his part.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that the extraction is more strong, then bind below the joint of the briseure and above the briseure, and stretch each one of the servants to his part.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the fracture is close to the shoulder joint, so that you place a straight band below the collarbone, and the other over the cost, below the fracture; and thus, if the fracture is on the cost, it is advisable to put a lighter band, as labor, until the fracture is even with both joints, and with the cost; then set the fracture, so as it seems fitting, and tie it up, so that abscesses do not come.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if abscesses come, do not restrain them until after seven days; put a moist cloth in the wound and olive oil rose, until the abscesses are calmed down; then tie it up, and the manner of tying it is that you place plaster on the fracture, then assemble the arm to the shoulder, and put your hand on the shoulder or breast; put a bandage, and restrain on the shoulder and arm, so that the arm is in its proper place, unless any thing prevents it, or if the bone is not moved.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	If you doubt that the bone does not move, then use esterels, and place a larger and stronger needle on the break one more large and strong than the others, and put two spaces between each needle, and each needle so big that it passes through the break three times from each side; then pull up the needles, as I have said at the beginning of this chapter about the break.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	If you see the positioning of the needles and the straining, as we have said, when you restore the injured member, and you doubt the abscess that is left, if it remains closed for five days, as we have said; then look at each three days of the closing ligature, whether it itches or swells, or any inflammation comes to the member because it is too tight.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If they do as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	And if no such accidents occur, after three or more days, let the patient lie on his back and hold his hands over his stomach; and place under the aid pillow one hundred pounds of even linen, and observe each hour of the day or night, whether the broken figure of the limb does not move or become softened; for the medicine to work, and give the patient the meat that we have previously placed before him, in such a manner that the meat be tender first; and when he comes to eat again, if it is thick.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	And it is customary that the shoulder and leg should be reset after forty days from the beginning; and therefore, one must dislocate and administer baths and medicines for the limb to become well.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if the stricture is crooked and blocked, so it stays stuck for three or four days.
de la brisure du bras	of a broken arm
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is made up of two bones, which are called the "fossicle", because one is small and is where the pouch is located; and the other is large, and that one is under the smaller bone; by chance, only the larger fossicle breaks or both, the small, and sometimes they break together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	When the small fossicles are broken, the treatment is light and healing; but when the large ones are broken, it leads to worse healing, and more severe damage than when both break together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If only the small fossicle is broken, it is recommended to stretch a little and put them even.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	In case the great frost is, then they must pull more strongly; and stretch above the cussin, and lift the pouch of his hand higher than others, and the fingers should be lower than others, and so that the patient crosses himself on it, and cuss above him higher, so that the patient does not suffer any pain; then extend the minister's arm to the part below to his hand, or to the tendon, and one other minister to the other above.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then put him in the mirror, according to his best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the break has pieces, then put each one in its place, and if there is no suitable form that can be held, and you cannot restore it to its place, then pull out the bone, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	If he has with the break a wound, I have spoken to the singular doctor about it; so take care.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	And if in the beginning of the restoration some swellings remain, apply a plaster made of linen dipped in rose oil and white beeswax, not too hard nor too soft; tie it on the swollen part gently, until they are appeased.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	And then apply the rose oil, and put on a plaster made of powder from the mill with much water, until it is placed, and the splints are set, so that the splint of the break is straighter and a little wider than the others; and observe that there should be six or more splints in these dispositions: whether the break is in one of the bones, or two; and tighten above the break more than elsewhere, and always less when you move it, as I have said at the beginning of this chapter; and so be the draperies on the break soft and moist, not hard nor harsh; and let the fillets, from which it is strained, be made of linen, neither too big nor too small, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And repair the limb and the joint after some days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	And if some foul accident happens to the limb, just like a prick that comes on the limb, it is fitting that you raise the limb in hot water, until the pricking subsides; and let the limb not be too tightly bound.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And then reapply the binding, and if the ligaments are loosened and the bones deviated, and it seems so, apply further pressure.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses I poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if the swelling does not subside in the limb because it is too tight, it is fitting that you loosen it a little, and let it be for some days, until the swelling subsides, and then bind it.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things come to the patient, which we have stated, for twenty days.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	and if you do this treatment for him, then tie his hands to his neck, and so that his necks are even, and warn him of movement and of numbness, and let him sleep on his back; and observe that this fracture is restored in thirty days or in forty-five days, and by chance in twenty days, according to the nature and constitution of the humors.
de la brisure de la main	of a broken hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	observes that at the back of the hand there are few fractures, and instead only sprains many times.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	and when the finger of the hand is broken or sprained, it is advisable that the patient tie a cross around him, and sit up straight in front of him equally; then put his hand over an extended elbow, and stretch out the broken bones, and make them even with the mallets, until they are well jointed; and apply plaster and bandages, unless there is an abscess coming on, then it applies a stake according to the quantity of the bone; and wrap him up in one half-cape of linen.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	In case of a break near the tendons inside the leg by the ankle bone, make a splint from cloth, and instruct the patient to tie it to his broken leg; then tie it with a long thread, so that the size is as great as the plantar bone of the foot, and the tying, as it suits.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	If the break is in the forefoot, it suits that you put a splint above and another below the leg, so that the fingers are straightened and aligned; then tie everything around the hand, and anchor the rope between the two.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	If the break comes to any of us on either foot, and it's swollen, tie it straight, as you like; and anchor it with the leg; and if you see that you should put a small straight splint to lift the fracture, and do not move; and if the break is in another toe, tie the ligament near the other healthy toe which is next; or tie them all together, so long as possible, or place a splint on top, as the swelled one; and beware of injury and proper placement of the abscess cut, and heal those who come to you, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	The bone of the fist breaks.
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	The bone of the fist is broken many times and one can see it when they turn their hand forward and backward; and the treatment is to tie both above and below the break.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And patients put their face on the ground, then each one stretches out these ministers equally; and this is when the break is covered with the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the break is close to the root of the fist, there are either one of the ligaments over the elbow and the others below the break.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And also if it's close to the joint, and then either there are ligaments over the elbow or below the break; then put the mirels (likely a type of splint) the bone equal to its two hands, so that it is according to its natural figure, and then apply plaster, and ligature, so that the abscesses do not come.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	If it has an abscess, so let it be treated first, then return to its work and cure; the release is made in that manner.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	It is necessary that you wrap the sprain in a bandage of two or three times, and keep the swelling there, then turn the leg until the toes reach the root of the nail, and put one long thread between the thigh and the knee, tie loose under, and fasten the chief with the thread above; then turn up the leg and above the knee the bandage, then set the splint on the bone of the knee; then apply eight threads in a gentle fold to tighten the ligature, then start tying again forming three or four turns above the sprain; and the more you go up towards the sprain, the less the ligature is tightened; then wait as two threads of the thread that you have put between the thigh and the knee, and tie three strips above, then return below to the chief with the thread, until you see from under the foot; and tighten it if it does not move from its place, then let it be so, then if no abscess or inflammation or other signs appear.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	If there is, if he dislocates, and addresses what comes to him, as we have said many times; and if it has pieces of bone that hold, then they should be kept, since one can; and if one cannot, then they should break the limb, and draw out the nails; and the cure should be done as we have said, until he is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And never is the chest broken in such a way that we have inserted needles, whether in the shoulder or in the arm; whatever method of treatment has been done will not fail to relieve the patient.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en L jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And it is said that the chest is restored within three days, or slightly less or more, according to the diversity of the constitutions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the groin road
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	She who is pregnant will have a small break, but it happens many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	But if it breaks, it's only a small crack or cut, and she will have much pain, and feel very ill.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is to put equal weights on both sides so they are assembled and joined, until they can be moved again; then apply the plaster, and put a round nail in it if you need to, and bind them as needed, then follow all the arrangements we have said for other breaks, in a similar manner, and put each person back in their condition, just as is necessary, until they are cured.
de la brisure de la jambe	of the leg break
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	Those who have the two bones in the leg, where one is called by the name "mustelz" and the other "foscile", all have another fracture when it comes to the arm; and because of this, the restoration is done as with the arm equally, and the wound is all healed. And if the two bones are broken together, then turn the leg in all directions.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the small bones are broken, turn it forward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	And if the large bone is broken, there will be great pain and it can be seen well; then turn it below.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	And then apply an extension, and put it in its place, and tie the ties equally; but be careful, if the break is ugly and there are more pieces, you should make the extension smaller and lighter; and make it according to your skill.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Et when you have completed your work, so take two faxes of flesh that pertain to the thigh from one side and the other, and let them be long enough from the knee down to the skin; then tie them tight above and below, and in the middle also, and at this tying the leg will not be able to bend either to the right or to the left, and thus it is well; and none of these should be bound too tightly, for if they are too tight, the flesh will burst, and they should put on the thigh to keep movement, and properly done, this is done in the break where there was a wound; and move each limb every day to see if there is an abscess or another accident.
de la brisure des os dou piet	from the break of the bones of the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle there comes no break, but with the bones of the foot sometimes a break occurs and as does this fracture, and it often happens in multiple dispositions.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	If it has the bone of the foot fracture, and you see these bones rising above one another, if he places himself on the ground, like if he were walking, and then places his foot on his side, where the bones are lifted up, then presses them so that they return to their own place; then applies plaster and cloth upon, and puts over his belly of the foot a small table with two nails fixed, then tightens the bandage around it, and other things as needed.
Et quant III jors ou IIII seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three days or four will have passed, if you release the bandage, because you will find the bones even, whether they are fractured, or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	In case of some broken bones, if you restore them, as we have said about the fingers on the hand; then put a splint on each broken bone according to its length, and make it a bit wider, then place under the foot the stable table that I have told you, and the tension will happen; and if there are II or III or more bones broken, if you put one splint above each bone according to its quantity, wrapped in one of drapes of linen, and tighten the table under the foot; and while standing on the head of the table away from the belly of the foot, so that it takes well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And it is fitting that you do not forget the other things I have said about other fractures, since we have spoken of them; and cure each accident according to what is necessary.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	Of the break of the bone at the finger
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the bone of a woman is broken, if it swells, then incline it to the back side of the neck, and hold it behind; then fill the basin with wool of the patient's size, and put in as much as I mentioned before; then straighten the woman's back, a little bit at a time, and so she will feel the cotton, until it comes into the opening of nature, and the bone returns to its place; and when she urinates, if the cotton is still inside, and when she has finished urinating, pull it out, and do this for 7 days before: then the break will be healed, and if you see it, take a container of wool and tie a rope around the wound, and pour the entire container into the nature; then blow through the rope so that the vessel is filled inside: nature will return to the bone; then fill with cotton again, and leave it for some days, until it is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	When the bone of the finger or thumb is broken in a man, or in a woman, so that it is restored as we have said with the bone of the heath; and these near-breaking injuries are not concealed from those who put their study and use there, and they listen to my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	For when the break signifies a stronger disposition on the right road of restoration: therefore.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the phallus, when it is broken, take an owl's gut and put it in the phallus; then wrap strips around, and let him go for three days or until he becomes clean again, and he will be healed quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	of break with wound.
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is to be considered by him who has a break with a wound, especially if it is great, so that the bone of the shoulder or of the elbow, or like such, may be healed now, if the remedies we have said testify for him.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound is sound, if you keep the vinegar stain, and you have nothing else, then start again to restore the break in the same hour, or on that day, because no more venom comes.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if the venom comes again, then leave the restoration until a new day, until the poison is appeased, and don't touch it on the third day or on the fourth, for you will bring about a bad accident.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the bone breaks is visible near the joint uncovered, it is to your advantage that you place it at a lighter point with your fingers slightly extended.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if you do not have the tool to place it evenly with your fingers, if the device is one of iron, which has seven or eight inches in length, and the width varies according to the quantity of the wound; and for that reason it is necessary to the master to apply three or four pounds, according as he needs for each cure of breakage; and let them be tight, and a little plump, so that they do not fold up at all under compression on the limb to your right, and are placed in front, and large from the middle towards the front, thus:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	And call it "palainche", because it is necessary that the curved nails be placed on top of the skull of the bone; and apply once, until it returns, and so are even one against the other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the break is subtle and the splint cannot well grasp the bone, so that you copy the head of the bone, until the splints have hold.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot bring the bone back as we have said, then with an instrument suitable for it, such as a cutting or incising one, to your power; then take away what remains in the bone of sharpness and small scratches.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is brought back and the patient feels great pain after, see that he is not in his natural place.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, 
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	If the wound is severe or great and you doubt that no worse accidents come to pass as we said, and you find pain in the limb if it should not be bound up with stitches; but instead, use a soft cloth, wrapped tight, and tie.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And if you see after one day or two in the morning bowels on top of the wound, so that you have put above all vinegar, and apply salve healing wounds, as ointment has been made to seem.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre II fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is fitting that you remove the limb twice a day, morning and evening, until it becomes softened and healed.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is fitting that the limbs be prepared in a certain manner so that the bowels move downwards lightly.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if they transgress every day, and it cannot be mended but rent again with a bow, see how there are small pieces of bone, therefore you should seek to mend the wound with care, and remove all these small pieces that come from that injury causing pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if an abscess or some other form of corruption comes to the body, it is fitting that you cure it according to what he has said in his chapter before.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And when the bone is broken and opens up in the limb, like the shoulder or elbow, and other great bones, do not treat it yourself, because many times death comes from this, but leave it to happen as long as possible; perhaps he will die after 20 days or 30 days, then cure the wound if you can, otherwise let him.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	That which comes from rubbing against a sore
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	They come often after the health of the wound, especially when it is near the joint, and it is a sad thing to see the figure of the limb; and by chance, it cannot be restored to its natural state.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Therefore take warning: if it is fresh, then the administrator should give medicines such as aloes, incense, and mirror, and saffron, aconite, and similar others; in such manner that you do not hold any of these things or all together, but confine them with wine or with abundance of oil or with ashes; and place it on the wound in poultices, and bind well, and do not loosen it in your hands for days; and then remove it, and repeat another, until the nodules are removed; or you tie a piece of bone well made; for the properties of the bone are such that they remove all swellings from the limbs; and if the nodulation is turned into hardness like stone, and it is necessary to remove it, so that the copes over, and the redundancy becomes apparent; or you take away any razor, until it is removed, and the cure until it is healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	A limb that is weak after a siege.
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the fracture of the bone is restored and stays in place after weak limbs and subtle movements, so happens for many causes: because one is due to having been tied too tightly, and was not tied loose enough as it needed; or because there are too many ties, and cannot come to the member; or because of repeated inflammation; or because of excessive movements, either too much in its hour or at all times; or because it has little blood in its body, so is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is that you make the patient eat, and soften the body, until the wound is multiplied in him; and administer bathing, and give joy and licorice; then put poultices on the member, so that the poultice attracts great inflammation, and the swelling rises often from the infected water, until the inflammation subsides in the member; and returns to its natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	One arm twisted after the joint.
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the member is twisted after restoration, and the bones break open, and the form of the limb is ugly, all natural powers are lost: do not believe false people who say that one must break the limb anew; many foolish men have done this in our land, and these works are blamed, and they bring great harm, and by chance death; however, if the nodulations and tortures are fresh, it is advisable to let them arise from hot water or to cook herbs that are good for soothing, like violets, roots, and mallow, and similar things; apply a poultice of mallow, as daquilon well does, and take musciliaz from violets, and mix with lard or olive oil, and apply it; or take figs fat, and grind them with flour of colon, and similar medicines that ease the pain.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And sometimes the neck is stuck due to continuous rubbing and prolonged rubbing with wet hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And so you should move the limb every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the twisted part is old and hardened, like stone, and requires being cut with iron, so that it covers just to the bone, do it at the subtle incision lightly; and put on a cushion and study in the treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of dislocations.
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When a dislocation comes about, if you want to now restore it properly.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	For when it is late, if the joints swell, and by chance they are reset to their place; for this reason we do not move them until they have returned to their normal state: many times it has brought on phlegm and other pains; whenever it happens, one must cure the patient, then let them go, as long as the swelling is gone; then apply a warm member of water and oil, then gently reset the limb, and treat each member as the treatment will come in its own place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the chapters for the treatment of dislocation of the head joint, to be done in small pieces.
des mandibules	of the jaw bones
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	It has happened that the jawbones are dislocated outward, and there are two kinds of dislocations: either they are a little bit osteotic (bone hard) and soft a little; or they are entirely displaced, and hang down towards the chin, so that the patient cannot hold their saliva in their mouth, nor close their lips, nor speak without spitting out saliva with their tongue.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it returns by more frequent movements.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And if it is whole and completed, it is necessary to reset it quickly, and not hesitate; and in such a manner that the minister takes care of the head of the patient, and gives him a certain amount of warm water from one of his hands into the root of the dislocation of the mandible inside the mouth, if the dislocation is two parts; and the other two parts are avoided, to make them equal; and instruct the patient to let his mandibles soften, and move them from all parts.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And he puts the warm water equal, until it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if they return heavy, especially if it is the two mandibles together, put them on hot water and oil, until they move lightly; do not hesitate to reset them, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	And when they are returned equal, and the mouth of the patient is closed well with moistened cloths made of oil rosary and wax, then place them lightly wrapped in moist cloth; and let him sleep on his back, and his joints being between two pillows, so that he does not move either to the right or left, nor straining himself too much, but taking easily food, until the pains are gone and the mandibles are closed; and then eat what he wants lightly, and do not work too hard at opening the mouth to drink and to swallow, until his mandible is well closed and sound.
Et se les II mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two mandibles cannot be set straight in one hour and are not converted to their original place, fever and sweating come, and with chance, an attack of wind, and by chance, vomiting blood.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	And when you see this, then know that it is a sign; and many have died in seven days.
de la forcelle	of the fist
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The fist cannot be drawn out from the chest cavity along the rib and in the flesh, and it is not brought out at all, unless one feels it well.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And the restoration is such that the sick man must lie on his back, and stretch out his arms; then press the lever towards the palm of your hand, and it will come back; then put on the plaster and the bandage, and bind it; and the head that is turned to the shoulder cannot be drawn out; unless not, and if it brings forth some pus, if it comes out at all, one must first reset it as we have said; then put on the plaster and the bandage, and bind it, and command the patient to rest until he is healed; and thus itself are brought back the chiés of the spine, when they are fixed in their place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	De la dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	Injuries occur in three ways: either they dislocate at the shoulder joint below, or at the neck area of the bone, and sometimes above, which is rare; and this does not happen to the back of the shoulder or inside for the tendons; but dislocation occurs more often downwards towards the joint itself, especially for those who have little strength, because it happens suddenly; for those with enough strength, it dislocates at a point, and returns to that point.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And sometimes it happens to some men that they strike or break something, and swell the shoulder with an abscess, and think that this is a dislocation.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	It is therefore necessary that you try it, until you are certain; and then begin treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	And it is known that the dislocations occur when they are lowered towards the joint, and you will find the difference between the diseased shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find differences manifest in them; and you will find a hollow at the top of the shoulder, and below the joint, there is also a hollow at the head of the shoulder, just as if it were an ulcer; and the patient cannot bring their hand to its natural position, nor can they move from any movements; and similarly, if she has been dislocated in the upper part, so that it is not hidden, you will find it manifestly at the joint; and this manner of dislocation is not difficult to correct, when it is new, or if the child is sick.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	Instruct the patient to lift his hand up high, then put your fingers below the wrist, and lift the joint with force in the same place above; and the minister lifts the hand and extends it in the same place as before, since he has placed it underneath.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	And if it does not come as we have said the day before, in order that the patient may be bathed in hot water; and he is anointed with a mixture of mollifying and soothing substances, such as a decoction of altes and fenugrec and mellilote in water, and is anointed; then he is placed on his back, and a cloth of equal thickness, not too soft nor too hard, is put underneath the wrist, and a stick is placed under it on his back, with one mire's weight; and the chief of the shoulder is lifted carefully, and the hand of the patient is treated; and another minister takes the head of the patient, if he does not move afterwards. In this way the shoulder will return to its proper place, and if you look at it, if it returns according to this method: and it is that you make him be present one man who is larger than the patient, and stands straight towards his cost (side), and thrusts his elbow down onto the side of the patient's arm, and lifts the arm above, so that the patient hangs in the air; and another minister treats the hand of the patient below towards the belly.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the patient is too light, he will try to lift with him anything heavy, and the dislocation will return now.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	And this is done in another way: and it's on striking a long wooden beam into the ground, so that the joint moves as in an arrow, not too big nor too small; then it is placed beneath the patient, but only if he has fallen softly above him, and the joints are still standing straight with the long stick; then his hand is stretched out from another side forming, and the joint returns to its place quickly; and if it doesn't want to return for all these things we have said, do this cure: take a wooden beam of two arms' length and four hands wide, which has the head on one end so that it can enter deeply below the axle, in the shape of
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	Instruct the patient to lie on his chest covered with a cloth, so that he is not struck by blows, then place him in the same position as the patient; and stretch out both arms above the chest of the long one, and tie the assistant's hand to the chest, and the arm to the head of the hand, then place the arm on the shoulder of an upright stick of a wide size, and let the hands be stretched down, and let his body hang from another part: the joints will now be in their place.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when she is done in any manner whatsoever, it is fitting that you place below the incision a spear of wool equal, then put on the apothecary's poultice made of powder from the mill, with incense and onion oil, upon all the shoulder and back, then strain downwards from the incision immediately, and turn the ligature upon the poultice, and embrace the hand to its neck, so that the hands remain thus.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it is fitting that he should eat little, until the members are comforted, for he will heal faster; and then he should eat more after five days or seven, and move him; and if he is firm and not softened, he is cured.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is swollen from moisture or for another reason, so it is fitting to administer cauterizations three times, as he is placed in front of the cauterization chair.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all this, and after seven days he fails to stay in his place, and cannot lift any arm above, then you will know that the nerve at the top of the shoulder is stretched or crushed or softened; and you will know that the joint has never been properly fixed in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The dislocation that occurs at the elbow and knee, or behind, is done by impulse and extension of hands, and serves another joint; and care until it is healthy.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after the healing comes griping in the limb, and slow movement, then use the patient multiple times, until that griping is alleviated, and returns to its original nature.
de la dislocation dou coute	of the dislocated shoulder
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	Says that the joint of the shoulder is dislocated at points, and returns to them; and if it has been dislocated in all parts, and even before and behind, for dislocations are not always returned, because one can see it well and feel it well; and it dislocates according to each figure.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the sick person to the healthy one, if it is clearly seen.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	For the joint is swollen, and cannot bend the arm, nor can it touch its shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And it is therefore necessary to reset him so that the abscess comes out, for if the abscess were to come out, then would be a great grief in resetting; and by chance it may not be able to be reset all of it, especially when it is inside the bone; this one is worse than the others, and is accompanied by greater pain, and by chance it will come to death.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes II mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the restoration is thus, when it can be reset as such that you stretch out his hand to both of your hands; and his arms are spread out, and his fingers are bent according to the arm's joint, on and below, and draw the joint into its socket, or to the root of his palm, so that he revives in his place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	If there is a dislocation in front, then it returns when he doubles his hand to its own, and fearing the nail of the palm that has been dislocated.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	If it does not return to its original place, administer strong extension; and let two ministers extend the arm, and bind with two strips of cloth, so that it will not move when extended; then turn the arm on each side, after having bound a double cloth long and wide; and when the joint moves into its place in the hand, apply ointment of oil to soften the joint, then set the joint in order, until it returns; and when it is returned to its original place, bind securely with linen cloth, and leave some joints open on the patient's neck, and let them rest for a while, then release the arm.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is firm in its place, you should release the ligament and let it be; and if you see that the joint is not tightly bound, then reapply the plaster and the ligament, and let it be as it was for some days, until it is firmly set; then release.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	And if he feels pain after the setting of the joint, and it moves, then bathe him well and rub him, and press until he is relieved; or you put on the joint a fat mutton's wool, then leave it for one day and one night, then take out the bone, and let the wound enter the bath; and when it sweats, if you rub the joint at the right time, then put back the wool, and then enter the bath again; and do so two or three times until he is cured; and if you see that, you place a hot moist cloth of fennel with butter on him, and strain over it; for he will return to his disposition.
li dislocation de la main	The dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The joints of the hand are displaced, and the return is lighter than the other joints. Therefore, it must be brought back to its original place immediately, in the same joint where it was displaced, so that the limb does not swell or come with an abscess.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	And the remedy is that you place the diseased hand on a table, and extend the ministers of the hand, and set the mirror in an even position, so that it sets its palm upon the appearance of the joint, and applies the poultice until it returns to normal. Therefore, you must look carefully whether it is well at rest; then place the patient's back of his hand on a table with extension and return.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	And if the dislocation is in the back of the hand, then put the patient's back against his back on a table, and place your hands above that appearance of the joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	But if it returns now, that is, if the pain caused by emplastrures (bandages) is appeased and calmed down, then let him so as to resume.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	And if he cannot endure it and you cannot set the joint after some days, then the joint will remain distorted; and there is nothing that can benefit the patient except for as long as his hands are swollen, and he cannot strain anything at all: therefore know that the nerves are crushed, or the arteries; if there is no other cause except to strain with cautery of the area, and by chance it may be worth another thing.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse V jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hands are at rest, so put on the plaster that we have said, then strain it and let it be for four days, then remove it and leave as is.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it cannot be moved and there is no injury, so apply the poultice of hot water and rub it until it is healed.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	of the dislocation of the two fingers of the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	Sometimes the two fingers of the hand are dislocated to one side, sometimes on the back of the palm or the belly; then they stick, and you push the dislocation into your pouches until it comes out, then support the head of the injured finger, and point towards the place where it is disjointed; and leave it for two days, and then put it equal to that day; and tie it with a bandage, as we have said, and take off the bandage from one day, and make it move again, and bind it in the same way; and do this repeatedly until it is tight, and doing so, if it is dislocated on the belly of the hand, do as you did before, until it is healed; and doing so, when it is disjointed at another place.

Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne. And if she does not return by this cure, take a table of three arms long, and shave it off above the skin, and put the patient on his side, and pour the chief of the table under the skin, then put the middle of the table on the spine; and put your feet on the other head of the table, and press well, until it returns to its place; and if you see, do so to the turnip which turns around to the hand.
