des dislocations de la hainche	Dislocations of the knee
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc IIII parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	It is known that the joints of the knee and the shoulder only come to dislocations, not as with other joints; and the joint of the knee is swollen in four parts: inside and outside, and before and behind; and closer to these, it is swollen more before and behind.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And it is known that the swelling of dislocation inside is such that when a diseased leg is joined to a healthy one, it becomes longer, and the patient's knees are wider than those of the healthy person, and they cannot double their knee-joint by heat; and the pus that forms near the inflamed area is thick, because the blood from the femur vein comes out.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of him who has this accident, is that these signs are contrary to those that precede.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	But the signs of him who has this before, are that he has a straight leg according to completion; all goes well, do not double bend the knee in pain, and if you want to make him walk, it will not happen beforehand, and he retains his urine, and swells the groin, and when he walks, it passes over the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of him who has this behind, are that he cannot stretch his knee nor bend it, and that leg is more twisted than the other, and the groin is softened, and there are swellings on the crotch under the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The remedies for this resemblance of dislocation are that you will return if the dislocation is old and it stays according to its disposition, there being no cure; and it does not seem wise for him to have presumptuousness.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des IIII manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And in this one where the dislocation is fresh, and it's of four kinds, so hurry that you return the joint to its place, and push it inside and further back, and let it move again with your right hand and left hand; by chance if it returns, and there's no need for any other treatment.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	And if it does not return in this way, you must choose one of the ministers to come and take firm hold of the leg with two hands, or tie it above the knee; and one other minister extends his hand over him in that manner so that he pours his hands below his seat, then tightens a strong cord on the chest; and one other tightens the head with a rope; and they all extend upwards and downwards once, until the patient is lifted up from the ground once, and stays.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as IIII semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This method of extension is common to four kinds of injuries, and if the dislocation has returned, as we have said, it is correct.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	If it is not so, then it is advisable to apply treatment to its appearance When the dislocations are in the arms, it is advisable that you lift the patient on his cost side, then put a bandage at the root of the elbow, and let him lie below the angle, then tighten the bandage towards the angle, and towards the furrow; then take hold of other servants their arms, and embrace the swollen arm of the sick man, and extend it to the outside form: if it returns to its place now; and this method of dislocation is lighter than the others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	And if you cannot tie it in that manner which we have said, then it is advisable to tie both feet and one arm of the sick man together with a strong rope on both heels and both knees; and let the sick leg be extended two times more than the others; then hang him by the head of a post, and above the ground two long arms; then command one servant to embrace the head of the elbow, and have other servants stand beside the sick man, who will embrace in such form: for now the joint is returning very quickly.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	And when the dislocations are at an end, treat the patient as we have said in those who have gout, and cut the tendon on the diseased leg precisely, and on the joint just as; then put two pins, one on the head and one on the other side of the foot, then place a pin between the joints of the diseased person in the shape; and set up strips of moist cloth around it so that the patient does not bleed, then stretch each of these servants towards him, and tie the ligament to his hand with the dislocation.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it returns, that is good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If it does not return, place the patient on a stool, and press as we have said in those who have gout, and treat the patient with the healthy side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when dislocation occurs in front, it is advisable to stretch the ill limb quickly, and as I have said; and put the weight of its pain on the angle of the ill body, then press with the other hand, and extend the leg towards the groin.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And if the dislocation is in the back, it is not advisable to extend the ill limb further or lift him up on the ground, but rather to keep him as he was when he fell backward, as we have said when lying down on both hind legs; and so put his weight on his face, and stretch out his joints as we have said before, and do press on the joint at the table; and will be at point when the ill limbs are extended, and they will be even; then add the splints, and apply plaster, and the bandage of a strip, so that the hind leg does not move; and if he rests for three days or four, then lift him up, and put on the plaster again; and if you see that they are even, as before, and leave the bandage for three days; then lift him up, and make him walk well, until his limbs are comforted.
de la dislocation dou genoil	Of the shoulder joint dislocation.

de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	of wound and dislocation together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When a wound comes with the dislocation, and you want to restore it, many times the patient dies: so do not be presumptuous in the treatment, if you are not wise in the art and have not long used it, and if you are not pitiful and merciful and slow down, nor harden; and use calming treatments for the abscess at first, leave the patient in the hands of God, if you do not see any hope of recovery; and when you see hope, now set the member in place as soon as the abscess heals; and when the member is back in place, administer calming treatments again, and cure the wound, as it seems fitting, with dried bandages; and if with the dislocation there is a breakage and small bones are fractured, set them and do what we have said for simple illnesses; and beware of entering into a path of fear, according to what I have said, because this will bring you more harm than good, as it is in accordance with your Creator, and with the wisdom that has armed you and your body.
